The Four Types of Isti'arah in Hanafi Usul
Explains haqiqah/majaz distinction and four types of isti'arah applied to Qur'anic similes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of isti'arah (tashrihiyya, makniyya, takhyiliyya, tarshihiyya) and apply them to classify Qur'anic similes according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Isti'arah is metaphor based on resemblance; four types classify how vehicle and tenor relate.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary introduces the key distinction between haqiqah (literal) and majaz (figurative) language. It then breaks down isti'arah into four subtypes based on how the resemblance (tashbih) is expressed. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly interpreting Qur'anic similes and avoiding over-metaphorization.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish haqiqah from majaz
Identify whether the relationship between word and meaning is one of resemblance (tashbih) or non-resemblance. If non-resemblance, it is majaz mursal; if resemblance, it is isti'arah.
The alaqa (relationship) determines the type of majaz.
2
Define the four types of isti'arah
Memorize the four types: tashrihiyya (vehicle word for tenor meaning), makniyya (tenor word with implicit resemblance), takhyiliyya (attributes of vehicle given to tenor), tarshihiyya (suitable attributes of vehicle given to tenor).
Each type corresponds to a different structural relation in the metaphor.
3
Apply the types to the given similes
Work through the examples: shari'ah compared to a tree, al-Hanafiyya to a tree, and kalimat al-baqiya to a lofty building. For each, identify which type(s) of isti'arah are present.
Multiple types can apply to different parts of the same simile.
4
Consider the tamthil vs. literal debate
Some scholars consider the entire expression as tamthil (composite simile), while 'Allama Khusru insists on a literal interpretation when possible. Weigh the arguments.
Tamthil compares composite states; literal interpretation preserves the text's apparent meaning.
5
Synthesize the usul principle
Conclude that in Hanafi usul, literal meaning is preferred unless clear evidence requires figurative interpretation, especially when the literal meaning includes subtleties.
This principle guides jurists in deriving rulings from Qur'anic similes.

Source Text

حقیقت اور مجاز کے درمیان علاقہ تشبیہ کا ہوگا یا غیر تشبیہ کا اگر علاقہ غیر تشبیہ کا ہو تو یہ مجاز مرسل ہے اور اگر علاقہ تشبیہ کا ہو تو یہ استعارہ ہے پھر استعارہ کی چار قسمیں ہیں اگر ذکر مشبہ بہ کا ہو اور مراد مشبہ ہو تو استعارہ تصریحیہ ہو گا جیسے "رایت اسدا نیز می" اور اگر ذکر مشبہ کا ہو اور مراد بھی مشبہ ہو لیکن وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہو تو یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہے اور اگر مشبہ بہ کے لوازمات مشبہ کے بھی مشبہ ہے لیکن وجہ تشبیہ مضمر فی النفس ہے تو یہ استعارہ مکیہ ہے، مشبہ بہ یعنی درخت کے لوازمات میں سے ہے کہ اس کی جڑیں ہوں تو اصول میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور درخت (مشبہ بہ ) کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کہ وہ مضبوط ہو تو حکم میں استعارہ ترشیہ ہے اسی طرح الحنیفیہ کو تشبیہ دی ہے درخت سے اور وجہ تشبیہ مذکور نہیں تو اس میں استعارہ مکنیہ ہے اور درخت مشبہ بہ کے لوازمات یعنی فروع کو ثابت کیا ہے مشبہ یعنی الخلیفیہ کے لئے تو یہ استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور اس کے مناسبات یعنی رفع کو ثابت کیا ہے مشبہ کے لئے تو رفع میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے۔ كلمته الباقية (كلمه توحيد ) کو تشبیہ دی ہے بلند عمارت کے ساتھ تو ذکر مشبہ کا مراد بھی مشبہ ہے تو اس میں استعارہ مکنیہ ہے اور مشبہ بہ کے لوازمات میں سے ہے کہ اس کی بنیاد میں ہوں تو اساس میں استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے اور عمارت کے مناسبات میں سے ہے کہ وہ بلند و بالا ہو تو شامتہ البناء میں استعارہ ترشیجیہ ہے۔ اور عند البعض یہ ساری عبارت تمثیل کے قبیل سے ہے۔ تعریف تمثیل : تمثیل کہتے ہیں بعض ملی جلی ہوئی اشیاء سے حاصل ہونے والی ہیئت کو دوسری ملی جلی ہوئی اشیاء سے حاصل ہونے والی بیت اور حالت سے تشبیہ دینے کو تو یہاں بھی شرعیت اور اصول اور فروع سے حاصل ہونے والی شکل کو تشبیہ دی گئی ہے۔ عمارت اور اس کی بنیادوں اور بلندی سے حاصل ہونے والی شکل کے ساتھ ۔ علامہ خسرو کی تحقیق : ۔ لیکن علامہ خسرو فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں نہ استعارہ ہے اور نہ ہی تمثیل ہے بلکہ کلام اپنی حقیقت پر محمول ہے اور ضابطہ بھی یہی ہے کہ جب تک ممکن ہو کلام کو اپنی حقیقت پر محمول کیا جائے خصوصاً جب حقیقت کلام لطائف کو بھی متضمن ہو ۔ خلاصہ اس کا یہ ہے کہ ہمارے لئے دو امر ہیں اور ان میں سے ہر ایک امر کے دو پہلو ہیں اور ہر ایک امر اپنے دونوں پہلووں سمیت دوسرے امر پر اور اس کی جانین پر مرتب ہے ان دو امروں میں سے ایک شرعیت ہے اور اس کے دو پہلو ہیں (۱) عقائد جو شرعیت کے لئے اصول کا درجہ رکھتے ہیں (۲) احکام عملیہ جو فروع کا درجہ رکھتے ہیں۔ دوسرا امر کلمہ شہادت ہے اور اس کے بھی دو پہلو ہیں (۱) ایمان جو کلمہ شہادت کے لئے اصل ہے (۲) عمل صالح جو کلمہ کی فرع ہے۔ اب دوسرا امریعنی کلمہ شہادت مرتب ہے امر اول یعنی شرعیت پر اور اسکی ایک جانب یعنی ایمان مرتب ہے عقائد پر اور دوسری جانب یعنی عمل صالح مرتب ہے احکام شرعیہ پر تو شاریخ نے پہلے جملہ میں امر اول اور اس کی جانین یعنی شرعیت اور اصول اور فروع حنیفیہ کو ذکر کیا اور دوسرے جملہ میں امرثانی کلمہ شہادت اور اس کے دونوں پہلوؤں ( ایمان اور عمل صالح ) کو ذکر کیا اور آخر میں لطیف انداز سے کشجرۃ طیبہ سے اس کی مثال بیان کر دی۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
Between haqiqat and majaz, the relationship (alaqa) is either tashbih (resemblance) or non-tashbih. If the relationship is non-tashbih, it is majaz mursal; if it is tashbih, it is isti'arah. Then isti'arah has four types: (1) If the word for the vehicle (musabbah bihi) is mentioned and the intended meaning is the tenor (musabbah), it is isti'arah tashrihiyya, e.g., 'I saw a lion' (meaning a brave man). (2) If the word for the tenor is mentioned and the intended meaning is also the tenor, but the reason for resemblance (wajh al-tashbih) is implicit, it is isti'arah makniyya. (3) If the accessories (lawazim) of the vehicle are attributed to the tenor, it is isti'arah takhyiliyya. (4) If the suitable attributes (munasabat) of the vehicle are attributed to the tenor, it is isti'arah tarshihiyya. Now understand: the author (musannif) has made a tashbih of shari'ah to a tree. The word for the tenor (musabbah) is mentioned and the intended meaning is also the tenor, but the reason for resemblance is implicit, so it is isti'arah makniyya. From the accessories of the vehicle (tree) is that it has roots, so in 'usul' it is isti'arah takhyiliyya, and from the suitable attributes of the tree is that it is strong, so in 'hukm' it is isti'arah tarshihiyya. Similarly, the Hanafi school (al-Hanafiyya) is compared to a tree, and the reason for resemblance is not mentioned, so in that comparison it is isti'arah makniyya, and the accessories of the vehicle (tree) i.e., branches (furu') are attributed to the tenor (al-Hanafiyya), so that is isti'arah takhyiliyya, and its suitable attributes i.e., elevation (raf') are attributed to the tenor, so in 'raf'' it is isti'arah tarshihiyya. The 'remainder word' (kalimat al-baqiya, i.e., the word of tawhid) is compared to a lofty building, so the word for the tenor is mentioned, the intended meaning is also the tenor, so in that comparison it is isti'arah makniyya. From the accessories of the vehicle is that it has a foundation, so in 'asas' it is isti'arah takhyiliyya, and from the suitable attributes of the building is that it is high and lofty, so in 'shamitat al-bina'' it is isti'arah tarshihiyya. According to some, this entire expression is of the category of tamthil. Definition of tamthil: Tamthil is to compare a state or condition derived from some composite things to another state or condition derived from other composite things. So here too, the form derived from shari'ah, usul, and furu' is compared to the form derived from a building, its foundations, and its height. Investigation of 'Allama Khusru: But 'Allama Khusru says that here neither isti'arah nor tamthil is present; rather, the speech is taken in its literal (haqiqi) meaning, and the principle is that when possible, speech should be taken in its literal meaning, especially when the literal meaning also includes delicate subtleties. The summary: For us there are two matters, and each of these two matters has two aspects, and each matter with both its aspects is related to the other matter and its sides. Of these two matters, one is shari'ah, and its two aspects are (1) beliefs (aqa'id), which are like usul for shari'ah, and (2) practical rulings (ahkam 'amaliyya), which are like furu'. The second matter is the word of shahadah (kalimat al-shahadah), and it also has two aspects: (1) iman, which is the asl for the word of shahadah, and (2) righteous action ('amal salih), which is its far'. Now the second matter, i.e., the word of shahadah, is related to the first matter, i.e., shari'ah, and one of its sides, i.e., iman, is related to beliefs, and the other side, i.e., righteous action, is related to the rulings of shari'ah. So the commentator (sharih) mentioned in the first sentence the first matter and its two sides—shari'ah, its usul and its furu' Hanafiyya—and in the second sentence he mentioned the second matter, the word of shahadah, and its two aspects (iman and righteous action), and at the end he subtly presented the example from the good tree (kashajaratin tayyibah). And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the classification of metaphorical language in the context of usul al-fiqh. The author first distinguishes between haqiqah and majaz, then defines majaz mursal and isti'arah based on the relationship (علاقہ). If the relationship is resemblance (tashbih), it is isti'arah; otherwise, it is majaz mursal. Then he lists four types of isti'arah: tashrihiyya (explicit), makniyya (implicit), takhyiliyya (imaginative), and tarshihiyya (augmentative). He applies these to the example of comparing shari'ah to a tree, and the Hanafi school to a tree, and the word of tawhid to a lofty building. Some scholars consider the entire expression as tamthil (simile), but 'Allama Khusru insists on taking the text in its literal meaning, especially when the literal meaning includes subtle benefits. He then provides a detailed analysis of two matters (shari'ah and kalimat al-shahadah) and their aspects, showing how they are interlinked, and concludes that the commentator (sharih) subtly referenced the Quranic verse 'like a good tree' (kashajaratin tayyibah).

Key Terms
استعارہ (isti‘ārah): A metaphorical expression where one word is used for another due to resemblance (tashbih).
مجاز مرسل (majāz mursal): Metaphor where the relationship is non-resemblance (e.g., causal).
تشبیہ (tashbīh): Simile; the basis for isti'arah.
تمثیل (tamthīl): A simile comparing composite forms from different sets of things.
استعارہ تصریحیہ (isti‘ārah taṣrīḥiyyah): Explicit metaphor: vehicle word mentioned, tenor intended.
استعارہ مکنیہ (isti‘ārah makniyyah): Implicit metaphor: tenor mentioned, resemblance implicit.
استعارہ تخیلیہ (isti‘ārah takhyīliyyah): Imaginative metaphor: accessories of vehicle attributed to tenor.
استعارہ ترشیحیہ (isti‘ārah tarshīḥiyyah): Augmentative metaphor: suitable attributes of vehicle attributed to tenor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is a metaphorical expression called 'isti'arah tashrihiyyah'?
A) When the word for the vehicle (musabbah bihi) is mentioned, but the intended meaning is the tenor (musabbah).
B) When the word for the tenor is mentioned, and the intended meaning is the vehicle.
C) When the accessories of the vehicle are attributed to the tenor.
D) When the word for the vehicle is mentioned, and the intended meaning is the vehicle itself.

Key Takeaway
Isti'arah has four types based on how vehicle and tenor relate; Hanafi usul prefers literal interpretation when possible, especially when subtleties are present.

Wisdom of Using Hal for Praise in Opening Statements
Commentator explains why matn used hal for praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify why the author deviated from customary praise structures and explain the grammatical rationale using the concept of hal in Usul al-Fiqh texts.

Core Idea
Praise is made a hal to subordinate it as a condition, equalizing it with the basmalah.

In this passage from the commentary on al-Talwih, the commentator explains a deliberate grammatical choice: praising Allah (hamd) is presented as a circumstantial accusative (hal) rather than a main clause. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind that choice, showing how such nuances reflect deeper legal and textual considerations in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify customary sentence types for praise
Recognize that normally, opening praise is expressed as a nominal sentence (e.g., al-hamdu lillah) or a verbal sentence (e.g., nahmadu Allah). These are main sentence elements.
2
Locate the deviation in the matn
The author instead used 'hamid' as a hal, which is a subordinate element describing the state of the speaker. This is the deviation from the customary style.
3
Grasp the reason: equality with basmalah
The commentator explains that the author intended to create equality between the hamd and the basmalah. Since the basmalah was already made a hal, the hamd follows suit; both become conditions (qayd) of the action 'I begin'.
4
Analyze the objection and response
An objection arises: if hal requires an implicit operator ('abtadi'u'), it effectively becomes a verbal sentence, negating the deviation. The answer clarifies that the deviation is not about sentence type but about the prominence of praise as a main part vs. subordinate condition.
The deviation is demoting praise from main element to condition.
5
Conclude the implication for usul
This grammatical choice signals that praise is a subordinate condition (qayd) of the act, not the act itself. This affects how legal texts interpret opening statements, consistent with Hanafi attention to grammatical nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حمد میں مشہور طریقہ سے عدول کی حکمت
قولہ آثر :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے اس عبارت سے شاریخ کی غرض سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ مائن نے حمد کے مشہور طریقہ یعنی جملہ اسمیہ اور جملہ فعلیہ سے عدول کیوں کیا؟
جواب: ماتن در اصل حمد اور تسمیہ میں برابری کرنا چاہتے ہیں اور ماتن نے حمد اور تسمیہ میں برابری دو طرح سے کی ہے۔ نمبرا ۔ جس طرح بسم اللہ کو ابدی کی انا ضمیر سے حال بنایا ہے۔ حامد کو بھی انا ضمیر سے حال بنایا ہے۔ تاکہ یہ دونوں ابتداء کی قید بن جائیں کیونکہ حال ذوالحال کے لئے قید ہوتا ہے اور تسمیہ وتحمید میں قید اور حال ہونے کے اعتبار سے تسویہ و برابری پائی جائے نمبر ۲۔ تسمیہ وتحمید میں رعایت تناسب کی دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ دونوں کو جنس واحد سے قید بنایا ہے یعنی دونوں کو حال بنایا ہے۔ ایک کو حال اور دوسری کو ظرف یا کسی اور جنس سے ابتداء کی قید نہیں بنایا۔
سوال:۔ حال بھی عامل کا تقاضا کرتا ہے تو حامد أحال کے عامل کو مقدر ماننے کے بعد یہ بھی جملہ فعلیہ بن جائے گا۔ یعنی جب یہاں عامل ابدی کو مان لیں تو یہ جملہ فعلیہ بن جائے گا۔ تو پھر مشہور طریقہ سے عدول تو نہ ہوا۔ لہذا ماقبل والا اعتراض وارد ہی نہیں ہوگا کہ جس کا جواب دینے کی ضرورت ہو۔
جواب:۔ سوال کی تقریر یہ نہیں ہے کہ جملہ فعلیہ اور جملہ اسمیہ سے عدول کیوں کیا ؟ بلکہ سوال یہ ہے کہ مشہور اور متعارف طریقہ یہ ہے کہ ایسا جملہ ذکر کیا جاتا ہے کہ جس میں حمد مسند یا مسند الیہ بن کر جملہ کا عمدہ جز و واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اور یہاں حمد کو قید بنایا ہے جملہ کا عمدہ جز نہیں بنایا اس کی کیا وجہ ہے؟ ( فلا اعتراض)
The wisdom of deviating from the customary style in praising
His statement 'athara': This is the second part of the commentary’s expression. The commentator’s purpose from this expression is to answer a presumed question. Question: Why did the author (matn) deviate from the customary way of expressing praise, i.e., the nominal sentence and the verbal sentence?
Answer: The author actually intended to create equality between praise and the mentioning of Allah's name (tasmiyah). The author established equality in two ways. First: Just as he made 'bismillah' a 'hal' from the pronoun 'ana' of 'abtadi'u', he also made 'hamid' a 'hal' from the pronoun 'ana', so that both become conditions (qayd) of the beginning, because a 'hal' is a condition for its owner (dhu al-hal). Thus, equality is achieved between tasmiyah and tahmid in terms of being a condition and a 'hal'. Second: Another reason for maintaining harmony between tasmiyah and tahmid is that he made both conditions from a single genus, i.e., he made both 'hal'; he did not make one a 'hal' and the other a 'zarf' or from another genus as a condition of the beginning.
Question: A 'hal' also requires an operator ('amil); so if we consider the operator of 'hamid' as implicit, then it too becomes a verbal sentence. That is, if we take 'abtadi'u' as the operator here, then it becomes a verbal sentence. Then the deviation from the customary way would not have occurred. Therefore, the previous objection would not arise, which needed an answer.
Answer: The formulation of the question is not that the deviation from the verbal sentence or nominal sentence has occurred for no reason. Rather, the question is that the customary and common way is to mention such a sentence where praise becomes the predicate or subject, i.e., a main part of the sentence. Here, praise has been made a condition (qayd), not a main part of the sentence; what is the reason for that? (So there is no objection).
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage addresses the wisdom behind the author's choice to present 'hamd' (praising Allah) not as a main clause (nominal or verbal sentence) but as a circumstantial accusative (hal). The commentator explains that the author aimed for equality between the basmalah and the hamd. The basmalah was made a hal describing the state of the speaker, so to achieve symmetry, the hamd was also made a hal. This way, both serve as conditions (qayd) of the action 'I begin'. The second point of equality is that both are from the same grammatical category (hal), not one as hal and the other as something else. Then a potential objection is raised: if hamd is a hal, it requires an operator, which could be the implicit verb 'abtadi'u', making it effectively a verbal sentence, thus nullifying the deviation. The answer clarifies that the objection misunderstands the nature of the deviation. The deviation is not from using a verbal or nominal sentence per se, but from the typical placement of praise as a main part of the sentence (subject or predicate). Here, praise is demoted to a subordinate 'hal', which is the unconventional aspect.

Key Terms
جملہ اسمیہ (jumla ismiyya): A nominal sentence beginning with a noun.
جملہ فعلیہ (jumla fi'liyya): A verbal sentence beginning with a verb.
حال (hal): A circumstantial accusative describing the state of the subject or object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main reason given for making 'hamd' a 'hal'?
A) To avoid repeating the same structure.
B) To create equality with the basmalah (tasmiyah).
C) Because Arabic grammar requires it in this context.
D) To emphasize the praise over the basmalah.

Key Takeaway
The author's choice to make hamd a hal is a deliberate grammatical strategy to subordinate praise as a condition, equalizing it with the basmalah.

Interpreting 'Firstly and Secondly' in Praise of Allah
Explaining three interpretations of 'firstly and secondly' in praising Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three possible interpretations of 'awwalan wa thaniyan' in praising Allah and explain how each interpretation draws on different aspects of Allah's perfection and blessings.

Core Idea
Praising Allah 'firstly and secondly' can refer to His essence and His blessings, or to origination and preservation, or to praise in this world and the Hereafter.

This passage from a Hanafi usul text unpacks the phrase 'awwalan wa thaniyan' (firstly and secondly) used in praising Allah. It presents three distinct interpretive possibilities, showing the richness of Islamic theological reflection and the careful analysis that scholars apply even to seemingly simple phrases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three interpretations
List the three possibilities given in the passage: (1) praise for essence/attributes (first) and for blessings (second); (2) praise for origination (first) and preservation (second); (3) praise in this world (first) and the Hereafter (second).
2
Examine the basis of each interpretation
For each interpretation, note what is being prioritized: the first emphasizes Allah's intrinsic perfection versus His favors; the second divides blessings into creation and sustenance; the third distinguishes between this life and the afterlife.
The second interpretation is supported by quoting Quranic surahs that begin with praise and focus on either origination or preservation.
3
Understand the concluding redirection
The passage ends by explaining that 'turning the reins of praise to Him secondly' means directing all praise solely to Allah, recognizing that all worship should be for Him alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا تَفضِيلُ الحَمدِ بِقَولِهِ أَوَّلًا وَثَانِيَا فَيَحْتَمِلُ وُجُوهَا : الأَوَّلُ أَنَّ الحَمدَ يَكُونُ عَلَى النِّعْمَةِ وَغَيرِهَا فَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى يَستَحِقُّ الحَمدَ أَوَّلًا لِكَمَالِ ذَاتِهِ وَعَظَمَةِ صِفَاتِهِ وَثَانِيَا بِجَمِيلِ نَعمَالِهِ وَجَزِيلٍ آلايْهِ الَّتِى مِن جُملَتِهَا التَّوفِيقُ لِتَالِيفِ هَذَا الكِتَابِ الثَّانِي أَنَّ نِعَمَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى كَثَرَتِهَا تَرْجِعُ إِلَى إِيجَادٍ وَإِبِقَاءِ أَوَّلًا وَإِيجَادِ وَإِيقَاء ثَانِبًا فَيَحمَدَهُ عَلَى القِسَمَينِ تَأْسيًا بِالسُّوَرِ المُفَتَّحَةِ بالتحمِيدِ حَيثُ أُشِيرَ فِي الفَاتِحَةِ إِلَى الجَمِيعِ وَفِي الْانعَامِ إِلَى الإِيجَادِ وَفِي الكَهْفِ إِلَى الإِبقَاءِ أَوَّلًا وَفِي السَّبَأُ إِلَى الإِيجَادِ وَفِي المَلَائِكَةِ إِلَى الإِبقَاءِ ثَانِيًا. الثَّالِث المُلاحَظَةُ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُ الحَمدُ فِي الأُولَى وَالآخِرَةِ عَلَى مَعنَى أَنَّهُ يَسْتَحِقُّ الحَمدَ فِي الدُّنْيَا عَلَى مَا يُعرَفْ بِالحُجَّةِ مِن كَمَالِهِ وَيَصِلُ إِلَى العِبَادِ مِن نَوَالِهِ وَفِي الآخِرَةِ عَلَى مَا يُشَاهَدُ مِن كِبْرِيَائِهِ وَيُعَايَنُ مِن نَعْمَائِهِ الَّتِي لَا عَينٌ رَأَت وَلَا أُذُنٌ سَمِعَت وَلَا خَطَرَتْ عَلَى قَلبِ بَشَرٍ وَإِلَيْهِ الْإِشَارَةُ بِقَولِهِ تَعَالَى وَآخِرُ دَعوَاهُم أَن الحَمدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ العَالَمِينَ فَإِن قُلت فَقَد وَقَعَ التَّعَرُّضُ لِلحَمدِ عَلَى الكبرِيَّاءِ وَالآلاءِ فِى دَارَى الفَنَاءِ وَالبَقَاءِ فَمَا مَعْنَى قَولِهِ وَلِعَنانِ الثَّنَاءِ إِلَيْهِ ثَانِيَا أَى : صَارِفًا عَطَفًا عَلَى حَامِدًا قُلتُ : مَعْنَاهُ قَصِدُ تَعظِيمِهِ وَنِيَّةُ التَّقَرُّبِ إِلَيْهِ فِي كُلِّ مَا يَصلُحُ لِذَلِكَ مِن الأَقوَالِ وَالْأَفعَالِ وَصَرِفِ الْأَمْوَالِ إِشَارَةً إِلَى أَنْوَاعِ العِبَادَاتِ فَإِنَّ نِعَمَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى تَستَوجِبُ الشُّكَرَ بِالقَلبِ وَاللَّسَانِ وَالجَوَارِحِ وَالْحَمدُ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا بِاللَّسَانِ وَفِيهِ إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى أَنَّ الأُخِذَ فِي العُلُومِ الإِسْلَامِيَّةِ يَنبَغِي أَن يُعرِضَ عَن جَانِبِ الخَلقِ وَيَصْرِفَ أَعِنَّةَ الثَّنَاءِ مِن جَمِيعِ الجِهَاتِ إِلَى جَنَابِ الحَقِّ تَعَالَى وَتَقَدَّسَ عَالِمًا بِأَنَّهُ المُستَحِقُّ لِلثَّنَاءِ وَحدَهُ
ترجمہ: اور لیکن حمد کی تفصیل بیان کرنا اس کے قول اولا و ثانیا سے پس کئی صورتوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ پہلا احتمال کہ حمد بھی نعمت پر ہوتی ہے اور کبھی غیر نعمت پر ۔ پس اللہ تعالیٰ اول احمد کے مستحق ہیں کمال ذات اور عظمت صفات کی وجہ سے اور ثانیا حمد کے مستحق ہیں اچھی اچھی نعمتوں اور بڑے بڑے احسانات کی وجہ سے اور ان تمام احسانات میں سے ایک اس کتاب کو لکھنے کی توفیق دینا ہے۔ دوسرا احتمال کہ اللہ تعالی کی نعمتیں اپنی کثرت کے باوجود لوٹتی ہیں ایجا داؤ لی ابقاء اولی کی طرف اور ایجاد ثانوی اور ابقاء ثانوی
As for the detailing of praise by his saying 'firstly and secondly', it admits of several possibilities: The first: that praise is for blessings and other things. So Allah, exalted, deserves praise firstly for the perfection of His essence and the greatness of His attributes, and secondly for the beautiful blessings and abundant favors, among which is the success to compose this book. The second: that the blessings of Allah, exalted, despite their abundance, return to origination and preservation firstly, and origination and preservation secondly. So He is praised for the two divisions, following the example of the surahs opened with praise, where in al-Fatihah reference is made to all, in al-An'am to origination, in al-Kahf to preservation firstly, and in Saba' to origination, and in al-Mala'ikah to preservation secondly. The third: consideration of His saying, 'To Him belongs praise in the first and the last,' meaning that He deserves praise in this world for what is known by proof of His perfection and what reaches the servants of His bounty, and in the Hereafter for what is witnessed of His grandeur and what is seen of His blessings that no eye has seen, nor ear heard, nor has occurred to the heart of man. To this refers His saying, 'And the last of their call will be: Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds.' If you say: he has already referred to praise for grandeur and favors in the two abodes of annihilation and eternity, so what is the meaning of his saying 'and turning the reins of praise to Him secondly'? I say: its meaning is the intention of glorifying Him and the resolve to draw near to Him in everything suitable for that from words, deeds, and spending of wealth, indicating the types of worship. For the blessings of Allah, exalted, require gratitude with the heart, tongue, and limbs, and praise is only with the tongue. And in this is an indication that the student of Islamic sciences should turn away from the aspect of creation and direct the reins of praise from all directions towards the court of the Truth, exalted and sanctified, knowing that He alone deserves praise.
Translation: But detailing praise by his saying 'firstly and secondly' admits of several possibilities. The first possibility: praise is for blessings and sometimes for non-blessings. So Allah, exalted, deserves praise firstly for the perfection of essence and greatness of attributes, and secondly for beautiful blessings and abundant favors, among which is the success to compose this book. The second possibility: the blessings of Allah, exalted, despite their abundance, return to origination and preservation firstly, and origination and preservation secondly.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the phrase 'أولاً وثانياً' (firstly and secondly) in praising Allah. The author presents three possible interpretations. The first: praise is for His essence and attributes (firstly) and for His blessings (secondly). The second: looking at blessings as divided into origination (first) and preservation (second), citing Quranic surahs that begin with praise. The third: based on the verse 'له الحمد في الأولى والآخرة' (to Him belongs praise in the first and the last), praise in this world is for His perfection and blessings known by proof, and in the Hereafter for what is witnessed of His grandeur and unseen blessings. The passage then explains the phrase 'ولعنان الثناء إليه ثانيا' (and turning the reins of praise to Him secondly) as indicating that the student of Islamic sciences should direct all praise solely to Allah, since only He deserves it. The Urdu translation summarizes the first two possibilities.

Key Terms
أولاً وثانياً (awwalan wa thaniyan): Firstly and secondly, used to sequence the types or aspects of praise.
عنان الثناء (inan al-thana'): The reins of praise, a metaphor for directing praise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the third possibility of 'awwalan wa thaniyan' refer to?
A) Praise for essence and attributes firstly, blessings secondly.
B) Praise for origination firstly, preservation secondly.
C) Praise in this world firstly, in the Hereafter secondly.
D) Praise with the tongue firstly, with the heart secondly.

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'awwalan wa thaniyan' in praise admits multiple valid interpretations based on what aspects of Allah's perfection and blessings are being prioritized.

Resolving Hal Simultaneity and Avoiding Jam' bayn al-Haqiqah wa al-Majaz
Commentary defending grammatical and usul coherence of opening phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul method of positing an extended agent action (ibtida' mutlaq) to justify a hal's simultaneity, and construct a plausible omission (hadhf) to avoid combining literal and metaphorical meanings in a single word.

Core Idea
A hal can be simultaneous with an extended agent action; an omitted word prevents combining literal and metaphorical meanings.

In Hanafi usul, every word in a revealed text is presumed to have a single meaning. This lesson examines a classical commentary that defends the grammatical construction of the basmalah and hamdalah by addressing two objections: temporal mismatch and combining literal and metaphorical. The commentator demonstrates that when the agent's action (the beginning of the book) is understood as an extended absolute beginning, the hal's simultaneity is preserved. Furthermore, by positing an implied second 'hamid', the problematic combination of meanings is avoided, adhering to the usul principle that prohibits using one word for both literal and metaphorical intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the relevant rule
Recall the grammatical rule that the hal (circumstantial accusative) must be simultaneous in time with its agent (the 'owner' of the state).
2
Analyze the first objection
The objection states that if 'hāmidan' is a hal for the agent 'ana' (implied in the basmalah), the action of beginning with Allah's name occurs prior to the praise, breaking simultaneity. Identify the temporal gap.
The objector assumes the beginning is instantaneous.
3
Apply the Hanafi response
The commentator distinguishes between an absolute beginning (ibtidā' muṭlaq) that extends from the start of composition to the start of research, and a restricted beginning (muqayyad) that is instantaneous. Here the intended beginning is the absolute one, so the time of the agent extends, allowing the hal to overlap.
This is a key Hanafi usul move: interpreting time as extended to preserve coherence.
4
Recognize the second objection
If 'hāmidan thaniyan' is interpreted as praise in the afterlife (metaphorical), the agent's time does not extend that far. The objection forces a reinterpretation: 'thaniyan' means 'intending praise', which is now metaphorical. This raises the issue of using the same word 'hāmidan' for both literal (verbal praise) and metaphorical (intention) meanings.
5
Apply the solution of hadhf (omission)
The commentator posits that the second 'hāmidan' is actually a separate omitted word: the original construction is 'hāmidan awwalan wa hāmidan thaniyan'. By treating the second as an omitted instance, each meaning attaches to a distinct word, avoiding the forbidden combination of literal and metaphorical in one word.
This shows the Hanafi principle that hadhf can be assumed to resolve apparent conflicts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِالتَّسْمِيَةِ وَالحَمدِ وَالصَّلاةِ فَإِن قُلتَ : فَعَلَى الوَجهِ الثَّالِثِ يَكُونُ حَامِدًا ثَانِيَا بِمَعنَى نَاوِيًا لِلحَمدِ وَعَازِمًا عَلَيْهِ لِيَكُونَ مُقَارِنَا لِلعَامِلِ وَحِينَيْذٍ يَلزَمُ الجَمْعُ بَينَ الحَقِيقَةِ وَالمَجَازِ قُلتُ : يُجعَلُ مِن قَبيلِ المَحذُوفِ أَى وَحَامِدًا ثَانِيَا بِمَعْنَى عَازِمًا عَلَيهِ فَلا يَلزَمُ الجَمعُ بَيْنَ الْحَقِيقَةِ وَالْمَجَازِ .
ترجمہ:۔ پس اگر تو کہے کہ حال بننے کیلئے شرط ہے عامل کے ساتھ ملا ہوا ہونا اور مذکورہ احوال مراد لیتا ہوں میں حامد أو غیرہ کو ابتداء بالتسمیہ کے ساتھ ملے ہوئے نہیں ہیں۔ میں جواب میں کہوں گا۔ (باء ) ابتدی کا مان ہیں بلکہ ظرف (متبر کا) کے متعلق ہو کر حال ہے اور تقدیر عبارت ہے متبر کا بسم اللہ ابتدئ الكتاب اور ابتداء امر عرفی ہے اور اس کا ممتد ہونا اعتبار کیا جاتا ہے شروع فی التصنیف سے شروع فی البحث تک اور اس کے ساتھ تبرک بالتسمیہ اور اسی طرح جمد وصلوٰۃ سے تبرک حاصل کرنا ملا ہوا ہے۔ پس اگر تو کہے تیسری صورت میں دوسرا حامد آنا دیا اور عازنا ( یعنی آخرت میں حمد کی نیت کرنے والا ہوں ) کے معنی میں ہوگا تا کہ یہ حال اپنے عامل (اندی) کے زمانہ کے ساتھ ملا ہوا ہو سکے اور اس وقت جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز لازم آئے گا۔ میں کہتا ہوں کہ اس کو محذوف کے قبیل سے بنایا جائے گا۔ اور تقدیر عبارت ہوگی۔ حامد الثانیا اور اس وقت یہ عاز ما کے معنی میں ہوگا۔ تو جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز لازم نہیں آئے گا۔
تحقیق لغوی : تعرض باب تفعل سے ہے ۔ بمعنی در پے ہونا۔ طلب کرنا نعم جمع ہے نعمت کی ۔ ”اعنہ عنان کی جمع ہے بمعنی لگام تقدس ہر عیب سے پاک ہونا۔
حامد ا یعنی حال اور اس کے عامل کا زمانہ ایک ہے
تشریح قولہ فان قلت:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا گیارہواں حصہ ہے۔ غرض شارح ایک اعتراض کرنا ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حامد ا کو ابتدئی کی انا ضمیر سے حال نہیں بنا سکتے۔ کیونکہ ضابطہ ہے کہ حال و ذو الحال کا زمانہ ایک ہوتا ہے اور یہاں پر زمانہ ایک نہیں ہے کیونکہ بسم الله ابدی کے متعلق ہے اور اس کی قید ہے تو ابتداء مقید بالقسمیہ ہوئی اور ظاہر ہے کہ ابتداء بالقسمیہ مقدم ہے زمانہ کے اعتبار سے اور حمد مؤخر ہے۔ تو حال اور عامل کا زمانہ ایک نہ ہوا۔
قلت :۔ یہ عبارت کا بارہواں حصہ ہے اور غرض شاریخ سوال مذکور کا جواب دینا ہے ۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ابتداء کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ابتداء مطلق اور ابتداء مقید ۔ ابتداء مطلق فعل ممتد ہے مقصود کے شروع ہونے تک۔ اور ابتداء مقید بالتسمیہ غیر ممتد ہے۔ یہاں ابتداء سے مراد ابتداء مطلق ہے تو ابتدئی اور حامد ا کا زمانہ ایک ہوا۔
قوله فان قلت :۔ یہ عبارت کا تیرواں حصہ ہے۔ اور غرض شاریخ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے پھر اس جواب پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ تیسری صورت میں اولا سے مراد دنیا میں محمد ہے اور ثانیا سے مراد آخرت میں حمد ہے۔ جب مصنف آخرت میں گیا ہی نہیں تو پھر وہاں تعریف کیسے کر لی۔ اور اگر وہاں جانے کے بعد تعریف کرنا مراد ہے تو پھر حال اور اس کے عامل کے زمانہ میں مقارنت نہیں رہے گی کیونکہ ابتداء مقصود تک تو ممتد ہو سکتی ہے آخرت تک نہیں۔
جواب:۔ ثانیا سے مراد نا دیا ہے۔ یعنی آخرت میں تعریف کی نیت کرنے والا ہوں اور نیت دنیا میں بھی پائی جاسکتی ہے پھر اس جواب پر اعتراض ہوتا ہے۔ حمد فی الدنیا والآخرة کی صورت میں جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز لازم نہیں آتا
سوال :۔ حامد ا اولا سے مراد حقیقی معنی لیا ہے یعنی زبان سے تعریف کرنا اور ثانیا سے مجازی معنی مراد لیا ہے یعنی حمد کی نیت کرنا تو ایک ہی لفظ ( حامد ) سے ایک ہی وقت میں حقیقی اور مجازی معنی مراد لیا ہے یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز ہے اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ قلت: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ سوال بالا کا جواب دینا ہے۔
جواب: جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز تب لازم آتا ہے کہ جب ہم ایک لفظ سے دو معنی مراد لیتے ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں تانیا سے پہلے دوسرا حامد محذوف ہے یعنی اصل میں حامداً اولا و حامد أثا نیا ہے تو پہلے حامد اسے حقیقی معنی اور دوسرے حامد اسے مجازی معنی مراد لیا ہے۔ لہذا جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز لازم نہیں آتی۔
With the mention of [Allah's] name, praise, and prayer. If you say: On the third aspect, he would be a second 'hamid' (praiser) meaning intending praise and resolving upon it so that it is simultaneous with the agent; and then combining the literal and metaphorical is necessary. I say: It is made from the category of the omitted, i.e., 'and a second hamid' meaning resolving upon it, so combining literal and metaphorical is not necessary. Translation: So if you say: For a hal to be valid, a condition is that it be connected with the agent; and I intend the mentioned states, so 'hamid' or other is not connected with the beginning with the basmalah. I answer: The ba' is for beginning, but it is a zarf (circumstantial) related to the verb, and it is a hal; and the implied expression is 'I begin the book with the name of Allah'; and beginning is a customary matter, and its extension is considered from the start of composition to the start of research; and with it, seeking blessing by the basmalah and similarly by praise and prayer is connected. So if you say: In the third case, the second 'hamid' would be 'azi[؟]' (meaning intending praise in the afterlife) so that this hal can be connected with the time of its agent (the pronoun 'ana'), and then combining literal and metaphorical becomes necessary. I say: This is made from the category of the omitted; the implied expression is 'hamidan al-thaniya' and at that time it means 'aziman', so combining literal and metaphorical is not necessary. Lexical investigation: 'ta'arraza' is from bab tafa''ala, meaning to pursue, to seek. 'ni'am' is plural of 'ni'mah'. 'a'innah' is plural of 'inān' meaning rein. 'taqaddus' means being pure from every defect. 'hamidan' means the time of the hal and its agent is one. Explanation of his statement 'fa-in qulta': This is the eleventh part of the commentary's expression. The aim of the commentator is to raise an objection whose conclusion is that 'hamidan' cannot be made a hal with the pronoun 'ana' of the beginning, because the rule is that the hal and its owner have one time; and here the time is not one because 'bismillah' is related to an eternal matter and is its restriction, so the beginning is restricted by the basmalah, and it is apparent that the beginning with the basmalah is prior in terms of time, and praise is later. So the time of the hal and the agent is not one. 'Qultu': This is the twelfth part, and the aim of the commentator is to answer the mentioned objection, the conclusion of which is that the beginning is of two types: absolute beginning and restricted beginning. The absolute beginning is an extended action until the beginning of the intended thing. The restricted beginning with the basmalah is non-extended. Here the beginning means absolute beginning, so the time of the beginning and 'hamidan' is one. His statement 'fa-in qulta': This is the thirteenth part, and the aim of the commentator is to answer a supposed objection, then an objection is made to that answer. Question: In the third case, 'awwalan' means praise in this world, and 'thaniyan' means praise in the afterlife. When the author has not gone to the afterlife, how can he praise there? If he intends praise after going there, then the hal and the agent's time are not simultaneous because the beginning can extend to the intended end but not to the afterlife. Answer: 'Thaniyan' means 'nāwiyan', i.e., intending praise in the afterlife, and intention can be found in this world. Then an objection is made to this answer: In the case of 'hamd fī al-dunyā wa al-ākhirah', combining literal and metaphorical is not necessary. Question: 'Hamidan awwalan' is taken in its literal meaning, i.e., praising with the tongue, and 'thaniyan' is taken in its metaphorical meaning, i.e., intending praise; so from one word 'hamid' at the same time both literal and metaphorical meanings are intended; this is combining literal and metaphorical, and it is not permissible. 'Qultu': This is the last part of the commentary's expression; the aim of the commentator is to answer the above objection. Answer: Combining literal and metaphorical becomes necessary only when we intend two meanings from a single word. We say: Before 'thaniyan', a second 'hamid' is omitted; i.e., originally it is 'hamidan awwalan wa hamidan thaniyan'; so from the first 'hamid' the literal meaning is intended, and from the second 'hamid' the metaphorical meaning is intended. Therefore combining literal and metaphorical is not necessary.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of the grammatical construction of the basmalah and hamdalah at the beginning of a book. The commentator addresses an objection regarding the temporal relationship between the hal (circumstantial accusative) 'hāmidan' and its agent. The rule is that the hal must share the same time as its agent. The objection is that if 'hāmidan' is a hal for the agent (the implied 'ana'), the agent's action (beginning with basmalah) is prior to the praise, so they are not simultaneous. The response distinguishes between two types of ibtidā' (beginning): the absolute beginning, which is an extended action spanning from the start of composition to the start of research, and the restricted beginning with basmalah, which is instantaneous. Here the intended ibtidā' is the absolute extended one, so the time of the agent and the hal coincide. A further objection arises: if 'hāmidan thaniyan' refers to praise in the afterlife, it cannot be simultaneous with the agent in this world. The answer is that 'thaniyan' means intending praise, which can occur in this world. Then the objection of combining literal and metaphorical (jam' bayn al-ḥaqīqah wa al-majāz) is raised: using 'hāmidan' once for literal praise and once for metaphorical intending. The response posits an omitted second 'hāmidan', so each meaning attaches to a separate word, avoiding the forbidden combination. This analysis follows Hanafi usul methodology in text interpretation.

Key Terms
حال (ḥāl): A circumstantial accusative indicating the state of the agent at the time of the action.
جمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز (jam' bayn al-ḥaqīqah wa al-majāz): Using a single word to convey both its literal and metaphorical meanings simultaneously, which is generally considered impermissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the commentator resolve the objection that the hal 'hāmidan' is not simultaneous with its agent?
A) By arguing that the agent's action is instantaneous.
B) By interpreting the agent's action as an extended absolute beginning, so the time of the hal and agent overlap.
C) By denying the need for simultaneity.
D) By reclassifying 'hāmidan' as a different grammatical element.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul approach to resolving textual ambiguities often involves extending the scope of agent actions or positing omissions, preserving both grammatical correctness and adherence to principles like the prohibition of combining literal and metaphorical meanings.

Causal Reasoning for Placing Salat after Hamd
Explanation of why salat upon the Prophet follows hamd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the causal reasoning (ta'lil) underlying the textual structure of a Hanafi matn and apply the principle of logical priority to understand the order of elements in an introduction.

Core Idea
The author places salat on the Prophet after hamd because the Prophet is the intermediary through whom the supreme blessing (Islam) reaches us—supplication follows praise by causal sequence.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the author of the matn follows hamd (praise of Allah) with salat (blessings) upon the Prophet. The reasoning is not arbitrary but based on a deep theological and logical priority: the greatest blessing is Islam, and it reaches humanity through the Prophet's mediation. Therefore, prayer for the Prophet naturally succeeds praise of Allah. This lesson will dissect this ta'lil and show how it reflects Hanafi usul principles of textual organization.

Guided Path
1
Locate the claim
Identify the statement being justified: the author follows hamd with salat upon the Prophet.
The claim is implicit in the author's structure.
2
Identify the cause (ta'lil)
Find the reason given: the greatest blessing (Islam) reaches servants through the Prophet's mediation.
The term 'بِتَوَسُّطِ النَّبِيِّ' is key.
3
Connect cause to effect
Understand that because the Prophet is the means (tawassut), supplication for him is a natural sequel (tilw) to praise of Allah.
This establishes a causal order: first the source of blessing (Allah), then the channel (Prophet).
4
Notice the subtlety
Observe the implicit reference to the Prophet's name, which indicates his high status is obvious.
This is a stylistic choice highlighting his excellence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ وَعَلَى أَفضَلِ رُسُلِهِ مُصَلِّيًا لَمَّا كَانَ أَجَلُ النِّعَمِ الوَاصِلَةِ إِلَى العَبدِ هُوَ دِينُ الإِسْلامِ وَبِهِ التَّوَصُّلُ إِلَى النِّعَمِ الدَّايُمَةِ فِى دَارِ السَّلَامِ وَذَلِكَ بِتَوَسُّطِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ صَارَ الدُّعَاءُ لَهُ تِلوَ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَأَرْدَفَ الحَمدَ بِالصَّلاةِ وَفِى تَركِ التصريح باسم النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى مَا فِي النُّسخَةِ المُقَرُوءَةِ تَنْوِيةِ بِشَانِهِ وَتَبِيهُ عَلَى أَنَّ كَونَهُ أَفَضَلَ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَمْرٌ جَلِيٌّ
His statement: 'And upon the most excellent of His Messengers, sending blessings.' Since the greatest of blessings reaching the servant is the religion of Islam, and by it one attains permanent blessings in the Abode of Peace, and that is through the mediation of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him), supplication for him became a sequel to praise of Allah Almighty. So he followed praise with salat. And in leaving explicit mention of the Prophet's name, as in the recited copy, is a subtle indication of his status and a notification that his being the most excellent of the Messengers (peace be upon him) is an obvious matter.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage explains the placement of salat (blessing) upon the Prophet after hamd (praise of Allah) in the author's introduction. The reasoning (ta'līl) is that the greatest blessing bestowed upon servants is the religion of Islam, which is the means to eternal blessings in Paradise. This blessing is conveyed through the mediation (tawassuṭ) of the Prophet. Therefore, supplication (du'ā') for the Prophet appropriately follows praise of Allah. The author also notes that leaving the explicit mention of the Prophet's name (as in some copies) subtly highlights his greatness, implying that his superiority is so obvious that it need not be stated. This follows the Hanafi usul principle of structuring texts to reflect logical and theological priorities.

Key Terms
توسّط (tawassuṭ): Mediation or intermediacy; here, the Prophet's role as the means through which the blessing of Islam reaches humanity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the author follow hamd with salat upon the Prophet?
A) Because it is customary in all Islamic writings.
B) Because the Prophet is the best of creation.
C) Because the greatest blessing, Islam, comes through the Prophet's mediation, so prayer for him follows praise of Allah.
D) Because the Prophet requested to be mentioned after every praise.

Key Takeaway
The placement of salat after hamd in a Hanafi matn is not arbitrary but follows a causal logic: the greatest blessing (Islam) reaches us through the Prophet, making supplication for him a natural sequel to praising Allah.

The Rule of Combining Literal and Figurative Meaning (Jama' bayn al-Haqiqa wa al-Majaz)
Resolving an objection about 'hamid' in a commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when combining literal and figurative meaning occurs in a single utterance and apply the Hanafi rule that such combination is not permissible, distinguishing cases with repeated words.

Core Idea
You cannot intend both literal and figurative meanings from one word at once, but separate occurrences of the word avoid the prohibition.

This passage from a commentary addresses a subtle objection about the word 'hamid' (praising). The commentator shows how to avoid the prohibited combination of literal and figurative meaning by treating two instances of the word as separate. Understanding this rule sharpens your ability to interpret legal texts precisely, a core skill in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector claims that using 'hamid' to mean both actual praise (literal) and intention (figurative) at the same time constitutes impermissible combining of literal and figurative meaning. First, recognize what the objection is.
The objection is based on the rule that one word cannot carry both meanings simultaneously.
2
Understand the commentator's answer
The commentator asserts that the phrase is actually 'hamidan awwalan wa hamidan thaniyan' with the second 'hamid' deleted but implied. The two 'hamid's are separate words.
This is a linguistic analysis: the deletion (hadhf) technique avoids the combination.
3
Recognize the underlying rule
The Hanafi position prohibits combining literal and figurative meaning in a single utterance (jama' bayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz). Identify the rule and its rationale.
The rule ensures clarity and prevents ambiguity in legal language.
4
Apply the rule to the case
Since there are two separate words, each carries one meaning. Therefore, no combination occurs. Verify that the commentator's solution respects the rule.
The repetition of the word is key: it is not one word used for both meanings.
5
Distinguish from other scenarios
Consider a scenario where one word is used without repetition and both meanings are intended. That would be a clear violation. Compare and contrast.
This helps solidify the boundary of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله فان قلت :۔ یہ عبارت کا تیرواں حصہ ہے۔ اور غرض شاریخ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے پھر اس جواب پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ سوال:۔ تیسری صورت میں اولا سے مراد دنیا میں محمد ہے اور ثانیا سے مراد آخرت میں حمد ہے۔ جب مصنف آخرت میں گیا ہی نہیں تو پھر وہاں تعریف کیسے کر لی۔ اور اگر وہاں جانے کے بعد تعریف کرنا مراد ہے تو پھر حال اور اس کے عامل کے زمانہ میں مقارنت نہیں رہے گی کیونکہ ابتداء مقصود تک تو ممتد ہو سکتی ہے آخرت تک نہیں۔ جواب:۔ ثانیا سے مراد نا دیا ہے۔ یعنی آخرت میں تعریف کی نیت کرنے والا ہوں اور نیت دنیا میں بھی پائی جاسکتی ہے پھر اس جواب پر اعتراض ہوتا ہے۔ حمد فی الدنیا والآخرة کی صورت میں جمع بین الحقیقة والمجاز لازم نہیں آتا سوال :۔ حامد ا اولا سے مراد حقیقی معنی لیا ہے یعنی زبان سے تعریف کرنا اور ثانیا سے مجازی معنی مراد لیا ہے یعنی حمد کی نیت کرنا تو ایک ہی لفظ ( حامد ) سے ایک ہی وقت میں حقیقی اور مجازی معنی مراد لیا ہے یہ جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز ہے اور یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ قلت: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ سوال بالا کا جواب دینا ہے۔ جواب: جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز تب لازم آتا ہے کہ جب ہم ایک لفظ سے دو معنی مراد لیتے ۔ ہم کہتے ہیں ثانیا سے پہلے دوسرا حامد محذوف ہے یعنی اصل میں حامداً اولا و حامداً ثانیا ہے تو پہلے حامد اسے حقیقی معنی اور دوسرے حامد اسے مجازی معنی مراد لیا ہے۔ لہذا جمع بین الحقیقت والمجاز لازم نہیں آتی۔
His statement: 'For if you say...' This is the thirteenth part of the expression. The commentator's purpose is to answer a presupposed question, then an objection is made on that answer. Question: In the third situation, 'first' refers to praise in the world and 'second' refers to praise in the Hereafter. When the author has not gone to the Hereafter, how can he praise there? And if he intends praise after going there, then there would be no simultaneity in time between the state and its operator, because the beginning can extend to the intended end but not to the Hereafter. Answer: 'Second' refers to intention, i.e., 'I am one who intends praise in the Hereafter,' and intention can be found in the world. Then an objection is raised on this answer: The case of 'praise in the world and the Hereafter' does not necessitate combining literal and figurative meaning. Question: If in 'hamid' (praising) 'first' is taken in its literal meaning (praise by tongue) and 'second' in its figurative meaning (intention of praise), then from a single word (hamid) at one time both literal and figurative meanings are intended, which is combining literal and figurative meaning, and this is not permissible. I say: This is the last part of the commentary's expression; the commentator intends to answer the above question. Answer: Combining literal and figurative meaning would only be necessary if we intend two meanings from one word. We say that before 'thaniyan' another 'hamid' is deleted, so the original is 'hamidan awwalan wa hamidan thaniyan'. The first 'hamid' is taken for literal meaning and the second 'hamid' for figurative meaning. Hence, combining literal and figurative meaning is not necessary.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage from the commentary addresses a potential objection regarding the permissibility of combining literal and figurative meaning (jama' bayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz) in the word 'hamid' (praising). The commentator presents a presupposed question: if 'first' and 'second' refer to praise in this world and the Hereafter respectively, how can the author praise in the Hereafter while still in this world? The answer is that 'second' refers to the intention of praise, which exists in this world. An objector then argues that using 'hamid' to mean both actual praise (literal) and intention (figurative) at the same time constitutes an impermissible combination of literal and figurative meaning. The commentator's final response is that the two instances of 'hamid' are separate words (one deleted but implied), so the combination does not occur. This reflects the Hanafi usul position that combining literal and figurative meanings in a single utterance is not allowed, but here it is avoided by considering two distinct words.

Key Terms
جمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز (jama' bayn al-haqiqa wa al-majaz): Using one word to intend both its literal and figurative meanings simultaneously in one utterance.
حذف (hadhf): Deletion of a word from a phrase while it remains implied, a common linguistic technique in Arabic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how is the problem of combining literal and figurative meaning avoided in the phrase 'hamidan awwalan wa hamidan thaniyan'?
A) By interpreting 'hamid' in only one sense.
B) By deleting the second 'hamid' and implying it.
C) By considering the second 'hamid' as a separate word from the first.
D) By using the word in its figurative sense only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule prohibits combining literal and figurative meaning in a single utterance; the commentator's solution shows that by implying a separate word, the combination is avoided, preserving the rule's integrity.

The Reason for Placing Salat Upon the Prophet After Hamd
Commentary expansion explaining the ordering of salat after hamd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the commentator's rationale for ordering salat after hamd and explain how the omission of the Prophet's name serves exaltation.

Core Idea
The greatest blessing reaches the servant through the Prophet's mediation, so supplication for him follows praise of Allah.

In this passage, the commentator explains why the author placed the invocation of blessings upon the Prophet immediately after praising Allah. He reveals that the greatest blessing—Islam—is attained through the Prophet's role as intermediary. He also justifies the deliberate omission of the Prophet's name as a mark of exaltation. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the textual ordering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
The commentator answers why salat on the Prophet follows hamd. Recognize that the ordering is not arbitrary but has a rationale.
2
Extract the rationale
Find the key sentence: the greatest blessing is Islam, obtained through the Prophet's mediation. This makes supplication for him a 'follower' (talu) of praise of Allah.
The term 'talu' indicates sequential relationship.
3
Analyze the deliberate omission
The commentator notes that the Prophet's name is omitted in the recited version to exalt his status and to indicate that his being the best of messengers is obvious.
Tanwiyah means exaltation.
4
Interpret the racecourse metaphor
The terms 'mujalla' (forerunner) and 'musalla' (follower) from a racecourse are used metaphorically. They can represent either abundant salutation or salutation upon the Prophet and his family respectively.
This enriches the understanding of the relationship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَولُهُ وَعَلَى أَفضَلِ رُسُلِهِ مُصَلِّيًا لَمَّا كَانَ أَجَلُ النِّعَمِ الوَاصِلَةِ إِلَى العَبدِ هُوَ دِينُ الإِسْلامِ وَبِهِ التَّوَصُّلُ إِلَى النِّعَمِ الدَّايُمَةِ فِى دَارِ السَّلَامِ وَذَلِكَ بِتَوَسُّطِ النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ صَارَ الدُّعَاءُ لَهُ تِلوَ الثَّنَاءِ عَلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فَأَرْدَفَ الحَمدَ بِالصَّلاةِ وَفِى تَركِ التصريح باسم النَّبِيِّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ عَلَى مَا فِي النُّسخَةِ المُقَرُوءَةِ تَنْوِيَةً بِشَانِهِ وَتَنْبِيهٌ عَلَى أَنَّ كَونَهُ أَفَضلَ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ أَمْرٌ جَلِيٌّ لَا يَحْفَى عَلَى أَحَدٍ ، وَالحَلَبَةُ بِالسُّكُونِ خَيلٌ تُجمَعُ لِلسِّبَاقِ مِن كُلِّ أَوبِ اُسْتَعِيرَت لِلمضمار . وَالمُجَلَّى هُوَ السَّابِقُ مِن أفراس السّباقِ وَالمُصَلَّى هُوَ الَّذِي يَتْلُوهُ ؛ لِأَنَّ رَأْسَهُ عِندَ صَلَوَيهِ وَمَعَنَى ذَلِكَ تَكثِيرُ الصَّلَاةِ وَتَكْرِيرُهَا أَو أَشَارَ بِالمُجَلّى إلَى الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ وَبِالمُصَلّى إِلَى الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الآلِ ؛ لِأَنْهَا إِنَّمَا تَكُونُ ضِمنًا وَتَبَعًا

ترجمہ:۔ جب بندے تک پہنچنے والی نعمتوں میں سے بڑی نعمت دین اسلام تھی اور اس سے وصول حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ ہمیشہ کی نعمتوں کی طرف سلامتی کے گھر میں اور یہ نعمت نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے واسطہ سے حاصل ہوئی۔ تو ہوگی عالی صلی اللہ عالیہ وسلم ثناء علی اللہ کے پیچھے ۔ پس مصنف نے ردیف بنادیا صلوۃ کو حمد کے ساتھ ۔ اور نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے نام کو صراحتاً چھوڑنے میں جیسا کہ نسخہ مقروہ (جو مشہور اور پڑھا جارہا ہے ) میں اشارہ کرنا ہے آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کی عظمت شان کی طرف اور تنبیہ ہے اس بات پر کہ آپ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا افضل الرسل ہونا واضح امر ہے۔ کسی پر مخفی نہیں ہے اور حلبہ گھوڑوں کی وہ جماعت جن کو دوڑ کے مقابلہ کے لیے جمع کیا گیا ہو ہر طرف سے۔ پھر مجاز لیا گیا اس کو میدان کے لیے (جس میں گھوڑے دوڑتے ہیں ) مجلی وہ گھوڑا ہے جو مقابلہ کرنے والے گھوڑوں میں سے پہلے نمبر پر آئے ۔ اور مصلی وہ ہے جو اس کے پیچھے ہو اور اس کو مصلی اس لیے کہتے ہیں کہ اس کا سر پہلے گھوڑے کے صلوین یعنی سرینوں کے پاس ہوتا ہے اس کا معنی و مطلب درود کو کثرت سے بھیجنا ہے۔ اور بار بار بھیجنا ہے ۔ یا اشارہ کیا ہے مجلی سے نبی صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم پر درود بھیجنے کی طرف اور مصلی سے آپ کی اولاد پر صلوٰۃ بھیجنے کی طرف اس لیے کہ اولاد پر یہ صلوۃ ضمنا اور تبعا ہے۔

لغوی تحقیق : تَلو بكسر التاء وسکون اللام اس کے دو معنی آتے ہیں۔ نمبر (۱) اونٹنی کا دودھ پینے والا بچہ جو اس کے پیچھے پیچھے چلتا ہو ۔ مونث تلوۃ ہے۔ نمبر (۲) ہر پیچھے آنے والی چیز یہاں یہی دوسرا معنی مراد ہے۔ تنویہ زور سے ذکر کرنا ،تعریف کرنا تعظیم کرنا۔ یہاں آخر معنی مراد ہے۔ اوب راستہ ، جہت و طرف یقال جاءوا من کل أوب ای من کل جہت ۔ حمد کے بعد تصلیہ علی النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کو ذکر کرنے کی وجہ

تشریح قولہ وعلی افضل رسلہ:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے اس عبارت میں شارخ نے ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دیا ہے۔
His statement: 'and upon the most excellent of His messengers, sending blessings' — since the greatest of the blessings reaching the servant is the religion of Islam, and through it one attains the eternal blessings in the abode of peace, and that is through the mediation of the Prophet (peace and blessings upon him), so supplication for him became a follower of praise of Allah Almighty; therefore he appended praise with salutation. And in omitting explicit mention of the Prophet's name (peace be upon him) as in the recited version, there is an exaltation of his station and an indication that his being the most excellent of messengers is a clear matter not hidden from anyone. And 'halabah' (with sukun) is horses gathered for racing from every side; it is metaphorically used for the racecourse. And 'mujalla' is the forerunner among the racehorses, and 'musalla' is the one that follows it, because its head is at its haunches. And the meaning of that is multiplying and repeating the salutation; or he indicated by 'mujalla' the salutation upon the Prophet, and by 'musalla' the salutation upon his family, because that is only included implicitly and as a follower.

Translation: When the greatest blessing reaching the servant was the religion of Islam, and through it one attains the everlasting blessings in the abode of peace, and this blessing was obtained through the mediation of the Prophet (peace and blessings upon him), then it became that blessing of Allah after praise of Allah. So the author made salutation follow praise. And in leaving out the explicit name of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as in the recited version, there is an indication of his great status and a notification that his being the most excellent of messengers is an obvious matter, hidden from no one. And 'halabah' is the group of horses gathered for racing from every side; then it was used metaphorically for the racecourse. 'Mujalla' is the horse that comes first among the racing horses, and 'musalla' is the one that follows it, and it is called 'musalla' because its head is at the haunches of the first horse. Its meaning and purport is to send salutation abundantly and repeatedly; or he indicated by 'mujalla' the sending of salutation upon the Prophet, and by 'musalla' the sending of salutation upon his family, because salutation upon the family is included implicitly and as a follower.

Linguistic research: 'Talu' (with kasra of the taa and sukun of the laam) has two meanings: (1) the young camel that drinks its mother's milk and follows her; feminine is 'tilwah'; (2) anything that follows. Here the second meaning is intended. 'Tanwiyah' means to mention loudly, praise, or exalt; here the last meaning is intended. 'Awb' means path, direction; it is said 'jā'ū min kulli awb' i.e., from every direction. The reason for mentioning salutation upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) after praise.

Explanation of his statement 'and upon the most excellent of his messengers': This is the first part of the commentary's expression; in this expression the commentator answers a presupposed question.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the author's phrase 'wa ʿalā afḍali rusulihi muṣalliyan' (and upon the most excellent of His messengers, sending blessings). The commentator explains the reason for placing salutation upon the Prophet immediately after praise of Allah: the greatest blessing to reach a servant is Islam, which is obtained through the Prophet's mediation, so supplication for him naturally follows praise of Allah. The omission of the Prophet's name by name in the recited version is deliberate, serving to exalt his status and indicate that his being the best of messengers is too obvious to need explicit mention. The commentator then provides a linguistic metaphor: 'halabah' (racehorses gathered from every side) is used metaphorically for the racecourse; 'mujalla' (the forerunner) and 'musalla' (the follower) are explained both as indicating abundant and repeated salutation, or as referring respectively to salutation upon the Prophet and upon his family (the latter being implicitly included). An Urdu translation follows, clarifying the same points. A linguistic investigation (lughawī taḥqīq) defines the words 'talu' (follower) and 'tanwiyah' (exaltation), and explains 'awb' (direction). The passage concludes by noting that this is the first part of the commentary where the commentator answers a presupposed question about the reason for this ordering.

Key Terms
تلو (talu): Anything that follows; here it means supplication for the Prophet follows praise of Allah.
تنويہ (tanwiyah): Loud mention, praise, exaltation; here the meaning of exaltation is intended for the Prophet's status.
حلبہ (halabah): Horses gathered for racing from every side; metaphorically used for the racecourse (majāz).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is salutation upon the Prophet placed immediately after praise of Allah?
A) Because the Prophet is the most excellent of messengers.
B) Because the greatest blessing, Islam, reaches the servant through the Prophet's mediation.
C) Because the author omitted the Prophet's name on purpose.
D) Because salutation upon the Prophet is a form of praise.

Key Takeaway
The ordering of salat after hamd is based on the fact that Islam—the greatest blessing—is attained through the Prophet's mediation, making supplication for him a natural follower of praise.

Tadmin vs Tasamuh: Defending Authorial Precision in Hanafi Usul
Explaining the correction of an imputation of linguistic leniency through the principle of tadmin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of tadmin to resolve an apparent grammatical error in a classical text and evaluate when imputing tasamuh is incorrect.

Core Idea
Tadmin preserves authorial precision by reinterpreting the verb's sense; imputing tasamuh is a defect when tadmin is available.

In Hanafi usul, when a classical author seems to misuse a verb complement, scholars face a choice: attribute it to the author's carelessness (tasamuh) or reinterpret the verb through tadmin (incorporation). This passage shows how a commentator incorrectly chose tasamuh, and how Ibn Jinni's authority on tadmin corrects that imputation. You will learn to apply this reasoning to protect the integrity of transmitted texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Apparent Grammatical Anomaly
Locate the verb and its complement that seem mismatched. Here, 'wufiq' (to be successful) takes a complement implying 'honor'—unusual for its normal usage.
The anomaly is the complement not matching the verb's typical pattern.
2
Understand the Tadmin Solution
Reinterpret the verb as carrying the meaning of another verb (e.g., 'sharaf' meaning 'to honor'), making the complement grammatically correct. This is tadmin.
Tadmin allows a broader sense without changing the text.
3
Evaluate the Commentator's Tasamuh Attribution
The commentator claimed the author was being careless. Consider his reasoning: authors focus on meaning over wording. But is this a sufficient justification?
Tasamuh is considered a defect when imputed without necessity.
4
Apply Ibn Jinni's Principle
Ibn Jinni states that tadmin is extremely widespread in Arabic; almost any apparent error can be explained by it. Therefore, when tadmin is possible, it is preferable to impute tasamuh.
This principle shifts the default assumption from error to correctness.
5
Conclude with the Correct Approach
The commentator's own attribution of tasamuh is itself tasamuh. In Hanafi usul, we prioritize tadmin to uphold the author's precision unless there is clear evidence of error.
The lesson: always exhaust tadmin before attributing error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب (۲):- یہ ہے کہ یہاں تضمین ہوئی ہے کہ وفق کو شرف کے معنی میں کیا اور اس کے اسم فاعل کو اس سے حال بنایا۔ تقدیر عبارت ہوگی۔ وفقنی اللہ مشرفا تالیف ہذا الکتاب خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ با صلہ شرف کا ہے۔ اور اس کا صلہ با آ سکتا ہے۔
قوله والمصنف :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ ایک سوال کا مقدر جواب ہے۔
سوال :۔ جب مائن کی اس کلام کو تضمین پر محمول کیا جا سکتا ہے تو پھر شاریخ نے اس کو تسامح کی طرف منسوب کیوں کیا ؟ جبکہ تسامح ایک قسم کا عیب ہے تو مصنف کی طرف عیب کی نسبت کیوں کی ؟
جواب :۔ مصنفین کی عادت کو دیکھتے ہوئے ان کی طرف تسامح کی نسبت کی ہے۔ مصنفین اکثر اوقات عبارت میں تسامح کرتے رہتے ہیں۔ کہ فعل کے صلات کو غلط ذکر کر دیتے ہیں کیونکہ ان کا (ماتن کا ) صح نظر معانی ہیں ۔ الفاظ نہیں ۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ان تمام جگہوں کو تضمین پر محمول نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔ تو اس لیے شک پیدا ہو گیا کہ یہاں تسامح ہوا ہے۔
فائدہ:۔ لیکن شاریخ کا یہ قول درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ علامہ ابن جنی کہتے ہیں کہ تضمین کا باب عرب میں اتنا وسیع ہے۔ کہ اگر میں ان کو اکٹھا کروں تو کئی کتابیں بن جائیں تو جہاں افعال کے صلات میں بظاہر تسامح نظر آتا ہے۔ ان عبارتوں کو تضمین پر محمول کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ لہذا مصنف کی طرف تسامح کی نسبت کرنے میں خود شاریخ سے تسامح ہوا ہے۔
Answer (2): This is that there is tadmin here, and the word wufiq has been used in the meaning of sharaf, and its active participle has been made hal from it. The presumed phrase would be: 'waffaqanī Allah mushrifan ta’līf hādhā al-kitāb'. The summary is that the complement is for sharaf, and its complement can come with bi. His statement: 'wa al-musannif' - this is the last part of the commentary's phrase. In short, the commentator is an implied answer to a question. Question: When the author's statement can be taken as having tadmin, why did the commentator attribute it to tasamuh? While tasamuh is a type of defect, why attribute a defect to the author? Answer: He attributed tasamuh to the author considering the habit of authors. Authors often practice tasamuh in their wording, i.e., they mention the complements of verbs incorrectly, because their main concern is meanings, not words. The summary is that not all such places can be taken as having tadmin, so doubt arose that here there is tasamuh. Benefit: But the commentator's statement is not correct, because Allamah Ibn Jinni says that the scope of tadmin in Arabic is so vast that if I were to collect it, it would fill several books. So wherever the complements of verbs appear to be tasamuh, these wordings can be considered as having tadmin. Therefore, in attributing tasamuh to the author, the commentator himself has committed tasamuh.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis of a point of linguistic interpretation in the commentary. The commentator (the sarh) had previously criticized the author (the matn) for a supposed error in the complement of a verb, calling it tasamuh (leniency/sloppiness). The passage stages a question-and-answer to defend the author. First, it proposes an alternative reading involving tadmin (incorporation), where the verb is taken in a derived sense to allow the complement. The questioner then asks: if tadmin can be applied, why did the commentator attribute tasamuh? The answer given is that authors sometimes deliberately overlook precise wording for meaning, so it is permissible to suspect tasamuh. However, the passage then provides a benefit (fā’idah) that corrects this: Allamah Ibn Jinni (the famous grammarian) confirmed that tadmin is so extensive in Arabic that almost any apparent complement error can be explained by it. Therefore, the commentator's criticism is itself a form of tasamuh, since he should have applied tadmin instead of imputing fault.

Key Terms
تضمین (tadmin): A linguistic device where a verb is used in a connotation that allows it to take a complement not normally associated with it, effectively incorporating another verb's meaning.
تسامح (tasamuh): Leniency or carelessness in expression, where the author does not strictly adhere to precise grammatical rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage consider the commentator's attribution of tasamuh to the author incorrect?
A) Because the author never makes errors in his writing.
B) Because the apparent error can be explained by the principle of tadmin, which is widely accepted in Arabic.
C) Because the commentator is always lenient.
D) Because the author's focus is on meanings not words.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, always exhaust the possibility of tadmin before imputing tasamuh to an author; preserving the author's precision is the default.

Critique of the Commentator's Interpretation of the Author's Metaphor
Critique of a commentator's metaphorical interpretation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the two textual flaws in the commentator's interpretation of the author's metaphor, applying principles of textual analysis from Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
The author likens the book's completion to breaking a seal, not its presentation; the naming precedes presentation.

In this passage, the super-commentator critiques the commentator's explanation of the author's metaphor 'kashu khatam' (like a sealed object). The commentator had interpreted the metaphor as comparing the book before completion to a sealed object, and after completion, presenting it to students as breaking the seal. The super-commentator identifies two errors: one in the referent of the breaking (completion vs. presentation) and one in the grammatical structure that reverses the causal order of naming and presentation. Understanding this critique sharpens your skills in textual analysis, a core competency in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentator's interpretation
Read the commentator's explanation of the author's metaphor. According to the passage, the commentator says: the author likened his book before completion to a sealed object, and after completion, presenting it to students is likened to breaking the seal.
This is the target of the critique.
2
Analyze the first objection: misidentification of the likened element
The super-commentator points out that the author's words indicate the completion itself (not the presentation) is likened to breaking the seal. Compare the commentator's claim with the author's wording to see the mismatch.
First flaw: the commentator shifted the correspondence.
3
Analyze the second objection: grammatical inversion of cause and effect
Examine the grammatical structure: from 'lammā tayassara itmāmuhu' onward, multiple introductory clauses (mawādd) precede the apodosis (tālī) 'sammaytu hādhā al-kitāb bi al-tawḍīḥ'. The commentator's interpretation would make the presentation (a part of the introductory clauses) the cause for naming, but the naming is already established before presentation. The super-commentator argues that the completion itself can be the cause, not the presentation.
Second flaw: logical order reversed.
4
Evaluate the overall critique
Consider whether the super-commentator's objections are valid based on the text. Apply the principle that in textual analysis, the literal wording and grammatical structure take precedence over speculative interpretation.
The critique strengthens the correct understanding of the author's intent.

Source Text

قولہ وفض :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے۔ اس میں شارع نے لغوی تحقیق بیان کی ہے۔ فض۔ یغض فضا اس کا معنی ہے کا شنایا تو ڑنا وغیرہ۔ اختتام کہتے ہیں کسی شئی کے آخر تک پہنچنا اور ختام کہتے ہیں اس مٹی کو جس سے مہر (لاک ) لگائی جاتی ہے۔ کتاب کی خط مختوم سے تشبیہ
قولہ جعل الكتاب : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ غرض شاریخ متن کی خوبی بیان کرتا ہے ۔ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے اپنی کتاب کو مکمل ہونے سے پہلے چھپی ہوئی چیز کے ساتھ اور اس چیز کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی ہے کہ جس پر مہر لگادی گئی ہو اور اس کے اندر نکات پر کوئی مطلع نہ ہو سکا ہو اور کتاب کے اختتام کے بعد طلبہ پر پیش کرنے کو مہر توڑنے کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی ہے۔ لیکن شاریخ کی یہ تقریر دو وجہ سے درست نہیں۔ نمبر ا۔ ایک تو اس وجہ سے کہ شاریخ کی کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مائن نے کتاب کو طلبہ پر پیش کرنے کو فض ختمام کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی ہے۔ حالانکہ ماتن کی کلام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ نفس اختتام کو فض ختام سے تشبیہ دی۔ وجہ نمبر ۲ ۔ یہ ہے لما تیسر اتمامہ سے لے کر ماتن نے کئی جملوں کا جو عطف ڈالا ہے ۔ یہ سب مقدم ہیں۔ اور

سميت هذا الكتاب بالتوضیح یہ تالی ہے۔ اور جب مقدم متعدد ہوں تو اس کا ہر ہر جزو تالی میں مؤثر ہوتا ہے۔ اب اگر یہ معنی مراد لیا جائے۔ جو شاریخ نے بیان کیا ہے تو اس سے لازم آئے گا۔ کہ اس کتاب کو طلباء پر پیش کرنا سبب ہے اس کا توضیح نام رکھنے کے لیے حالانکہ نفس اختتام کتاب کو تسمیہ بالتوضیح کا سبب بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ اور عرض علی الطلبہ کو سبب نہیں بنایا جاسکتا۔ کیونکہ مشہور و متعارف یہ ہے کہ کتاب کا نام پہلے رکھا جاتا ہے۔ طلبہ پر پیش بعد میں کیا جاتا ہے۔
His statement: 'wa fadd' – this is the first part of the commentary's phrase. In it, the commentator explains a lexical investigation. 'Fadda, yafuddu, faddan' its meaning is to break open, etc. 'Ihtitam' means reaching the end of something, and 'khatam' means the clay with which a seal is affixed. The book is likened to a sealed line. His statement: 'jaala al-kitab' – this is the second part of the commentary's phrase. In short, the commentator describes the excellence of the text. In this phrase, the author likened his book, before its completion, to a sealed object, with nobody able to know its points, and after completion, presenting it to the students is likened to breaking the seal. But the commentator's explanation is incorrect for two reasons. First: The commentator's words indicate that the author likened presenting the book to the students to breaking the seal, whereas the author's words indicate that the completion itself is likened to breaking the seal. Second: Because from 'lammā tayassara itmāmuhu' onward, the author has attached several clauses, all of which are introductory. And the book has been named 'al-Tawdih' – this is the apodosis. When the introductory clauses are multiple, each part of the introduction influences the apodosis. Now if the meaning taken is the one the commentator explained, it would imply that presenting the book to the students is the cause for naming it al-Tawdih, whereas the completion itself can be made the cause, and presenting to the students cannot be made the cause, because it is well known that the name of a book is given first, presentation later.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage continues the analysis of the commentator's remarks. Here, the commentator explains the lexical meaning of 'fadd' (to break open) and 'khatam' (seal). He then interprets the author's metaphor in the line 'jaala al-kitab…' as meaning the book before completion is like a sealed object, and after completion, presenting it to students is like breaking the seal. The passage objects to this interpretation on two grounds. First, the author's wording indicates that the completion itself (not the presentation) corresponds to breaking the seal. Second, the grammatical structure shows that the naming of the book 'al-Tawdih' is the apodosis of several introductory clauses; the presentation to students is among the introductory clauses and cannot be the cause of the naming, whereas the completion can be. The known practice is that books are named before being presented, so the commentator's reading reverses the logical order.

Key Terms
تشبیہ (tashbih): A rhetorical device likening one thing to another; here used to explain the author's metaphorical language about the book as a sealed object.
فض (fadd): To break open, specifically the breaking of a seal.
ختام (khatam): Seal, the clay or instrument used to seal a document.
مقدم (muqaddam): Introductory clause or premise; in grammar, something placed before the main clause.
تالی (tālī): Apodosis; the main clause that depends on the introductory clauses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second objection to the commentator's explanation?
A) The commentator ignored the lexical meaning of 'khatam'.
B) The commentator's interpretation reverses the causal order of naming and presentation.
C) The commentator misidentified the author's purpose.
D) The commentator added clauses not present in the original.

Key Takeaway
The correct textual analysis of the author's metaphor shows that completion, not presentation, is likened to breaking the seal, and that grammatical structure confirms the logical priority of naming over presentation.
