Defending Preposition Usage through Tadmin and the Correct Use of 'Sawab'
Defending the author's use of 'ala' with 'sabaqa' against the commentator's claim of error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the concept of tadmin (implication) to justify the use of 'ala' with 'sabaqa', and identify the correct usage of the term 'sawab' in legal debates.

Core Idea
Tadmin can change the required preposition; 'sawab' is only used when no justification exists for the opposing view.

This lesson examines a grammatical objection raised by a commentator against an author's use of the preposition 'ala' with the verb 'sabaqa'. The passage refutes the objection by invoking the linguistic principle of tadmin (implication), showing that 'sabaqa' here incorporates the meaning of verbs that naturally take 'ala'. Additionally, it highlights a methodological point: the term 'sawab' (the correct) should only be applied when the opposing view has no valid justification, which is not the case here.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
What does the commentator claim about the author's use of 'ala' with 'sabaqa'? Note the commentator's basis (the poet's usage).
The commentator asserts that 'sabaqa' should take 'ila', not 'ala'.
2
Understand the Concept of Tadmin
How does the defender justify the use of 'ala'? By arguing that 'sabaqa' here implies the meanings of 'ghalaba' (overcome), 'waqafa' (stand over), or 'ittala'a' (ascend), all of which take 'ala'.
Tadmin allows a verb to carry the force of another verb, influencing its prepositional requirements.
3
Analyze the Methodological Point about 'Sawab'
Why does the passage reject the commentator's use of the term 'sawab' (the correct)? Because 'sawab' is used in opposition to 'ghalat' (error) and implies that the other side has no justification. Since tadmin provides a justification, the commentator's claim of 'sawab' is itself inappropriate.
The passage emphasizes that 'sawab' should be reserved for cases where the opposing position is indefensible.
4
Apply the Principle to Other Cases
Consider another verb like 'raghiba' (to desire). If a text uses 'raghiba ala', can tadmin justify it? Yes, if 'raghiba' implies 'arada' or 'ghalaba', both taking 'ala'.
This shows how tadmin can be used to explain seemingly irregular preposition usage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ والصواب:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا آخری حصہ ہے۔ اس میں شاریخ نے ماتن پر اعتراض کیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ سبقت کا صلہ علی نہیں آتا بلکہ ائی آتا ہے جیسا کہ شاعر نے کہا ہے ” سبقت العالمین الی المعالی کہ میں سبقت لے گیا جہاں والوں سے بلندیوں کی طرف تو شاعر نے سبقت کا صلہ الی ذکر کیا ہے۔ نہ کہ علی لیکن مصنف نے صا علی ذکر کیا ہے۔ تو یہ خلاف ضابطہ ہے۔
جواب اول: شاریخ کا والصواب کہنا درست نہیں۔ کیونکہ صواب غلط کے مقابلے میں بولا جاتا ہے۔ تو اس کا اطلاق وہاں ہوتا ہے جہاں ۔ جانب مخالف کی کوئی توجیہ نہ ہو سکے۔ اور یہاں تو جیہ ہو سکتی ہے کہ یہاں تضمین ہوئی کہ یہ غلب یا وقف یا اطلع کو متضمن ہو۔ اور ان سب کا صلہ علی آ سکتا ہے۔
His statement: 'wa al-sawab' – this is the last part of the commentary's phrase. In it, the commentator objects to the author. The summary is that the complement of 'sabaqa' does not come with 'ala', but rather with 'ila', as the poet said: 'sabaqtu al-alameena ila al-ma'ali' – 'I preceded (all) people toward high glories.' So the poet mentioned 'ila' as complement, not 'ala'. But the author mentioned 'ala', which is against the rule. First answer: The commentator's saying 'wa al-sawab' is not correct, because 'sawab' is used in opposition to 'ghalat', and it is applied where the opposite side has no justification. Here there is a justification: that there is tadmin, implying that the verb incorporates the meaning of 'ghalaba' or 'waqafa' or 'ittala'a', and all of these take 'ala' as complement.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage presents a specific objection by the commentator regarding the preposition used with the verb 'sabaqa' (to precede). The commentator claims that the correct preposition is 'ila' (to) not 'ala' (over/upon), and that the author's use of 'ala' is an error. The passage refutes this by invoking tadmin: the verb 'sabaqa' here incorporates the meaning of other verbs like 'ghalaba' (to overcome), 'waqafa' (to stand over), or 'ittala'a' (to ascend), all of which take 'ala'. Therefore, the author's usage is correct and the commentator's claim of error is itself unfounded. The passage also notes a methodological point: the term 'sawab' (the correct) should only be used when the opposing view has no valid justification; here, tadmin provides justification, so 'sawab' is inappropriate.

Key Terms
صواب (sawab): The correct position; used in opposition to error (ghalat). The passage restricts its use to when no possible justification exists for the other view.
تضمين (tadmin): Implication; a linguistic device where a verb carries the meaning of another verb, affecting its grammatical properties such as preposition requirements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage reject the commentator's claim that the author's use of 'ala' with 'sabaqa' is a mistake?
A) Because 'sabaqa' always takes 'ala' in Arabic.
B) Because the author is infallible.
C) Because 'sabaqa' here incorporates other verbs that take 'ala' through tadmin.
D) Because the commentator misquoted the poet.

Key Takeaway
Tadmin is a powerful tool in Arabic grammatical analysis; the term 'sawab' should be reserved for cases where the opposing view has no justification.

Three Meanings of Mubani and Furu' in Usul al-Fiqh
Defining the terms مشارع, مبانی, and فروع with three interpretations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three possible meanings of mubani and furu' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, and identify which interpretation is being used in a given passage.

Core Idea
Mubani and furu' have three distinct meanings — original masail, universal proofs, or matn texts — and context determines which is intended.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks the opening phrase of the matn by clarifying the terms mubani (foundations) and furu' (branches). These terms appear frequently in usul al-fiqh, but they are not monolithic. The commentator presents three valid interpretations, each placing the terms in a different relationship: foundational issues vs. their rulings, universal proofs vs. particular rulings, and core texts vs. commentaries. Understanding these layers is essential for reading usul works correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terms being defined
Locate the terms mubani and furu' in the passage. The commentator explicitly lists three probabilities for each.
2
Extract the three interpretations
List each of the three meanings for mubani and the corresponding meaning for furu'. The passage numbers them 1, 2, and 3.
3
Understand the relationship in each interpretation
For each interpretation, note how mubani and furu' relate: In #1, furu' are definitions and rulings attached to the original masail. In #2, mubani are universal proofs that yield particular rulings. In #3, mubani are the matn texts and furu' are their commentaries.
4
Recognize context signals
When reading other usul passages, examine whether the discussion focuses on foundational issues (meaning #1), proofs (meaning #2), or textual exposition (meaning #3). Signal words like 'adillah' or 'kulliyyah' point to #2; 'shuruh' or 'hawashi' point to #3.
5
Apply to a sample sentence
Given a sentence like 'The mubani of usul are the sources of law,' determine which meaning fits. Here, 'sources' suggests universal proofs (meaning #2).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشارع الشرع:۔ اس میں شرع کو پانی سے تشبیہ دی۔ اور طلباء کے ذہنوں کو شریعت کے تالابوں پر وارد ہونے والے پیاسوں کے ساتھ تشبیہ دی۔ علی ان جعل اصول الشرعیہ اول شرعیت سے مراد اصول فقہ ہیں۔ محمدۃ تمہید سے ہے۔ اس کا معنیٰ ہے سیدھا کرنا ۔ مبانی میں کل تین احتمال ہیں۔ اس سے مراد اصول فقہ کے اصل مسائل ہیں ۔ اور فروع سے مراد وہ تعریفات اور احکام ہیں جو اصل مسائل کے ساتھ متعلق ہیں۔ نمبر ۲۔ مبانی سے مراد دلائل کلیہ اور فروع سے مراد احکام جزئیہ۔ نمبر ۳۔ مبانی سے مراد اس فن میں لکھے جانے والے متون ہیں اور فروع سے مراد شروح و حواشی ہیں۔
Mashari' al-Shar': In it, the Shari'ah is likened to water. And the minds of students are likened to thirsty ones arriving at the ponds of the Shari'ah. 'Ala an ja'ala usul al-shar'iyyah: The first 'shar'iyyah' refers to usul al-fiqh. Muhammadah: from tamhid, meaning to straighten. Mubani: there are three probabilities. First: it refers to the original masail of usul al-fiqh, and furu' refers to the definitions and rulings related to the original masail. Number 2: Mubani refers to universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah) and furu' refers to particular rulings (ahkam juz'iyyah). Number 3: Mubani refers to the matn (texts) written in this discipline, and furu' refers to the commentaries (shuruh) and glosses (hawashi).
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a lexical and technical explanation of the opening phrase of the matn. The commentator likens the Shari'ah to water and scholars to the thirsty. He then clarifies that 'usul al-shar'iyyah' refers to usul al-fiqh. The word 'Muhammadah' is derived from 'tamhid' meaning to straighten. The core of the discussion is the three possible meanings of 'mubani' (foundations) and 'furu'' (branches). The first meaning interprets mubani as the fundamental issues of usul and furu' as the associated definitions and rulings. The second meaning interprets mubani as universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah) and furu' as particular rulings. The third meaning interprets mubani as the written texts (mutun) of the discipline and furu' as the commentaries and glosses. This shows the multi-layered nature of usul al-fiqh discourse.

Key Terms
مشارع الشرع (Mashari' al-Shar'): Refers to the watering places of the Shari'ah, a metaphor for the sources of Islamic law.
مبانی (Mubani): Foundations; can mean the original masail, universal proofs, or the matn texts of usul al-fiqh.
فروع (Furu'): Branches; can mean rulings related to the foundations, particular rulings, or commentaries on the matn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the three meanings of 'mubani'?
A) The original masail of usul al-fiqh
B) The universal proofs (adillah kulliyyah)
C) The matn texts of the discipline
D) The biographical dictionaries (tabaqat)

Key Takeaway
Mubani and furu' have three valid meanings; the correct interpretation depends on the context of the usul discussion.

The Word Su'ud: Literal and Figurative Meaning
Defining 'su'ud' and answering an objection about Allah's direction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between literal and figurative meanings of su'ud and apply the Hanafi usul principle of majaz to avoid theological impossibility.

Core Idea
Su'ud means literal ascent, but for Allah it is figurative (majaz) meaning acceptance — avoiding attributing direction to Allah.

This passage explains the lexical meaning of su'ud and addresses a critical theological objection. If good deeds literally 'ascend' to Allah, that would imply He is located in a place. The commentator resolves this by invoking figurative usage (majaz), a cornerstone of Hanafi usul that safeguards tawhid. You will learn how to identify when a word must be taken figuratively and why.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term and its lexical meaning
The passage defines su'ud as moving from a lower to a higher place. Recognize this as the literal (haqiqi) meaning.
This is the starting point for understanding the issue.
2
Recognize the theological problem
If su'ud is taken literally when applied to good words 'ascending' to Allah, it would imply Allah is in a direction or place, which contradicts Islamic creed.
Allah is not confined to space.
3
Understand the necessity of figurative interpretation (majaz)
The commentator states that here su'ud is used figuratively in the sense of tawajjuh (turning towards). This preserves the scriptural expression while avoiding tashbih.
This is a key principle in Hanafi usul to reconcile texts with 'aqidah.
4
Apply the principle to the specific case
In Quran 35:10, 'ilayhi yas'adu al-kalimu al-tayyibu', the verb yas'adu is interpreted figuratively, meaning good words are accepted by Allah, not that they physically ascend.
This safeguards tawhid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قولہ والصعود:۔ یہ عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ اور غرض شارخ صعود کا لغوی معنی بیان کرتا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ صعود کہتے ہیں نیچے سے اوپر کے مکان کی طرف چڑھنا، حرکت کرنا۔ قولہ استعغیر :۔ یہ عبارت کا پانچواں حصہ ہے اور غرض شاریخ سوال مقدر کا جواب دیتا ہے۔ سوال: صعود کہتے ہیں نیچے سے اوپر کے مکان کی طرف حرکت کرنے کو تو اس سے لازم آئے گا کہ کلمات طیبہ اللہ کے مکان اور جہت کے طرف حرکت کرتے ہیں اور یہ ستلزم ہے اللہ تعالیٰ کے متمکن فی المکان ہونے کو جو کہ باطل ہے۔ جواب:۔ یہاں صعود اپنے حقیقی معنی میں مستعمل نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ مجاز اتوجہ کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے یعنی الکلم الطیب اللہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوتے ہیں۔
His saying 'wa al-su'ud': This is the fourth part of the text. The commentator intends to explain the lexical meaning of su'ud, which is: su'ud means climbing, moving from a lower place to a higher place. His saying 'ista'ira' (?) : This is the fifth part of the text, and the commentator intends to answer an implied question. Question: Su'ud means moving from a lower to a higher place, and this would necessitate that good words move towards Allah's place and direction, which would entail that Allah is located in a place, which is false. Answer: Here su'ud is not used in its real meaning, but figuratively in the sense of 'turning towards' (tawajjuh), i.e., good words turn towards Allah.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage defines the word 'su'ud' and addresses a theological objection. The lexical meaning of su'ud is ascending physically. An implied question arises: If we say good deeds 'ascend' to Allah, that would imply Allah is in a specific direction or place, which is incompatible with Islamic creed (Allah is not confined to space). The commentator answers by stating that here su'ud is used figuratively (majaz) to mean 'turning towards' (tawajjuh). This figurative usage is common; for example, in the Quranic verse 'ilayhi yas'adu al-kalimu al-tayyibu' (to Him ascends good speech) is understood metaphorically. In Hanafi usul, such figurative interpretations are necessary to avoid anthropomorphism (tashbih) while preserving the scriptural expression.

Key Terms
مجاز (majāz): Figurative or metaphorical usage of a word, as opposed to its literal meaning (haqiqah).
توجہ (tawajjuh): Turning towards, directing attention; used as the figurative meaning of su'ud in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the literal meaning of su'ud not applicable when talking about good words ascending to Allah?
A) Because it would imply Allah is in a place
B) Because good words are not physical objects
C) Because the Quran does not use the word su'ud
D) Because the commentator disliked it

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when the literal meaning leads to impossibility (muhal), a word must be interpreted figuratively (majaz) with a contextual clue (qarinah).

8 min
Simile of Rulings and Pillars of Universal Proofs
Explains the simile (tashbih) and answers a key objection about the term 'arkan'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two interpretations of 'rukn' in Hanafi usul and explain how universal proofs can be considered pillars for rulings.

Core Idea
Rulings are like a fortress; their pillars can be external sources of strength or internal derived proofs.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih explains why the matn author likened Sharia rulings to a fortress and called the four universal proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas) its 'pillars'. A natural question arises: if pillars are integral parts, how can external proofs be pillars? The commentator provides two elegant answers that deepen our understanding of the relationship between universal sources and particular rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the simile and its basis
The commentator states that rulings are likened to a fortress (mahall). Understand the point of comparison: just as a fortress protects from physical enemies, rulings protect from Satan and Hellfire.
Note the use of 'tashbih' as a pedagogical tool.
2
Recognize the terminological problem
The matn says rulings are 'based on four pillars' (arkan), but the universal proofs are external to the rulings themselves. This seems contradictory if 'rukn' means integral part.
The commentator anticipates this objection.
3
Analyze the first answer: external support
The commentator cites Quranic usage: 'fatawalla biruknihi' (he turned away with his pillar). Here 'rukn' means external source of strength, not an internal part. So universal proofs can be called pillars as they strengthen rulings.
This answer relies on linguistic flexibility (majaz).
4
Analyze the second answer: internal reinterpretation
If 'rukn' must be internal, then 'universal proofs' refer to the summary universal proofs (dalail kulliyah ijmaaliyyah) and 'rulings' refer to the particular detailed proofs (dalail juz'iyyah tafseeliyyah) that derive from them. The particular proofs are internal branches of the universal proofs.
This answer redefines the terms to make universal proofs the foundational internal pillars.
5
Note the grammatical composition
The commentator clarifies the structure of the simile: 'the likened-to is added to the likening', e.g., 'jinin al-ma' i.e., 'ma' is the likened-to and 'lin' is the likening. This confirms the analogy between rulings and a fortress.
This final part shows the care in rhetorical construction.

تشبيہ الاحكام ۔ يہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے۔ اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے متن کی خوبی بیان کی ہے۔ جس کا حاصل يہ ہے کہ ماتن نے بنی علی اربعہ ارکان قصر الاحكام میں احكام شرعيہ کو تشبیہ دی ہے محل کے ساتھ۔
وجہ تشبیہ :۔ کہ جس طرح محل میں آدمی دشمنوں سے محفوظ ہوتا ہے۔ اور پریشانی سے محفوظ ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح شرعیت کے احکام پر عمل کرنے سے شیطان کی دشمنی و پھسلانے سے اور جہنم کے عذاب سے محفوظ ہو جاتا ہے۔۔
سوال :۔ مئی کے ارکان شئی میں داخل ہوتے ہیں۔ تو ماتن نے دلائل کلیہ کو احکام کے لیے ارکان کیسے بنا دیا۔ حالانکہ دلائل کلیہ احکام سے خارج ہیں۔
جواب (۱):۔ رکن بھی کبھی کبھی شئی کے اس خارج پر بھی بولا جاتا ہے جس سے قوت حاصل کی جائے جیسے اللہ کا ارشاد ہے فتولی بر کنہ اب يہاں رکن شئی میں داخل نہیں ہے۔ تو يہاں بھی ارکان سے مراد وہ اشیاء لیں گے جو شیء سے خارج ہوں البتہ وہ اس کے لئے مقوی ہوں۔ لہذا دلائل کلیہ کو احکام کے لیے ارکان بنا سکتے ہیں ۔
جواب (۲):۔ ارکان سے یہی مراد ہے کہ جو شی میں داخل ہو لیکن ارکان سے مراد دلائل کلیہ اجمالیہ ہوں گے اور احکام سے مراد دلائل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ ہوں گے جو دلائل کلیہ اجمالیہ پر متفرع ہیں۔ اور دلائل جزئیہ دلائل کلیہ کی طرف مراجع ہیں لہذا دلائل کلیہ کو احکام کے لیے ارکان بنانا درست ہے۔
قوله فاضاف المشبہ بہ : یہ عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے۔ اس میں ترکیبی تحقیق کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ کہ احکام میں مشتبہ بہ کی اضافت نشتہ کی طرف ہے۔ جیسے جین الماء میں لین مشبہ بہ ہے۔ اور مآ ومشبہ ہے۔ اصل میں تھا۔ الماء لچھیں ۔ قولہ والا حکام:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا چوتھا حصہ ہے غرض شاریخ ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب دینا ہے۔ احکام شرعیہ کی بنیا دادلہ اربعہ پر ہے
سوال: یہ ہے کہ توضیح کی عبارت سے یہ بات معلوم ہوتی ہے کہ احکام شرعیہ کے محل کی بنیا د ادلہ کلیہ پر ہے۔ اور ادلہ کلیہ چار ہیں حالانکہ احکام شرعیہ کی بناء دلائل جزئیہ پر ہے جیسے نماز کا قائم کرنا حکم شرعی ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل اقیمو الصلوٰۃ ہے اور
Simile of rulings: This is the second part of the commentary's phrase. In this passage, the commentator expresses the excellence of the matn. Its summary is that the matn author, in 'based on four pillars', likened the Sharia rulings to a fortress (mahall) in 'qasr al-ahkam'. The reason for the simile: Just as in a fortress a man is safe from enemies and safe from distress, similarly, by acting upon the rulings of Sharia, one becomes safe from the enmity of Satan and his misguidance and from the punishment of Hellfire. Question: The 'pillars' are part of the thing. So how did the matn author make the universal proofs (dalail kulliyah) into pillars for the rulings, while the universal proofs are external to the rulings? Answer (1): Sometimes 'pillar' is also used for an external thing from which strength is derived, as God said: 'He turned away with his pillar' (fatawalla biruknihi). Here the pillar is not internal to the thing. So here too, by 'pillars' we take those things that are external to the thing but are strengthening for it. Therefore, we can make universal proofs as pillars for the rulings. Answer (2): By 'pillars' is meant what is internal to the thing, but by 'pillars' are meant the universal summary proofs, and by 'rulings' are meant the particular detailed proofs that branch off from those universal summary proofs, and the particular proofs refer back to the universal proofs. So it is correct to make universal proofs as pillars for the rulings. His statement 'so he added the likened to' (qalahu fadif al-mushabbah bihi): This is the third part of the commentary. It indicates a compositional analysis: in the rulings, the likened-to is added to the likening, like 'jinin al-ma' where 'lin' is the likened-to and 'ma' is the likening; originally it was 'al-ma' lihin'. His statement 'and the rulers' (wa al-ahkam) is the fourth part of the commentary; the commentator intends to answer an implied question: the basis of Sharia rulings is on the four proofs. The question is this: from the wording of Al-Tawdih, it is understood that the basis of the locus of Sharia rulings is on universal proofs, and the universal proofs are four, while the rulings of Sharia are based on particular proofs, like establishing prayer is a Sharia ruling and its proof is 'establish prayer' (aqimu al-salah).
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the simile (tashbih) in the matn. The commentator explains that the matn author likened the Sharia rulings to a fortress (mahall) because just as a fortress protects from enemies and distress, acting on Sharia rulings protects from Satan, misguidance, and Hellfire. Then a question arises: if pillars (arkan) are integral parts of a thing, how can universal proofs (dalail kulliyah) be called pillars for rulings when they are external? Two answers are given. First, the word 'rukn' can be used for an external source of strength, as in the Quranic verse 'fatawalla biruknihi' (he turned away with his pillar). Second, if 'rukn' is taken as internal, then 'universal proofs' refer to the summary universal proofs (dalail kulliyah ijmaaliyyah) and 'rulings' refer to the particular detailed proofs (dalail juz'iyyah tafseeliyyah) that derive from them. Thus, the universal proofs can be seen as internal pillars. The passage then notes additional parts of the commentary: 'so he added the likened to' points out the grammatical construction of the simile, and 'and the rulers' addresses an implied question about the basis of rulings on four proofs, though the text is cut off.

Key Terms
تشبيہ (tashbih): A simile likening rulings to a fortress in terms of protective function.
ارکان (arkan): Pillars; here used metaphorically for either external strengthening sources or internal foundational elements.
دلائل کلیہ (dalail kulliyah): Universal proofs, i.e., the four sources: Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas (in their general sense).
رکن (rukn): Pillar; can mean either an integral part or an external source of strength, as shown by Quranic usage.
دلائل جزئیہ تفصیلیہ (dalail juz'iyyah tafseeliyyah): Particular detailed proofs, i.e., specific textual evidences for individual rulings (e.g., 'aqimu al-salah' for prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first answer given in the passage for why universal proofs (dalail kulliyah) can be called pillars (arkan) of rulings?
A) They are internal parts of the rulings.
B) The word 'rukn' can be used for an external thing that provides strength, as in the Quranic verse.
C) Universal proofs are the same as particular proofs.
D) The matn author made a linguistic error.

Key Takeaway
The term 'rukn' in Hanafi usul can be understood either as an external strengthener or an internal source, resolving the apparent contradiction in calling universal proofs pillars of rulings.

Definition of Laqab and Its Application to Usul al-Fiqh
Defines laqab and classifies usul al-fiqh as a laqab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define laqab, distinguish it from kunya and ism, and explain why usul al-fiqh qualifies as a laqab.

Core Idea
A laqab indicates praise or blame by its original meaning, unlike kunya or ism.

In this passage, the commentator of Al-Tahrir clarifies a key terminological distinction in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the difference between a laqab (title), kunya (teknonym), and ism (proper name). Understanding this distinction is essential for reading classical texts, where titles carry specific connotations. We will then see why the phrase 'usul al-fiqh' itself is a laqab, praising the discipline as the foundation of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of names
Recognize that the passage distinguishes three categories: kunya, ism, and laqab, based on their prefixes and whether they indicate praise or blame.
2
Define kunya and ism
Kunya starts with 'ab' or 'umm' and does not indicate praise/blame. Ism does not start with 'ab' or 'ibn' and also does not indicate praise/blame.
3
Define laqab
Laqab does not start with 'ab' or 'ibn' but does indicate praise or blame by its original meaning.
This is the key distinguishing feature.
4
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Usul al-fiqh does not start with 'ab' or 'ibn', and it indicates praise because it is the foundation for fiqh, which brings worldly order and salvation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والملقب علم يشعر : یہ شرح کی عبارت کا بارہواں حصہ ہے۔ یہاں سے شارخ تعریف لقمی کی مناسبت سے لقب کی :۔ تعریف کر رہے ہیں۔
تمہید :۔ ہر وہ لفظ جو اب یا این کے ساتھ شروع کیا جائے اور مدح اور ذم پر اپنے اصل مفہوم کے اعتبار سے دلالت نہ کرے۔ اس کو کنیت کہتے ہیں۔ اور وہ لفظ جواب اور ابن کے ساتھ شروع نہ کیا جائے ۔ اور نہ ہی مدح و ذم پر دلالت کرے۔ تو اس کو علم کہتے ہیں ۔ اور وہ لفظ جو ابن اور اب سے شروع نہ ہو لیکن اصل کے اعتبار سے مدح یا زم پر دلالت کرے تو اسکو لقب کہتے ہیں اور یہاں اصول الفقہ لقب ہے اس فن کے لئے ، اس لئے کہ یہ لفظ ابن اور اب سے شروع نہیں کیا گیا ۔ اور مدح پر بھی دلالت کرتا ہے باقی رہی یہ بات کہ مدح پر کس طرح دلالت کر رہا ہے تو اسکی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اصول فقہ اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کر رہا ہے کہ یہ فقہ کیلئے بنی اور بنیاد ہے اور فقہ سے نظام معاش چلتا ہے نیز فقہ ہی آخرت میں نجات کا ذریعہ ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ یہ مدرج ہے۔ أَمَّا تَعْرِيفُهَا بِاعْتِبَارِ الْإِضَافَةِ فَيَحْتَاجُ إلَى تَعْرِيفِ الْمُضَافِ، وَهُوَ الْأَصُولُ وَالْمُصَافِ إِلَيْهِ، وَهُوَ الْفِقْهُ
And the titled thing, knowledge indicates: This is the twelfth part of the commentary's text. From here, the commentator defines the title (laqab) in relation to the titular definition. Introduction: Every word that is started with 'ab' or 'umm' and does not indicate praise or blame by its original meaning is called 'kunya'. And a word that does not start with 'ab' or 'ibn' and does not indicate praise or blame is called 'ism' (proper name). And a word that does not start with 'ibn' or 'ab' but indicates praise or blame by its original meaning is called 'laqab'. And here, usul al-fiqh is a laqab for this discipline, because this word does not start with 'ibn' or 'ab', and it indicates praise. As for how it indicates praise, the reason is that usul al-fiqh indicates that it is the foundation and basis for fiqh, and through fiqh the system of livelihood runs, and fiqh is also the means of salvation in the Hereafter, and it is clear that this is praiseworthy. As for its definition by way of addition, it requires defining the first part, which is al-usul, and the second part, which is al-fiqh.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage provides a technical definition of 'laqab' (title) within the context of defining usul al-fiqh. It distinguishes three types of names: kunya (begins with ab/umm, does not indicate praise/blame by original meaning), ism (proper name, does not begin with ab/ibn, no praise/blame), and laqab (does not begin with ab/ibn, indicates praise or blame by original meaning). Usul al-fiqh is a laqab because it does not start with ab or ibn and indicates praise: it points to the fact that it is the foundation for fiqh, which is praiseworthy for its role in worldly order and salvation. The passage also introduces the additive definition of usul al-fiqh, which requires defining its components: usul (principles) and fiqh (jurisprudence). This is a standard usul al-fiqh definition of the term 'laqab' as applied to the discipline.

Key Terms
لقب (laqab): A word that does not start with 'ab' or 'ibn' and indicates praise or blame by its original meaning.
کنیت (kunya): A word starting with 'ab' or 'umm' that does not indicate praise or blame by its original meaning.
علم (ism): A proper name that does not start with 'ab' or 'ibn' and does not indicate praise or blame.

Key Takeaway

Resolving the Division of Acts: Ma'na Masdari and Haasil Masdar
Answering an objection about dividing fi'l into itself and something else.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ma'na masdari and haasil masdar and apply this distinction to resolve logical objections in fiqh terminology.

Core Idea
A masdar has two realities: conceptual meaning and external state; this distinction saves the division of acts from self-division confusion.

In usul al-fiqh, precise terminology is essential to avoid logical contradictions. Here, the commentator answers an objection against dividing acts (fi'l) into categories. The objection claimed such a division would divide a thing into itself and another. The commentator resolves this by unpacking two aspects of a masdar (verbal noun): its conceptual meaning and its externally realized form. Understanding this distinction will sharpen your ability to analyze fiqh definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Understand the logical problem: dividing fi'l into categories seems to divide a thing into itself and something else, which is impossible.
The objector thinks 'fi'l' is used univocally.
2
Understand the two aspects of masdar
Learn that any masdar has ma'na masdari (the pure concept) and haasil masdar (the external state when the concept is realized).
E.g., salat: ma'na masdari = 'praying', haasil masdar = the physical and spiritual state of the praying person.
3
Examine the example of salat
Apply the distinction to a concrete fiqh term: salat is a masdar with both aspects.
The difference is that ma'na masdari has no external existence, while haasil masdar does.
4
Apply to muqsam and qism
Take the muqsam (thing being divided) as haasil masdar (external act), and the qism (divisions) as ma'na masdari (concepts). Then there is no self-division.
The external act (haasil masdar) is divided by its conceptual aspects (ma'na masdari).
5
Recognize the broader principle
Valid classification requires distinguishing between existential and conceptual levels. This principle is used in Hanafi usul to avoid logical pitfalls.
This shows the importance of precise terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب: مصدر میں دو چیزیں ہوتی ہیں (۱) معنی مصدری جو واضح ہے (۲) حاصل مصدر جس سے مراد وہ ہیئت ہے جو فاعل کو معنی مصدری کو واقع کرتے وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے جیسے صلوۃ ، مصدر ہے اس کا معنی مصدری تو نماز پڑھنا ہے لیکن اس کا حاصل مصدر وہ کیفیت ہے جو مصلی کو نماز پڑھتے وقت حاصل ہوتی ہے اور دوسری بات یہ ہے کہ معنی مصدری خارج میں نہیں پایا جاتا لیکن حاصل مصدر خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے، اب جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم نے فعل جو مقسم کے درجہ میں ہے اس سے حاصل مصدر مرا دلیا ہے جو خارج میں پایا جاتا ہے لہر دوسری خرابی لازم نہیں آئے گی اسی طرح جب فعل مقسم سے مراد حاصل مصدر ہے اور وہ فعل جواس کی قسم بنتا ہے اس سے مراد معنی مصدری ہے تو پہلی خرابی یعنی انقسام الشی الی نفسہ والی غیرہ بھی لازم نہیں آئے گی۔
Answer: In masdar there are two things: (1) the masdari meaning which is clear, (2) haasil al-masdar by which is intended the form that is obtained for the doer when he performs the masdari meaning. For example, salat is a masdar; its masdari meaning is to pray, but its haasil masdar is the state that the one praying obtains while praying. The second thing is that the masdari meaning is not found externally, but haasil masdar is found externally. Now the gist of the answer is that we intended by fi'l, which is in the position of the thing being divided (muqsam), the haasil masdar, which is found externally, therefore the second problem will not arise. Similarly, when by the fi'l that forms its division (qism) we intend the masdari meaning, then the first problem, i.e., the division of a thing into itself and something else, will also not arise.
Source pages p. 222

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an objection against dividing acts (fi'l) into categories. The objection was that dividing fi'l into itself and something else is invalid. The commentator resolves this by distinguishing between two aspects of a masdar (verbal noun): the masdari meaning (ma'na masdari) and the haasil masdar (the resultant state). For example, salat (prayer) as a masdar means 'to pray', but its haasil masdar is the specific form and state that the praying person attains. The key point is that the masdari meaning is not found externally (i.e., in the real world) while the haasil masdar is externally found. So when the muqsam (the thing being divided) is taken as the haasil masdar, the division is valid because it refers to the external act, and when the qism (the divisions) are taken as the masdari meaning (the concept), there is no overlap. Thus the logical problem is avoided. This is a fine example of Hanafi usul al-Fiqh resolving semantic complications.

Key Terms
مصدر (masdar): A verbal noun that has two aspects: its base meaning (ma'na masdari) and the resultant form (haasil al-masdar).
حاصل مصدر (haasil al-masdar): The form or state that is obtained when the masdari meaning is realized, e.g., the state of praying is the haasil masdar of salat.
معنی مصدری (ma'na masdari): The basic meaning of the masdar, e.g., 'the act of praying' is the ma'na masdari of salat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of distinguishing between ma'na masdari and haasil masdar in this passage?
A) To explain that prayer has two meanings.
B) To resolve the problem of dividing fi'l into itself and something else.
C) To show that haasil masdar is not real.
D) To argue that salat is not a valid masdar.

Key Takeaway
The haasil masdar / ma'na masdari distinction allows classification of acts without logical contradiction.

Understanding Takhsis in the Definition of Fiqh: Personal vs Type Specification
Objection and response on specificity of fiqh definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between takhsis shakhsi and takhsis naw'i, and apply this distinction to evaluate definitions of fiqh.

Core Idea
Fiqh is a dynamic type, not a fixed list—its instances expand while its category stays distinct.

This passage from Al-Tarweeh addresses a critique of the definition of fiqh by Sadr al-Shariah. The objector claims that fiqh, as understood by the people, is a fixed, specific set of rulings, but the author's definition makes it a general concept that can increase or decrease. The response clarifies that 'specification' can mean either personal specification (takhsis shakhsi) which is rejected, or type specification (takhsis naw'i) which is accepted. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how the Hanafi school views fiqh as a living discipline that grows through ijtihad while remaining a coherent branch of knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the objector's claim: fiqh is a specific, determinate science (makhsus) and cannot change. What is the basis of this claim?
The objector relies on common usage (qawm).
2
Distinguish Two Types of Takhsis
The response introduces two meanings of 'specification': personal (takhsis shakhsi) and type (takhsis naw'i). Explain each in your own words.
Personal specification fixes the individual issues; type specification fixes the category but allows variation in instances.
3
Apply the Distinction to the Objection
Which meaning did the objector intend? Show that if personal specification was meant, it is false; if type specification was meant, it is true and consistent with the author's definition.
The objector likely conflated the two.
4
Extract the Hanafi Position
State the accepted view: fiqh is a type (naw') of knowledge that remains distinct even as its individual rulings increase or decrease through ijtihad.
This aligns with the dynamic nature of fiqh.

خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ قوم کے نزدیک فقہ مخصوص علم کا نام ہے۔ اور مصنف کی تعریف کے مطابق یہ ایک مفہوم کلی ہے جو کم زیادہ ہوتارہتا ہے۔ جواب :۔ یہ ہے کہ آپ نے کہا کہ قوم کے نزدیک مخصوص و معین علم و مسائل کا نام فقہ ہے ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ تخصیص سے کیا مراد ہے تخصیص شخصی یا تخصیص نوعی مراد ہے اگر آپ کہتے ہیں کہ تخصیص شخصی مراد ہے کہ فقہ چند گنے چنے مسائل کا نام ہے کہ نہ کمی ہو سکے اور نہ زیادتی تو فلانسلم کیونکہ یہ دوسرے علوم کی طرح علم ہے اور دوسرے علوم میں علماء کی نظر وفکر سے مسائل کم زیادہ ہوتے رہتے ہیں تو یہ بھی ایک علم ہے اس میں بھی کمی زیادتی ہوگی اور اگر آپ کہتے ہیں کہ تخصیص نوعی مراد ہے تو یہ مسلم ہے لیکن ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ تخصیص نوعی یعنی نوع کی تخصیص باقی رہے اور اس کے افراد کم زیادہ ہوتے رہیں خلاصہ یہ کہ مسائل کا کم زیادہ ہونا تخصیص نوعی کے خلاف نہیں
Summary: According to the people, fiqh is the name of a specific science. And according to the author's definition, it is a general concept that increases and decreases. Answer: You said that according to the people, fiqh is the name of a specific and determinate science and issues. We ask: what is meant by specification? Is personal specification intended or type specification? If you say personal specification is meant, that fiqh is the name of a few counted issues that cannot decrease or increase, then we do not accept, because it is a science like other sciences, and in other sciences, issues increase and decrease according to the view and thought of scholars, so this too is a science, it will also have increase and decrease. And if you say type specification is meant, then this is accepted, but it is possible that type specification, i.e., specification of the type, remains and its individual instances increase and decrease. Summary: The increase and decrease of issues is not contrary to type specification.
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection to the definition of fiqh given by the matn author (Sadr al-Shariah). The objector claims that fiqh, as understood by the people (qawm), is a fixed, specific body of knowledge, but the author's definition makes it a general concept that can vary. The response clarifies that if by 'specific' the objector means personal specification (takhsis shakhsi) — i.e., a fixed set of issues — then that is rejected because fiqh, like all sciences, evolves as scholars derive new rulings. If instead type specification (takhsis naw'i) is meant — i.e., fiqh remains a distinct type of knowledge — then that is acceptable, and the number of individual issues within that type can vary. The key point is that a type can have increasing or decreasing instances without losing its identity.

Key Terms
تخصیص شخصی (takhsis shakhsi): Personal specification: fiqh as a fixed set of specific issues that cannot change.
تخصیص نوعی (takhsis naw'i): Type specification: fiqh as a category of knowledge that remains distinct even as its individual issues increase or decrease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between takhsis shakhsi and takhsis naw'i in the context of defining fiqh?
A) Takhsis shakhsi refers to personal opinions, while takhsis naw'i refers to general principles.
B) Takhsis shakhsi means a fixed set of issues, while takhsis naw'i means a category that can have varying instances.
C) Takhsis shakhsi is for the Sahaba, and takhsis naw'i is for later scholars.
D) Takhsis shakhsi is used in the Shafi'i school, and takhsis naw'i in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
Fiqh is defined as a type of knowledge (naw') whose individual rulings can increase and decrease, but its category as a distinct science remains fixed.

The Condition of Zuhur in the Definition of Fiqh
Analyzes the condition of 'zuhur' in the definition of fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why zuhur 'ala al-mujtahid is the correct interpretation and identify the flaws in alternative interpretations.

Core Idea
Zuhur in the definition of fiqh means manifestation to the individual mujtahid — not to a group.

The definition of fiqh includes the condition that rulings must be 'manifest' (zahir) to the mujtahid. Commentators raised two possible readings: manifestation to some Companions or to the majority. Both lead to contradictions. The resolved understanding is that zuhur is personal to each mujtahid, preserving the status of all Companions as fuqaha and including rulings from ahad hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the problem
The matn's definition of fiqh requires zuhur. The commentators propose two possible interpretations: zuhur fi al-jumlah (to some) and zuhur fi al-akthar (to the majority).
2
Analyze zuhur fi al-jumlah
If manifestation to only some Companions is meant, then many Companions who were unaware of certain rulings would not be fuqaha, which contradicts their unanimous status as fuqaha.
Reference to Companions referring to Aisha (RA) illustrates their seeking knowledge from others.
3
Analyze zuhur fi al-akthar
If manifestation to the majority is meant, the majority cannot be precisely defined, and additionally, rulings from ahad hadith would not be considered fiqh until widespread, which is false.
Ahad hadith are valid sources of fiqh for the mujtahid who knows them.
4
Derive the correct interpretation
The intended meaning is zuhur 'ala al-mujtahid — manifestation to the individual mujtahid. Once a ruling is known to him, it becomes part of his fiqh, regardless of how many others know it.
This interpretation avoids both problems and aligns with the practice of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : ماتن نے جو تعریف کی ہے اس میں ظہور کی قید ہے شاریخ نے کہا کہ اب ہم پوچھتے ہیں ظہور فی الاکثر مراد ہے یا ظہور فی الجملہ مراد ہے یعنی ظہور ا کثر صحابہ پر ہوا ہو یا بعض صحابہ پر اگر ظہور فی الجملہ مراد ہو یعنی بعض کو وحی کے نزول کا علم ہو بعض کو پتہ نہ ہو اس صورت میں معنی ہوگا کہ فقیہ کے لئے ان احکام کا جاننا شرط ہے جن کا ظہور بعض پر ہو چکا ہو تو لازم آئے گا کہ صحابہ فقیہ نہ ہوں کیونکہ بہت سارے صحابہ کرام پر بعض مسائل کا ظہور نہیں ہوا یہی وجہ ہے کہ وہ حضرت عائشہ کی طرف رجوع کرتے تھے تو اس سے لازم آئے گا کہ وہ فقیہ نہ ہوں حالانکہ وہ بالا جماع فقیہ ہیں اور اگر ظہور فی الاکثر مراد ہو یہ بھی درست نہیں کیونکہ اکثر مجبول ہیں غیر منضبط ہیں کیونکہ پتہ نہیں چلتا کہ نزول وحی کے وقت کتنے صحابہ تھے کیونکہ صحابہ تجارت وغیرہ میں مشغول رہتے تھے یہ پتہ نہیں چلتا کہ کتنے موجود تھے اور اگر بالفرض تسلیم بھی کرلیں کہ اکثر صحابہ معلوم منضبط ہیں پھر بھی درست نہیں کیونکہ پھر یہ لازم آئے گا کہ جو احکام اخبار احاد سے ثابت ہیں وہ فقہ سے نہ ہوں جب تک اکثر افراد پر ظاہر نہ ہو جائیں حالانکہ ایسے احکام بھی فقہ میں داخل ہیں خلاصہ یہ کہ یہ تعریف بھی اشکال اور خلل سے محفوظ نہیں ہے۔ جواب :۔ ظہور سے مراد نہ تو ظہو فی الجملہ ہے اور نہی ظہور علی الاعم بلکہ ا سے مرا ظہورعلی المجتہد ہے کہ اگر مجتہد پر ظہور ہوا ہو مجتہد کو جانا ضروری ہو گا ظہور فی الاکثر اور ظہور فی الجملہ مراد نہیں (واللہ اعلم بالصواب)
Fourth: The author (matn) placed a condition of zuhur in the definition. The commentators said: We ask: Is zuhur al-akthar (manifestation to the majority) intended, or zuhur fi al-jumlah (manifestation to some)? That is, did it happen to most Companions or to some? If zuhur fi al-jumlah is intended, i.e., some knew of the revelation while others did not, then it would require that a faqih must know those rulings that have been manifested to some. This would entail that the Companions are not fuqaha, because many of them were not aware of some rulings, and they would refer to Aisha. Thus they would not be fuqaha, whereas they are unanimously fuqaha. And if zuhur fi al-akthar is intended, that is also incorrect because the majority is not precisely known; we cannot ascertain how many Companions were present at the time of revelation as they were engaged in trade, etc. Even if we assume the majority is known, it would still be invalid because then rulings established by ahad hadith would not be fiqh until they become manifest to the majority, whereas such rulings are included in fiqh. In summary, this definition is not free from problems. Answer: The intended meaning of zuhur is neither zuhur fi al-jumlah nor zuhur al-akthar. Rather, it means zuhur 'ala al-mujtahid (manifestation to the mujtahid). So if it is manifest to the mujtahid, he must know it. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage addresses a critique of the definition of fiqh that includes a condition of zuhur (manifestation). The objectors propose two possible interpretations: manifestation to a few (zuhur fi al-jumlah) or manifestation to the majority (zuhur fi al-akthar). Each is shown to be problematic. Zuhur fi al-jumlah would wrongly exclude some Companions from being fuqaha. Zuhur fi al-akthar is also flawed because the majority is not defined and rulings from ahad hadith would be excluded. The author's response clarifies that zuhur refers to the ruling being manifest to the individual mujtahid; once it becomes known to him, it enters the realm of fiqh for him. This interpretation preserves the status of all Companions as fuqaha and includes rulings from ahad hadith.

Key Terms
ظہور (zuhur): Manifestation or clear knowledge of a ruling to the mujtahid.
ظہور فی الجملہ (zuhur fi al-jumlah): Manifestation to a subset of the Companions, not all.
ظہور علی المجتہد (zuhur 'ala al-mujtahid): Manifestation specifically to the person performing ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct interpretation of 'zuhur' in the definition of fiqh according to the author?
A) Manifestation to the majority of scholars
B) Manifestation to some of the Companions
C) Manifestation to the individual mujtahid
D) Public knowledge among all Muslims

Key Takeaway
The condition of zuhur in the definition of fiqh must be understood as personal manifestation to the mujtahid, not as widespread knowledge.

Subject Matter of Usul al-Fiqh: Proofs and Rulings as Essential Accidents
Defining the subject matter and essential attributes of usul al-fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the subject matter of usul al-fiqh as proofs and rulings with respect to their essential accidents, and explain why the hujjiyya of the Quran and Sunnah is not investigated within usul.

Core Idea
Usul al-fiqh investigates proofs and rulings not as essences, but as bearers of essential accidents.

This passage from Al-Talwih presents a critical refinement of the common definition of usul al-fiqh. While many say usul discusses proofs and rulings, the author clarifies that a science never discusses the essences themselves but their states and accidents. Understanding this distinction is foundational for navigating usul al-fiqh properly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common definition
The passage begins by stating the widely accepted definition: usul al-fiqh discusses the legislative proofs (adilla) and rulings (ahkam). Note that this is the starting point.
2
Refine the definition with ellipsis
The commentator explains that the phrase is elliptical; it should read 'states of proofs and rulings' because a science does not discuss the subject itself but its states and accidents. This omission is conventional.
The Arabic uses mudhaf mahzuf (omitted genitive construct).
3
Define 'essential accident' (al-‘arad al-dhati)
An essential accident is a predicate external to the thing whose origin is the essence, either directly or through a coextensive or more general intermediate. Examples: perception for humans (direct), laughter through wonder (coextensive), movement through being animal (more general).
This is a key philosophical concept from logic that structures the subject of every science.
4
Understand how essential accidents are investigated
The investigation involves predicating these essential accidents on the subject (proofs and rulings) or their types. Examples: 'the Book establishes the ruling definitively', 'the command indicates obligation', 'the general indicates certainty', 'the general that has been specified indicates probability'.
All discussions in usul reduce to establishing essential accidents of proofs and rulings.
5
Address the objection about Quran and Sunnah
The passage answers why ijma‘ and qiyas are explicitly included as topics but not the Quran and Sunnah. The reason: the probative value of Quran and Sunnah is considered self-evident (badihi) for the usuli, having been established in theology (kalam), while ijma‘ and qiyas require proof.
This shows that usul focuses on acquired matters (kasbiyyat) that need evidence.

الخ۔۔۔۔۔ یہ اصول فقہ کے مسائل میں سے ہے
فعلم ان : ماقبل پر تفریح اول کا بیان ہے کہ یہ تمام مباحث مذکورہ یعنی شرائط دلیل اور انواع حکم ۔ مباحث محکوم به ب مباحث محکوم علیہ ان ساری مباحث کا تعلق قضیہ کلیہ کے ساتھ ہے۔ جس طرح قضیہ کلیہ مسائل اصول فقہ سے ہے اسی طرح یہ مباحث بھی اصول فقہ میں سے ہیں اور ماقبل میں جو کہا گیا تھا کہ یہ موصل الی الفقہ بتوصل قریب ہوں اس کا یہی مطلب ہے

الترويج لحل التوضيح والتلويح
تلویح
قَوْلُهُ عُلِمَ أَنَّهُ يُبْحَثُ فِي هَذَا الْعِلْمِ عَنْ الْأَدِلَّةِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ وَالْأَحْكَامِ) يَعْنِي عَنْ أَحْوَالِهِمَا عَلَى حَذْفِ الْمُصَافِ ، إِذْ لَا يُبْحَثُ فِي الْعِلْمِ عَنْ نَفْسِ الْمَوْضُوعِ ، بَلْ
عَنْ أَحْوَالِهِ وَعَوَارِضِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّ حَذَفَ هَذَا الْمُصَافِ شَائِعٌ فِي عِبَارَةِ الْقَوْمِ . قَوْلُهُ ) فَمَوْضُوعُ هَذَا الْعِلْمِ الْمُرَادُ بِمَوْضُوعِ الْعِلْمِ مَا يُبْحَثُ فِي الْعِلْمِ عَنْ
عَوَارِضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْعَرْضِ هَهُنَا الْمَحْمُولُ عَلَى الشَّيء الْخَارِجُ عَنهُ وَبِالْعَرْضِ الذَّاتِي مَا يَكُونُ مَنْشَأَهُ الذَّاتُ بِأَنْ يَلْحَقَ الشَّيْءَ لِذَاتِهِ كَالْإِدْرَاكِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ أَوْ بِوَاسِطَةِ أَمْرٍ يُسَاوِيهِ كَالضَّحِكِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ بِوَاسِطَةِ تَعَجُّبِهِ أَوْ بِوَاسِطَةِ أَمْرٍ أَعَمَّ مِنْهُ دَاخِلٍ فِيهِ كَالتَّحَرُّكِ لِلْإِنْسَانِ بِوَاسِطَةِ كَوْنِهِ حَيَوَانًا وَالْمُـرَادُ بِالْبَحْثِ عَنْ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ حَمُلُهَا عَلَى مَوْضُوعِ الْعِلْمِ كَقَوْلِنَا الْكِتَابُ يُثْبِتُ الْحُكْمَ قَطْعًا أَوْ عَلَى أَنْوَاعِهِ كَقَوْلِنَا الْأمْرُ يُفِيدُ الْوُجُوبَ أَوْ عَلَى أَعْرَاضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ كَقَوْلِنَا الْعَامُ يُفِيدُ الْقَطَعَ أَوْ عَلَى أَنْوَاعِ أَعْرَاضِهِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ كَقَوْلِنَا الْعَامُ الَّذِي خُصَّ مِنْهُ الْبَعْضُ يُفِيدُ الظَّنَّ وَجَمِيعُ مَبَاحِثِ أُصُولِ الْفِقْهِ رَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى إِثْبَاتِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الذَّاتِيَّةِ لِلْأَدِلَّةِ وَالْأحْكَامِ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِثْبَاتُ الْأَدِلَّةِ لِلْأحْكَامِ وَثُبُوتُ الْأَحْكَامِ بِالْا دِلَّةِ بِمَعْنَى أَنَّ جَمِيعَ مَحْمُوَلَاتِ مَسَائِلِ هَذَا الْفَنْ هُوَ الْإِثْبَاتُ وَالنُّبُوتُ وَمَا لَهُ نَفْعٌ وَدَخَلٌ فِي ذَلِكَ فَيَكُونُ مَوْضُوعُهُ الْأَدِلَّةَ وَالْأَحْكَامَ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِثْبَاتُ الْأَدِلَّةِ لِلْأَحْكَامِ وَثُبُوتِ الأحكامِ بِالْأَدِلَّةِ ، فَإِنْ قَلْت فَمَا بَالُهُمْ يَجْعَلُونَ مِنْ مَسَائِلِ الْأُصُولِ إِثْبَاتَ الْإِجْمَاعِ وَالْقِيَاسِ لِلْأحكام وَلَا يَجْعَلُونَ مِنْهَا إثْبَات الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ لِذَلِكَ قُلْتُ ؛ لأنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ بِالنَّظَرِ فِي الْفَنْ هِيَ الْكَسْبِيَّاتُ الْمُفْقِرَةُ إِلَى الدَّلِيلِ وَكَوْنُ الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ حُجَّةٌ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْبَدِيهِي فِي نَظَرِ الْأُصُولِي لِتَقَرُّرِهِ فِي الْكَلَامِ وَشُهْرَتِهِ بَيْنَ
It is known that this science discusses the legislative proofs and the rulings, meaning their states, by omitting the genitive construction, for a science does not discuss the subject itself, but rather its states and accidents. However, this omission of the genitive is common in the expression of the people. He said: So the subject of this science: what is intended by the subject of a science is that whose essential accidents are investigated. And what is meant by 'accident' here is the predicate upon a thing that is external to it. And by 'essential accident' is that whose origin is the essence, either attaching to the thing due to its essence, like perception for a human, or through a coextensive intermediate, like laughter for a human through his wonder, or through a more general intermediate contained within it, like movement for a human through being an animal. And what is meant by investigating essential accidents is predicating them upon the subject of the science, as in our saying: 'The Book establishes the ruling definitively', or upon its types, as in our saying: 'The command indicates obligation', or upon its essential accidents, as in our saying: 'The general indicates certainty', or upon the types of its essential accidents, as in our saying: 'The general from which a part has been specified indicates probability.' And all the discussions of usul al-fiqh go back to establishing the essential accidents of the proofs and rulings, in terms of the proofs establishing the rulings and the rulings being established by the proofs, meaning that all the predicates of the issues of this art are establishment and being established and what has benefit and enters into that. So its subject is the proofs and rulings in terms of the proofs establishing the rulings and the rulings being established by the proofs. If you say: Why do they include among the issues of usul the establishment of ijma' and qiyas for rulings, and they do not include among them the establishment of the Book and Sunnah for that? I say: Because the purpose of investigation in the art is the acquired matters that need evidence, and the fact that the Book and Sunnah are proofs is like the self-evident in the view of the usuli due to its being established in theology and its fame among...
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage defines the subject matter of usul al-fiqh. It begins by stating the common definition: usul al-fiqh discusses the legislative proofs (adillah) and rulings (ahkam). However, the commentator (Taftazani in al-Talwih) refines this: a science does not discuss the essences themselves, but rather their states (ahwal) and accidents (awaridh). Thus, the phrase 'discusses proofs and rulings' is elliptical, omitting the word 'states of'. This omission is conventional among scholars. The subject of a science is that which is investigated with respect to its essential accidents (awaridh dhatiyya). An 'accident' here is a predicate external to the thing. An 'essential accident' is one whose source is the essence, either directly (e.g., perception for humans) or through a coextensive intermediate (e.g., laughter through wonder) or through a more general intermediate (e.g., movement through being an animal). Investigating essential accidents means predicating them on the subject or its types, as in examples like 'the Book establishes the ruling definitively' or 'the command indicates obligation'. All usul discussions reduce to establishing essential accidents of proofs and rulings from the perspective that proofs establish rulings and rulings are established by proofs. The passage then addresses an objection: why are ijma' and qiyas explicitly included as topics but not the Quran and Sunnah? The answer: because the probative value (hujjiyya) of the Quran and Sunnah is considered self-evident (badihi) for the usuli, having been established in theology (kalam), while ijma' and qiyas require proof and are therefore the focus of investigation.

Key Terms
العرض الذاتي (al-‘arad al-dhati): An accident whose origin is the essence, either directly or through a coextensive or more general intermediate.
موضوع العلم (mawdu‘ al-‘ilm): That whose essential accidents are investigated in the science.
الأدلة (al-adilla): The proofs (Quran, Sunnah, ijma, qiyas) that establish rulings.
الأحكام (al-ahkam): The rulings (obligation, prohibition, etc.) that are established by proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that the probative value (hujjiyya) of the Quran and Sunnah is not investigated in usul al-fiqh, while ijma and qiyas are?
A) Because the Quran and Sunnah are not proofs for rulings.
B) Because their probative value is self-evident (badihi) for the usuli, having been established in theology.
C) Because ijma and qiyas are stronger proofs than the Quran and Sunnah.
D) Because usul al-fiqh only discusses acquired matters and the Quran and Sunnah are innate.

Key Takeaway
The subject matter of usul al-fiqh is proofs and rulings with respect to their essential accidents; the Quran and Sunnah are not investigated because their probative value is self-evident.

Can a Single Science Have Multiple Subjects? The Hanafi Position on Unity of Subject
Resolving whether a single science can have multiple subjects

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a single science cannot have multiple subjects unless the subject is an attribution (idafa), and evaluate the counterargument from the example of medicine.

Core Idea
A single science’s subject is one: either a single thing or a relation between two things, never two unrelated things.

In this passage, the author of al-Tawdih addresses a foundational issue in the philosophy of science: can a single discipline study more than one subject? The majority of scholars cite medicine as an example, but the Hanafi position, as articulated here, insists on a stricter criterion. Understanding this debate sharpens your ability to define the scope of a science, which is crucial for delineating the subject matter of usul al-fiqh itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central question and the opposing positions
Read the passage and identify the two views: the claim that a single science can have multiple subjects (jumhur) vs. the author's refutation. Note the medicine example.
Focus on the author's statement: 'This is not correct.'
2
Define the key terms: mawdu', ilm, masa'il, idafa
Distinguish between the subject (mawdu'), the issues (masa'il), and the investigated matter (mabhooth 'anhu). Understand idafa as a relation between two things.
The passage treats idafa as a special case that allows both relata to be counted as one relational subject.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument for unity
The author argues that the unity of a science is based on the unity of its issues (masa'il), which in turn requires a single subject. If the subject is not an idafa, multiple subjects would imply multiple sciences.
The argument is aqli (rational): if the subject is manifold, the science would lack unity.
4
Examine the counterexample of medicine and the Hanafi response
Opponents say medicine studies both body and medicines. The author responds that medicines are studied only insofar as they affect the body; thus the true subject is the human body alone.
The response shows that apparent multiplicity can be reduced to a single subject via subordination.
5
Apply the principle to usul al-fiqh
Recognize that the subject of usul al-fiqh is a relation (idafa) between proofs and rulings, making it a single relational subject. If it were not a relation, it would require one subject.
This reinforces how Hanafi usul defines its own subject matter.

وَاحِدٍ أَنْ يَصْطَلِحَ حِينَئِذٍ عَلَى أَنَّ الْفِقْهَ وَالْهَنْدَسَةَ عِلْمٌ وَاحِدٌ وَمَوْضُوعَهُ شَيْئَانِ فِعْلُ الْمُكَلَّفِ وَالْمِقْدَارُ وَمَا أَوْرَدُوا مِنَ النَّظِيرِ ، وَهُوَ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ وَالْأدْوِيَةُ فَجَوَابُهُ أَنَّ الْبَحْتَ فِي الْأَدْوِيَةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ مِنْ حَيْثُ إِنَّ بَدَنَ الْإِنْسَانِ يَصِحُ بِبَعْضِهَا وَيَمْرَضُ بِبَعْضِهَا فَالْمَوْضُوعُ فِي الْجَمِيعِ بَدَنُ الْإِنْسَانِ . ترجمہ: اور جان لے تو کہ بیشک میں جب واقع ہو ا موضوع اور مسائل کی مباحث میں تو میں نے ارادہ کیا یہ کہ سناؤں تجھ کو ان دونوں کی بعض وہ مباحث کہ نہیں ہے مستغنی علم حاصل کر نیوالا ان سے اگر چہ نہیں ہیں لائق وہ ( ابحاث ) اس فن کے ۔ ان ( مباحث ) میں سے (ایک بحث ) یہ ہے کہ تحقیق ذکر کیا ہے انہوں نے کہ بیشک ایک علم کہ کبھی ہوتے ہیں اس کیلئے ایک سے زیادہ موضوع جیسا کہ علم طب ہے مثال کے طور پر کہ بحث کی جاتی ہے اس ( طب ) میں بدن انسانی کے احوال سے اور ادویہ کے احوال سے اور ان دونوں کی مثل کے احوال سے اور یہ (مذکورہ بات صحیح نہیں ہے اور تحقیق اس بارہ میں یہ ہے کہ کسی علم میں مجوث عنہ اگر ہو ایک شئی کی اضافت دوسری کی طرف جیسا کہ بیشک اصول فقہ میں بحث کی جاتی ہے ادلہ کے حکم کو ثابت کرنے سے اور منطق میں بحث کی جاتی ہے تصور یا تصدیق (معلوم ) کے تصور یا تصدیق ( مجبول ) تک پہنچانے سے اور کبھی ہوتے ہیں بعض ، وہ عوارض جن کو دخل ہے مجوث عنها مسائل میں پیدا ہونے والے مضافین میں سے ایک سے اور بعض عوارض دوسرے سے پس موضوع اس علم کا دونوں مضاف ہوں گے اور اگر نہ ہو مجوث عند اضافت تو نہیں ہوگا ایک علم کا موضوع کثیر اشیاء کیونکہ علم کا متحد اور مختلف ہونا سوائے اس کے نہیں وہ معلومات یعنی مسائل کے اتحاد اور اختلاف کے اعتبار سے ہوتا ہے۔ پس موضوع کا مختلف ہونا ثابت کر دیگا علم کے مختلف ہونے کو اور اگر مراد لیا جائے ایک علم سے کہ ایک علم وہ ہے کہ واقع ہو جائے اصطلاح اس بات پر کہ وہ ایک علم ہے بغیر رعایت کرنے ایسے معنی کے جو ثابت کرے وحدت کو تو اس کا کوئی اعتبار نہیں ہے ۔ علاوہ اس کے کہ بیشک ہر ایک کیلئے ( جائز ہوگا کہ ) وہ اصطلاح قائم کر لے اس وقت اس بات پر کہ بیشک فقہ اور ھندسہ ایک علم ہے اور اس کا موضوع دو چیزیں ہیں فعل مکلف اور مقدار ۔ اور جو وارد کی ہے انہوں نے نظیر اور وہ ( نظیر ) بدن انسانی اور ادویہ ہیں تو جواب اس ( نظیر ) کا یہ ہے کہ بیشک بحث ادویہ میں سوائے اس کے نہیں وہ اس حیثیت سے ہے کہ بیشک بدن انسانی صحیح ہوتا ہے بعض ( ادویہ) کیسا تھا اور مریض ہوتا ہے بعض ( ادویہ ) کیسا تھے ۔ پس موضوع تمام میں بدن انسانی ہے تشریح: واعلم اني لما وقعت - صاحب توضیح فرماتے ہیں کہ یہاں تک میں نے موضوع کے متعلق مباحث کو ذکر کیا ہے اب میرا ارادہ ایسی مباحث کو ذکر کرنے کا ہے جو مباحث ایسی تو نہیں کہ جن کو اصول فقہ کے موضوع میں دخل ہولیکن بایں ہمہ اصول فقہ کو جاننے والا ان سے مستغنی نہیں ہو سکتا۔ چنانچہ یہاں پر تین مباحث کو ذکر کریں گے۔ کیا علم واحد کے موضوع متعدد ہو سکتے ہیں بحث اول: یہ ہے کہ کیا ایک علم کے موضوع میں تعدد ہو سکتا ہے یا نہیں؟ یعنی متعدد اشیاء ایک علم کا موضوع بن سکتی ہیں یا نہیں صاحب توضیح فرماتے ہیں کہ جمہور علماء محققین کے مذہب میں یہ ہے کہ علم واحد کے موضوع میں مطلقاً تعدد ہوسکتا ہے جیسا کہ علم طب کے موضوع میں تعدد ہے کہ اس کا موضوع بدن انسانی اور ادویہ ہیں لیکن صاحب توضیح فرماتے ہیں کہ ملی الاطلاق یہ کہہ دینا کہ ایک علم کے موضوع میں تعدد ہوتا ہے صحیح نہیں ہے بلکہ اس میں تفصیل ہے کہ علم کے اندر جو چیز مبحوث عنھا
Know that when I entered into the discussions of the subject and the issues, I intended to make you hear some of its discussions which the diligent student cannot do without, even if they are not befitting of this art. Among them, they have mentioned that a single science may have more than one subject, like medicine for example: it investigates the states of the human body and the states of medicines and the like. And this is not correct. The verification in it is that the investigated thing in a science, if it is an attribution of something to another, as in Usul al-Fiqh one investigates the establishment of proofs for the ruling, and in logic one investigates the conveying of a conception or assent to a conception or assent, and some of the accidents that have entry into the investigated thing arise from one of the two relata and some from the other, then the subject of this science is both relata. And if the investigated thing is not attribution, then the subject of a single science cannot be many things, because the unity and diversity of a science is only by the unity and diversity of the known things, i.e., the issues. So diversity of the subject necessitates diversity of the science. And if by 'single science' is meant what is conventionally agreed to be a single science without regard to a meaning that necessitates unity, then there is no consideration for it. Moreover, anyone could then agree that fiqh and geometry are a single science and its subject is two things: the act of the mukallaf and quantity. And as for the example they gave, which is the human body and medicines, the answer is that investigation in medicines is only insofar as the human body becomes healthy with some and sick with some, so the subject in all is the human body. Translation: [Urdu translation of the above Arabic]. Explanation: [Urdu tashreeh explaining that the author of al-Tawdih says he has discussed the subject, now will discuss three issues; first is whether a single science can have multiple subjects; the majority say yes absolutely, but the author says it is not correct absolutely; rather there is detail, and the text cuts off.]
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is from the sharh on al-Tawdih, addressing the question of whether a single science can have multiple subjects. The author begins by stating that he will present certain discussions that, although not strictly part of the subject of usul al-fiqh, are essential for the student. The first point: some scholars claim that a single science can have more than one subject, citing medicine as an example (body and medicines). The author refutes this as incorrect in absolute terms, and provides a tahqiq (verification). He explains that if the investigated matter (mabhooth 'anhu) in a science is an idafa (attribution) between two things, as in usul al-fiqh (proofs for rulings) and logic (conveying conceptions/assents), then the subject is that relation, not the two things separately. If it is not an attribution, then a science cannot have multiple subjects because the unity of a science is based on the unity of its issues (masa'il); different subjects would imply different sciences. He further shows that even the example of medicine does not truly have two subjects: medicines are studied only insofar as they affect the body, so the real subject is the human body. The Urdu translation and tashreeh clarify that the author (Sahib al-Tawdih) disagrees with the majority of verifying scholars who allow absolute multiplicity, and instead says it requires detail—specifically, if the subject is a relation, both relata are included, but if not, it cannot be multiple. The text cuts off but the argument is clear: the unity of a science is determined by the unity of its subject matter, not by conventional agreement.

Key Terms
موضوع (mawdu'): The subject of a science; that which is investigated in a science (al-mabhooth 'anhu). According to the author, it may be a single thing or a relation between two things, but cannot be multiple unrelated things.
علم ('ilm): A science or discipline; its unity is determined by the unity of its subject and its issues (masa'il).
مسائل (masa'il): The issues or problems studied in a science; they are the known things (ma'lumat) that determine the unity or diversity of a science.
إضافة (idafa): Attribution or relation between two things; if the investigated matter is an idafa, the subject of the science includes both relata as a relational whole.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Tawdih, can a single science have multiple subjects without any condition?
A) Yes, absolutely, as in medicine.
B) No, never; a science must have exactly one subject.
C) It can if the subject is a relation (idafa) between two things, otherwise not.
D) It depends on the science: some sciences have multiple subjects, some do not.

Key Takeaway
A single science has one subject, either a single thing or a relation (idafa) between two things; apparent multiplicity is resolved by subordination of investigations to one primary subject.

advanced
10 min
One Thing Can Be the Subject of Multiple Sciences
Rejects the famous principle that one thing cannot be subject of two sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rational proof to demonstrate that a single entity can be the subject of multiple sciences, and evaluate the opposing view.

Core Idea
A truly single thing can have multiple attributes, allowing it to be investigated under different aspects in distinct sciences.

This lesson tackles a foundational debate in usul al-fiqh: can one thing serve as the subject of two different sciences? The author rejects the famous opinion that it cannot, offering a rational argument based on the nature of a truly simple entity. Understanding this dispute clarifies how sciences are distinguished—not solely by their subject but also by the attributes they investigate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested principle and the Hanafi rebuttal
State the well-known claim: one thing cannot be the subject of two sciences. Then note the author's immediate response: it is not impossible, it actually occurs.
The author uses 'mashhur' to indicate the famous position he is opposing.
2
Deconstruct the rational proof (dalil aqli)
Follow the argument: the truly one (al-wahid al-haqiqi) has no parts, so any attributes must attach to its essence. Since multiple attributes (essential, relational, positive, negative) can inhere, the same essence can be investigated in different sciences.
The proof uses tripartite rationale: no parts → no partial attachment → attributes belong to essence → infinite regress avoided.
3
Analyze the role of 'haythiyya' (aspect)
The 'haythiyya' (e.g., 'insofar as it has shape') is not part of the subject but a qualification that specifies which attributes are studied. It distinguishes sciences without multiplying the subject.
If 'haythiyya' were part of the subject, each science would investigate that aspect itself, not the entity's attributes—contrary to reality.
4
Apply the concept to the example of geometry and physics
Geometry studies bodies of the world insofar as they have shape; physics studies the same bodies insofar as they have nature. The subject is identical, but the attributes and thus the sciences differ.
This concrete example demonstrates that the principle is not only theoretically possible but practically realized.
