وسکون ذوالواسطہ ہونے کے اعتبار سے موخر اور واسطہ ہونے کے لحاظ سے مقدم ہوں گے یہی تقدم الشئی علی نفسہ ہے یہ تو ایسے ہو گیا کہ فر من المطر وقام تحت المیز اب یعنی بارش سے بھاگ کر پرنالے کے نیچے کھڑے ہو گئے ۔ والمشهور في الخ۔ اس مشہور اشکال کا مشہور جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں ہر دو چیزیں الگ الگ ہیں ایک ہے نفس صحت نفس مرض اور ایک ہے امکان صحت اور امکان مرض اسی طرح ایک ہے نفس حرکت نفس سکون نفس شکل اور ایک ہے امکان حرکت امکان سکون اور امکان شکل جب معاملہ اس طرح ہے تو اب حیثیت جو واسطہ ہے یہ امکان صحت امکان مرض امکان حرکت امکان سکون امکان شکل ہے اور ذوواسطہ نفس صحت نفس مرض نفس حرکت نفس سکون اور نفس شکل ہے پس ذو واسطہ جو چیز ہے وہ اور ہے اور جو واسطہ ہے وہ اور ہے تو تقدم اشتی علی نفسہ لازم نہ آیا۔

تحقیق: تحقیقی جواب کا بیان ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ تم نے قید کا معنی ہی غلط کیا ہے تم نے کہا کہ قید کہتے ہیں کہ عوارض ذاتیہ کا موضوع کیلئے ثبوت حیثیت کے واسطہ سے ہوگا یہ منی غلط ہے بلکہ صحیح معنی یہ ہے کہ علم میں جوعوارض مبحوث عنہا ہوں گے ان سے بحث کے وقت اس حیثیت کا لحاظ ہو گا یعنی یہ بحث کی قید ہے آگے عوارض عام ہیں ان کا ثبوت بالواسطہ ہو یا بلا واسطہ بعنوان دیگر یہاں پر چیزیں دو ہیں ایک یہ ہے کہ حیثیت قید ہو عوارض کے ثبوت کی اور دوسری یہ کہ حیثیت قید ہو عوارض ذاتیہ سے بحث کی اور یہی معنی ہے حیثیت بیانیہ کا پس شاریخ کی کلام لوٹ گئی صاحب توضیح کے کلام کی طرف گویا کہ صاحب تلویح نے اسی معنی کو بیان کیا جس کو صاحب توضیح نے بیان کیا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔

وَمِنْهَا أَنَّ الْمَشْهُورَ اَنَّ الشَّيْءَ الْوَاحِدَ لَا يَكُونُ مَوْضُوعًا لِلْعِلْمَيْنِ أَقُولُ هَذَا غَيْرُ مُمْتَنِعٍ بَلْ وَاقِعٌ فَإِنَّ الشَّيءَ الْوَاحِدَ يَكُونُ لَهُ أَعْرَاضٌ مُتَنَوّعَةٌ فَفِي كُلّ عِلْمٍ يُبْحَثُ عَنْ بَعْض مِنْهَا كَمَا ذَكَرُنَا.

وَإِنَّمَا قُلْنَا إِنَّ الشَّيْء الْوَاحِدَ يَكُونُ لَهُ أَعْرَاضٌ مُتَنَوِّعَةٌ فَإِنَّ الْوَاحِدَ الْحَقِيقِيَّ يُوصَفُ بِصِفَاتٍ كَثِيرَةٍ ، وَلَا يَضُرُّ أَن يَكُونَ بَعْضُهَا حَقِيقِيَّةً وَبَعْضُهَا إِضَافِيَّةٌ وَبَعْضُهَا إِيجَابِيَّةٌ وَبَعْضُهَا سَلْبِيَّةٌ ، وَلَا شَيْءٍ مِنْهَا يَلْحَقُهُ لِجُزْئِهِ لِعَدَمِ الْجُزْءُ لَهُ فَلُحُوقُ بَعْضِهَا لَا بُدَّ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِذَاتِهِ قَطْعًا لِلتَّسَلْسُلِ فِي الْمَبْدَأُ فَلُحُوقُ الْبَعْضِ الْآخَرِ إنْ كَانَ لِذَاتِهِ فَهُوَ الْمَطْلُوبُ وَإِنْ كَانَ لِغَيْرِهِ نَتَكَلَّمُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْغَيْرِ حَتَّى يَنْتَهِيَ إِلَى ذَاتِهِ قَطْعًا لِلتَّسَلُسُلِ فِي الْمَبْدَأُ .

وَلَأَنَّهُ يَلْزَمُ اسْتِكْمَالُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِهِ إِذَا ثَبَتَ ذَلِكَ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الشَّيْء الْوَاحِدَ مَوْضُوعَ عِلْمَيْنِ وَيَكُونَ تَمِيرُهُمَا بِحَسَبِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْمَبْحُوثِ عَنْهَا وَذَلِكَ ؛ لأنَّ الْحَدَ العِلْمَيْنِ وَاخْتِلالَهُمَا بِحَسَبِ الْحَادِ الْمَعْلُومَاتِ وَاخْتِلافِهَا وَالْمَعْلُومَاتُ هِيَ الْمَسَائِلُ فَكَمَا أَنَّ الْمَسَائِلَ تَتَّحِدُ وَتَخْتَلِفُ بِحَسْبِ مَوْضُوعَاتِهَا وَهِيَ رَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى مَوْضُوعِ الْعِلْمِ فَكَذَلِكَ تَتَّحِدُ الْمَسَائِلُ وَتَخْتَلِفُ بِحَسَبِ مَحْمُوَلَاتِهَا وَهِيَ رَاجِعَةٌ إِلَى تِلْكَ الْأَعْرَاضِ وَإِنْ أُرِيدَ أَنَّ الِاصْطَلَاحَ جَرُى بأنَّ الْمَوْنُوعَ مُعْتَبَرٌ فِي ذَلِكَ لَا الْمَحْمُولَ فَحِينَئِذٍ لَا مُشَاحَّةَ فِي ذَلِكَ عَلَى أَنَّ قَوْلَهُمُ : إِنَّ مَوْضُوعَ الْهَيْئَةِ هِيَ أَجْسَامُ الْعَالَمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ لَهَا شَكُلُ وَمَوْضُوعُ عِلْمِ السَّمَاءِ وَالْعَالَمِ مِنَ الطَّبِيعِى أَجْسَامُ الْعَالَمِ مِنْ حَيْثُ لَهَا طَبِيعِيَّةٌ قَوْلٌ بِأَنَّ مَوْضُوعَهُمَا وَاحِدٌ لَكِنَّ اخْتِلافَهُمَا بِاخْتِلَافِ الْمَحْمُولِ ؛ لأَنَّ الْحَيْثِيَّةَ فِيهِمَا بَيَانُ البُحُوثِ عَنْهُ لَا أَنَّهَا جُزء الْمَوْضُوعِ وَإِلَّا يَلْزَمُ أَنْ لَا يُبْحَثُ فِيهِمَا عَنْ هَاتَيْنِ الْحَيْثِيَّتَيْنِ ، بَلْ عَمَّا يَلْحَقُهُمَا لِهَاتَينِ الْحَيْنِيَّتَيْنِ وَالْوَاقِعُ خِلَافَ ذَلِكَ ،

وَالله أَعْلَمُ. ترجمہ :۔ اور ان میں سے ایک (بحث) یہ ہے کہ بیشک مشہور یہ ہے کہ تحقیق شئی واحد نہیں ہو سکتی موضوع دو علموں کا میں کہتا ہوں کہ یہ منع نہیں ہے بلکہ واقع ہے کیونکہ ایک شئی کیلئے ہوتے ہیں مختلف متنوع اعراض پس ہر علم میں بحث کی جاتی ہے ان میں سے بعض سے جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا اور جزی نیست ہم نے کہا کہ بیشک مئی واحد کیلئے مختلف اعراض ہو سکتے ہیں کیونکہ واحد حقیقی کو موصوف کیا جاتا ہے صفات کثیرہ کے ساتھ اور نہیں ہے مضر یہ کہ ہوں ان (صفات ) میں سے بعض حقیقی اور بعض اضافی اور بعض صفات ایجابی اور بعض سلبی اور نہیں ہے کوئی شئی ان صفات میں سے جو لاحق ہو اس کو اس کے جز کی وجہ سے بوجہ
Movement and stillness: according to being the intermediate they are posterior, and according to being the intermediate they are prior. This is the precedence of a thing over itself. It is like fleeing from the rain and standing under the spout. And the famous [objection]... The well-known answer to this famous objection is that here the two things are separate: one is the essence of health and the essence of illness, and the other is the possibility of health and the possibility of illness. Similarly, one is the essence of motion, essence of rest, essence of shape, and the other is the possibility of motion, possibility of rest, and possibility of shape. When the matter is like this, then the aspect (haythiyya) which is the intermediate is the possibility of health, possibility of illness, possibility of motion, possibility of rest, possibility of shape, and the thing with the intermediate is the essence of health, essence of illness, essence of motion, essence of rest, and essence of shape. So the thing with the intermediate is one thing, and the intermediate is another; thus the precedence of a thing over itself does not necessarily arise.

Tahqiq: A statement of the investigative answer, the gist of which is that you misunderstood the meaning of qayd (condition). You said that qayd means that the essential attribute is established for the subject through the mediation of an aspect. This is wrong. Rather, the correct meaning is that in knowledge, the attributes that are investigated, at the time of discussing them, that aspect is taken into consideration. That is, it is a condition of the discussion. Subsequently, the attributes are general; their establishment may be mediated or unmediated in another sense. Here there are two things: one is that the aspect is a condition for the establishment of attributes, and the other is that the aspect is a condition for the discussion of the essential attributes. And this is the meaning of 'aspect of expression' (haythiyya bayaniyya). So the speech of the commentator returns to the speech of Sahib al-Tawdih, as if Sahib al-Talwih expressed the same meaning as Sahib al-Tawdih expressed. And Allah knows best.

And among them is that the famous (opinion) is that one thing cannot be the subject of two sciences. I say this is not impossible but rather occurs, because one thing can have diverse attributes, so in each science one investigates some of them, as we mentioned.

We only said that one thing can have diverse attributes because the truly one (al-wahid al-haqiqi) can be described with many attributes, and it does not harm that some of them are essential, some relational, some positive, and some negative. None of them attach to it due to a part (since it has no part), so the attachment of some of them must be due to its essence, to prevent infinite regress in the principle. Then the attachment of the other part, if it is due to its essence, that is what is sought; and if due to something else, we speak about that other until it ends at its essence, cutting off infinite regress in the principle.

And because it would require its completion from something else. When that is established, it is possible for one thing to be the subject of two sciences, and their distinction is according to the attributes investigated. That is because the definitions of the two sciences and their differences are according to the limits of the known things and their differences. The known things are the problems. Just as the problems become one and differ according to their subjects, and they refer to the subject of the science, likewise the problems become one and differ according to their predicates, and they refer to those attributes. If it is intended that the convention is that the subject is considered in that, not the predicate, then there is no disputation in that. Moreover, their statement: 'The subject of geometry is the bodies of the world insofar as they have shape, and the subject of celestial physics is the bodies of the world insofar as they have nature' is a statement that their subject is one, but their difference is by difference of the predicate, because the aspect in them is a statement of the investigation about it, not that it is a part of the subject. Otherwise, it would necessitate that they do not investigate in them about these two aspects, but rather about what attaches to them due to these two aspects, and the reality is contrary to that.

And Allah knows best. Translation: And among them (a discussion) is that indeed the famous (opinion) is that one thing cannot be the subject of two sciences. I say this is not prohibited but rather occurs, because one thing has various diverse attributes. So in each science, investigation is made about some of them, as we have mentioned. And we have not said that one thing cannot have diverse attributes because the truly one is described with many attributes, and it is not harmful that some of them are essential, some relational, some positive, and some negative. And there is no thing among these attributes that attaches to it due to its part because it has no part. So the attachment of some of them must be due to its essence to prevent infinite regress in the principle. So the attachment of the other, if it is due to its essence, that is what is sought, and if due to something else, we speak about that something else until it ends at its essence to prevent infinite regress in the principle. And because it would require its completion from something else. When that is established, it is possible for one thing to be the subject of two sciences and their distinction is according to the attributes investigated. That is because the definitions of the two sciences and their difference are according to the limits of the known things and their differences, and the known things are the problems. So just as the problems become one and differ according to their subjects and they refer to the subject of the science, likewise the problems become one and differ according to their predicates and they refer to those attributes. If it is intended that the convention is that the subject is considered in that, not the predicate, then there is no disputation in that. Moreover, their statement: 'The subject of geometry is the bodies of the world insofar as they have shape, and the subject of celestial physics is the bodies of the world insofar as they have nature' is a statement that their subject is one, but their difference is by difference of the predicate, because the aspect in them is a statement of the investigation about it, not that it is a part of the subject. Otherwise, it would necessitate that they do not investigate in them about these two aspects, but rather about what attaches to them due to these two aspects, and the reality is contrary to that. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute. The author begins by addressing a well-known objection regarding the precedence of a thing over itself, clarifying that the aspect (haythiyya) and the thing-with-aspect (dhu al-haythiyya) are distinct, so no self-precedence arises. He then moves to the main issue: the famous claim that one thing cannot be the subject (mawdu') of two sciences. The author rejects this, arguing it is not only possible but actual. His proof is rational: a truly single entity (al-wahid al-haqiqi) can possess multiple attributes—essential, relational, positive, negative—none of which attach due to a part (since it has no parts). Therefore, their attachment is to the essence itself, preventing infinite regress. Thus, the same essence can be the subject of different sciences, each investigating a different set of attributes. He supports this with the example of geometry and natural science (physics), which both study bodies of the world but from different aspects: shape and nature. The author emphasizes that the aspect (haythiyya) is not part of the subject but a qualification of the investigation. If conventional terminology restricts science definition to the subject alone, there is no dispute; but in reality, the predicate (attribute) also distinguishes sciences. The final Urdu translation summarizes the Arabic argument.

Key Terms
مَوْضُوع (mawdu'): The subject of a science, the thing about which the science investigates its essential attributes.
عَرَض ('arad): An attribute or accident that attaches to the subject; in this context, the diverse attributes that can be investigated in different sciences.
حَيْثِيَّة (haythiyya): An aspect or consideration under which something is investigated; the perspective that distinguishes one science from another.
وَاحِد حَقِيقِيّ (wahid haqiqi): A truly single entity with no parts, capable of multiple attributes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the main reason one thing can be the subject of two sciences?
A) Because the thing has parts that can be separated.
B) Because the thing can have multiple attributes, each investigated in a different science.
C) Because sciences are defined only by their subjects.
D) Because the subject must be a genus.

Key Takeaway
A single entity can be the subject of multiple sciences because it can possess diverse attributes, and sciences are distinguished by which attributes they investigate.

Rational Proof That Divine Attributes Are Essential Accidents
Proving divine attributes attach directly via rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply rational proof (dalil aqli) to establish that divine attributes attach directly to the Essence without mediation, and explain why mediation leads to absurdity.

Core Idea
Divine attributes must attach directly to the Essence; mediation leads to infinite regress or composition, both impossible.

This passage presents a rational proof defending the Maturidi-Hanafi position that divine attributes (sifat haqiqiyya) are essential accidents that inhere directly in the Essence. The argument systematically eliminates all possible forms of mediation, showing that only direct attachment is coherent. Understanding this proof is crucial for grasping the Hanafi usul principle that the subject matter of a science — here, the divine essence — has essential accidents that are investigated without intervening intermediaries.

Guided Path
1
Define the categories of attributes
Identify the four types of attributes mentioned: real (haqīqiyya), relational (iḍāfiyya), negative (salbiyya), and positive (ijābiyya). Understand that the proof focuses on real attributes, which are self-subsisting in intellection and existence.
Real attributes are those not needing another in conception or external existence; relational attributes need another only in external existence.
2
Pose the central question
The author asks whether real attributes attach to the Exalted (Bārī Taʿālā) directly or through an intermediary. This frames the entire proof.
3
Eliminate each possible intermediary
Consider each hypothetical intermediary: (a) a part of God (impossible because God is simple; would imply composition); (b) a disparate thing (would imply need for another, leading to contingency); (c) another attribute (would repeat the question, leading to infinite regress). Since all are impossible, direct attachment is necessary.
The argument uses reductio ad absurdum: if mediation existed, it leads to an impossibility, so the original premise (direct attachment) must hold.
4
Conclude and extend the proof
Conclude that real attributes attach directly, making them essential accidents. The same reasoning is applied to relational attributes. Finally, if the One God can have multiple types of essential accidents, then creatures can a fortiori (bi-ṭarīq al-ūlā).
The conclusion reinforces the Hanafi usul framework: the subject of a science is defined by its essential accidents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و خلق وغیرہ پھر ہر ایک کی دو قسمیں ہیں وجود یہ اور سلبیہ صفات حقیقیہ ان صفات کو کہتے ہیں کہ جو اپنے تعقل اور تصور میں اور تحقق في الخارج میں غیر کی محتاج نہ ہوں اور صفات اضافیہ کہ جن کا تعقل اور تصور میں تحقق تو غیر پر موقوف نہ ہو البتہ محقق فی الخارج غیر پر موقوف ہو مثلا واجب الوجود ہونا یہ تصور اور تعقل میں غیر کی محتاج نہیں ہے البتہ تحق في الخارج میں فرق کی محتاج ہے اور صفات سلبیہ وہ ہیں جس کی نفی کی جائے جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا جو ہر نہ ہونا عرض نہ ہونا صفات ایجابی وہ ہیں جن کو ثابت کیا گیا ہو باری تعالی کیلئے جیسے مالک ہونا رازق ہونا اب ہم صفات حقیقیہ کے بارے میں بحث کرتے ہیں کہ یہ صفات باری تعالی کو بلا واسطہ لاحق ہیں یا بالواسطہ اگر یہ صفات بلا واسطہ لاحق ہوں تو ہمارا مدعی ثابت ہو گیا کہ یہ عوارض ذاتیہ ہیں اور اگر یہ صفات بالواسطہ لاحق ہوں تو ہم پوچھتے ہیں کہ واسطہ باری تعالے کا جز ہوگا یا غیر ہو گا جز واسطہ نہیں بن سکتا کیونکہ باری تعالی تو بسیط محض ہیں اس سے باری تعالی کا مرکب ہونا لازم آئیگا اور اگر غیر جز واسطہ ہے تو دو حال سے خالی نہیں یا تو دوسری صفت واسطہ ہوگی یا امر مباین واسطہ ہوگا اب اگر واسطہ امر مباین ہو تو یہ بھی درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں اللہ تعالی کا اپنی صفات میں استعمال من الغیر لازم آئیگا اور میں تلزم ہے احتیاج الی الغیر کو اور احتیاج الی الغیر مستلزم ہے حدوث اور ممکن ہونے کو اور یہ باطل ہے اور اگر واسطہ کوئی صفت ہو تو پھر ہم اس کے بارے میں ایسے ہی بحث کریں گے کہ اگر وہ صفت باری تعالی کو بلا واسطہ لاحق ہے تو وہ عوارض ذاتیہ میں سے ہوگی اگر بالواسطہ لاحق ہوں تو دو حال سے خالی واسطہ امر مباین ہوگا یا کوئی اور صفت ہو گی یہ سلسلہ چلتا رہے گا تو یہ ستلزم تسلسل ہے جو کہ باطل ہے اب لا محالہ کہنا ہو گا کہ وہ صفت بلا واسطہ کے عارض ہے باری تعالی کو اور یہی ہمارا مدعی ہے اب ایسے ہی صفات اضافیہ کے بارے میں بحث کریں گے جیسے صفات حقیقیہ کے بارے میں بحث کی ہے تو یہ بھی باری تعالی کو بالذات لاحق ہونگی اب جب باری تعالی جو واحد حقیقی ہے اس کے عوارض ذاتیہ کے مختلف انواع ممکن ہیں تو مخلوق کیلئے عوارض ذاتیہ کی مختلف انواع بطریق اولی ممکن ہونگی۔
And creation etc. Then each has two types: affirmative and negative. Real attributes (sifāt haqīqiyya) are those that are not in need of another in their intellection, conception, and external existence. Relational attributes (sifāt iḍāfiyya) are those whose intellection and conception are not dependent on another, but their external existence is dependent on another, e.g., being Necessarily Existent – this is not in need of another in intellection and conception, but in external existence it is in need of distinction. Negative attributes are those that are negated, like the Exalted not being a substance or an accident. Positive attributes are those that are affirmed for the Exalted, like being Owner, Provider. Now we discuss real attributes: whether these attributes attach to the Exalted without mediation or with mediation. If they attach without mediation, our claim is proven that they are essential accidents. If they attach with mediation, we ask: Is the intermediary a part of the Exalted or other than a part? It cannot be a part, because the Exalted is pure simple, which would necessitate composition. If it is other than a part, it is either another attribute or a disparate thing. If it is a disparate thing, that is invalid because then the Exalted would be using something other than Himself in His attributes, which necessitates need for another, which necessitates contingency and possibility – and that is false. If the intermediary is an attribute, then we similarly discuss it: if that attribute attaches without mediation, it is among essential accidents; if with mediation, the intermediary is either a disparate thing or another attribute – this chain continues, necessitating infinite regress, which is false. So inevitably, we must say that the attribute attaches to the Exalted without mediation, and that is our claim. Similarly, we will discuss relational attributes as we discussed real attributes, so they too attach to the Exalted essentially. Now, since the Exalted, Who is the truly One, can have different types of essential accidents, then for creatures different types of essential accidents are a fortiori possible.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof establishing that divine attributes are essential accidents (ʿaraḍ dhātiyya) that directly attach to the Essence without mediation. The author first defines types of attributes: real (haqīqiyya), relational (iḍāfiyya), negative (salbiyya), and positive (ijābiyya). Then he focuses on real attributes and argues: if they attach directly, our claim is proven; if mediated, the intermediary must either be part of God (impossible because God is simple) or something else. If something else, it leads to regress or need for another, which is impossible. So they must attach directly. The same extension applies to relational attributes. Finally, he concludes that if God, the truly One, can have multiple types of essential accidents, then creatures can have them a fortiori.

Key Terms
عوارض ذاتیہ (aʿrāḍ dhātiyya): Essential accidents that directly attach to the subject without mediation; in this passage, they are the attributes that inhere in the essence.
صفات حقیقیہ (sifāt haqīqiyya): Real attributes that are self-subsisting and not dependent on another in conception or existence.
صفات اضافیہ (sifāt iḍāfiyya): Relational attributes whose intellection is independent but external existence depends on another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Divine attributes must inhere in the Essence directly; any mediation is rationally impossible.

Differentiation of Sciences by Essential Accidents
Addressing how two sciences can share one subject yet be distinct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that sciences can share a subject and be distinguished by essential accidents, using the example of astronomy and physics.

Core Idea
Sciences are distinguished by essential accidents, not solely by subject.

In this passage, the author addresses a key usul al-fiqh question: can two sciences share the same subject matter and still be considered distinct? The Hanafi position asserts that distinction arises not only from the subject (mawḍūʿ) but from the essential accidents (aʿrāḍ dhātiyya) studied. This principle is critical for understanding how usul al-fiqh relates to other Islamic sciences, and highlights the importance of the predicate (maḥmūl) in defining a science.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
The passage begins by framing the problem: if two sciences have the same subject, how are they distinguished? This sets up the debate between the Hanafi position and the opposing convention.
2
Understand the Hanafi claim
The author argues that the unity and difference of sciences rest on the unity and difference of their problems (masāʾil), which are determined by both subject and predicate. Since predicates are essential accidents, sciences can be distinguished by different types of essential accidents.
This is a key shift from the conventional view that the subject alone suffices for distinction.
3
Examine the proof: the example
The philosophers' example of astronomy (ʿilm al-hayʾa) and physics (ʿilm al-ṭabīʿī) is given. Both study celestial bodies (ajsām al-ʿālam), but astronomy studies them in terms of shapes (ashkāl) and physics in terms of nature (ṭabīʿ). Thus, they share a subject but differ in essential accidents.
This empirical example establishes actual occurrence, not just permissibility.
4
Recognize the opposing view
The opposing school (al-qawm) holds that sciences are distinguished solely by their subjects, based on the established convention (iṣṭilāḥ). The author acknowledges this convention but argues that reality and rational proof allow for distinction by accidents as well.
The Hanafi response does not deny the convention's utility but asserts a more fundamental principle.
5
Synthesize the ruling
The passage concludes with the Hanafi position: it is permissible (jāʾiz) and actually occurring (wāqiʿ) for multiple sciences to share one subject in essence, while being distinguished by different essential accidents. This is a deliberate departure from the opposing view.
This principle has implications for how we define and classify Islamic sciences, including usul al-fiqh.

Source Text

(واللہ اعلم بالصواب)۔ تلویح قَوْلُهُ ) وَمِنْهَا أَنَّ الْمَشْهُورَ) الْمَبْحَثُ الثَّالِثُ فِي جَوَازِ تَشَارُكِ الْعُلُومِ الْمُخْتَلِفَةِ فِي مَوْضُوعٍ وَاحِدٍ بِالذَّاتِ وَالاعْتِبَارِ وَ كَمَا خَالَفَ الْقَوْمَ فِي جَوَازِ تَعَدُّدِ الْمَوْضُوعِ لِعِلْمٍ وَاحِدٍ كَذَلِكَ خَالَفَهُمْ فِي امْتِنَاعِ الْحَادِ الْمَوْضُوعِ لِعُلُومَ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ وَادَّعَى جَوَازَهُ ، بَلْ وُقُوعَهُ أَمَّا الْجَوَازُ فَلَانَّهُ يَصِحُ أَنْ يَكُونَ لِشَيْءٍ وَاحِدٍ أَعْرَاضٌ
If two sciences have a single subject, how are they distinguished? And it is: - This is the answer to the implied question. Question: The distinction of sciences is by subject, so when both have a single subject, how are they distinguished? Answer: The unity and difference of sciences is based on the unity and difference of their problems. That is, if the problems are unified, the sciences are unified; if the problems differ, the sciences differ. The unity and difference of problems is established by the subject of the proposition as well as by the predicate. The predicate of the proposition is the essential accidents. So the distinction of sciences will be by essential accidents: one science discusses one type of essential accidents, and another science discusses another type. And if it is intended: - This is the answer to the implied question. Question: Brother, your proof that sciences are distinguished by predicate is correct, but what about the fact that the people have established the convention that sciences are distinguished by subject, not by predicate and essential accidents? Answer: The author said: Your convention is valid in its place, but the reality is that sciences can be distinguished by subject as well as by essential accidents. In external reality, two sciences have a single subject, as they say: - This is a proof for the second claim. The claim was that in external reality two sciences have a single subject. The philosophers say that the subject of astronomy is celestial bodies in terms of shapes – i.e., all bodies, spheres, and what is composed of them, in terms of their shapes like triangle, square, etc. So astronomy is an independent art; its subject is celestial bodies in terms of shapes. Physics has several types; one type is the science of the sky; its subject is also celestial bodies in terms of nature. Now astronomy's subject is celestial bodies and the science of the sky's subject is also celestial bodies – two sciences with a single subject, because both sciences discuss the same aspect. It is understood that the aspect is the expression of essential accidents. When the aspect is expressed, it falls outside the subject. When the aspect is outside, both sciences have one thing as subject, which is celestial bodies. The remaining distinction in sciences is by essential accidents: one science discusses one type of essential accidents (shapes) and the other science discusses another type (nature). So distinction is by that type. (And Allah knows best what is correct). Al-Talwih: His saying: 'And among them is that the well-known [view]' – the third inquiry concerning the permissibility of different sciences sharing one subject in essence and consideration. Just as he opposed the people regarding the permissibility of multiple subjects for one science, likewise he opposed them regarding the impossibility of a single subject for multiple sciences, and claimed its permissibility, rather its occurrence. As for permissibility, because it is sound for one thing to have [multiple] accidents.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage discusses the principle that sciences (ʿulūm) can be distinguished by their essential accidents even when they share the same subject. The author presents a question: if two sciences have the same subject, how are they distinguished? The answer: sciences are unified or differentiated by their problems (masāʾil), which are determined by both subject and predicate (maḥmūl). Since the predicates are essential accidents, sciences are differentiated by different types of essential accidents. The author then addresses an objection: the established convention (iṣṭilāḥ) is that sciences are distinguished by subject, not by accidents. The author argues that in reality, distinction can be by accidents as well, and gives the example of astronomy (ʿilm al-hayʾa) and physics (ʿilm al-ṭabīʿī), which both deal with celestial bodies (ajsām al-ʿālam) but from different aspects: astronomy by shapes (ashkāl) and physics by nature (ṭabīʿ). Thus, they share the same subject but differ in essential accidents. The Arabic excerpt from Al-Talwih confirms that the author opposes the view that multiple sciences cannot share one subject in essence and consideration, and asserts its permissibility and actual occurrence.

Key Terms
عوارض ذاتیہ (aʿrāḍ dhātiyya): Essential accidents that serve as predicates of the subject; the aspects by which sciences are distinguished.
موضوع (mawḍūʿ): The subject matter of a science; that which the science investigates in terms of its essential accidents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes astronomy (ʿilm al-hayʾa) from the science of the sky (ʿilm al-samāʾ)?
A) Their subjects are different.
B) They study different types of essential accidents.
C) They have different methods.
D) They are the same science.

Key Takeaway
Two sciences can share the same subject (mawḍūʿ) yet be distinct by studying different essential accidents (aʿrāḍ dhātiyya).

Rational Proof for Multiple Essential Attributes (A'radh Dhatiyya)
Expansion of a rational proof for multiple essential attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rational proof (dalil aqli) used in Hanafi usul to establish multiple essential attributes for a simple entity, and apply the principles that reject infinite regress (tasalsul) and usage of another (isti'mal min al-ghayr).

Core Idea
Attributes of a simple entity must attach either immediately or mediately; mediation leads to absurdity, so immediate attachment proves essential attributes.

In this passage, the commentator expands on the author's proof that a single entity (such as Allah) can have multiple essential attributes of different types. The proof proceeds by examining how attributes can attach to a simple being, eliminating impossible intermediaries, and concluding that immediate attachment is necessary. This rational argument (dalil aqli) is fundamental in Hanafi usul for establishing the reality of divine attributes without compromising tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting premise
The proof begins with the observation that an attribute attaches to an entity either immediately (without intermediary) or mediately (through an intermediary).
This dichotomy is exhaustive for a simple entity.
2
Analyze the possible intermediaries
If mediately, the intermediary must be either (a) a part of the entity, (b) a separate entity (amr mubayin), or (c) another attribute. Each possibility is examined.
For Allah, having parts is impossible (He is basit).
3
Apply Hanafi theological principles
A part is impossible for a simple being. A separate entity would imply that Allah uses something other than Himself (isti'mal min al-ghayr), which is impossible because it indicates need and deficiency.
Allah is ghani (self-sufficient).
4
Eliminate possibilities leading to absurdity
If the intermediary is another attribute, then that attribute itself must attach either immediately or mediately, leading to infinite regress (tasalsul) if mediation continues. Infinite regress is absurd.
Thus, infinite regress is rejected in Hanafi kalam.
5
Conclude immediate attachment for some attributes
Since all mediated options lead to impossibility, at least one attribute must attach immediately. This immediate attachment makes that attribute an essential attribute ('arad dhati).
This establishes the existence of essential attributes.
6
Extend to multiple attributes via two principles
First: any attribute that attaches through an essential attribute is itself essential. Second: when the locus is one, difference in attributes is typal (naw'i), not individual (shakhsi). Thus multiple essential attributes of different types are possible.
Example: hearing, sight, speech in a single person are typally different.

Source Text

نوع واحد کے اشخاص کا اختلاف جز این نیست محلوں کے اختلاف کے ساتھ ہوتا ہے۔

قولہ ولانہ: اس کا عطف ہے کلام سابق کے مضمون پر ہے یعنی اگر وہ (لحوق) اس کے غیر کی وجہ سے ہو پس وہ باطل ہے کیونکہ میں ستلزم ہے تسلسل کو اور کیونکہ یہ تلزم ہے واحد حقیقی کے اپنی صفات میں غیر سے استعمال کو اور وہ محال ہے کیونکہ یہ ثابت کرتا ہے نقصان کو اس کی ذات میں اور احتیاج کو اس کے کمالات میں اور اس میں نظر ہے کیونکہ اگر مراد لیا جائے استعمال سے امر مباین تو ظاہر ہے کہ وہ لازم نہیں آتا بوجہ جائز ہونے اس بات کے کہ ہو لاحق ہونا بعض دوسری صفات کا کسی صفت کی وجہ سے اور اگر مراد لیا جائے عام امر مبائین سے اور صفت سے تو ہم تسلیم نہیں کرتے کہ بے شک احتیاج بعض صفات کا بعض کی طرف ثابت کرتا ہے نقصان کو ذات میں اور کیسے ثابت کریگا؟ حالانکہ صفت خلق موقوف ہے علم اور قدرت اور ارادہ پر اور مکن ہے کہ بنایا جائے اس کو شخص اس کے ساتھ جب ہو غیر امر مبائین اور ماسبق (مختص) ہو اس کے ساتھ جب نہ ہو وہ غیر امر مبانین پس نام ہو جائیگا ان دونوں امور کے مجموعہ سے مطلوب یعنی دوسرے عرض ذاتی کو ثابت کرنا۔

فی واحد کے لئے مختلفة الانواع اعراض ذاتیہ کے ممکن ہونے پر دلیل

قولہ انما قلنا: اس عبارت میں شاریخ نے متن کی وضاحت کی ہے ماتن نے فرمایا تھا کہ شئی واحد کیلئے مختلفة الانواع اعراض ذاتیہ ہو سکتے ہیں اس کی دلیل دی تھی اس کی وضاحت کرتے ہیں کہ باری تعالی ذاتا و اعتبارا ایک ہیں ان کی مختلف صفات ہیں بعض حقیقی اور بعض صفاتی بعض ایجابی اور بعض سلبی یعنی مختلف صفات باری تعالی کیلئے ثابت ہیں اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ بعض صفات مثلا صفات ایجابید اللہ تعالی کو جو لاحق ہیں بالواسطہ یا بلا واسطہ اگر بلا واسطہ لاحق ہیں تو مطلوب ثابت ہوا کہ یہ صفات اعراض ذاتی ہوئیں اور اگر بالواسطہ لاحق ہیں تو واسطہ باری تعالی کا جز ہوگا یا جز نہیں ہوگا اگر واسطہ جز ہو تو یہ باطل ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالی بسیط ہیں اگر جز نہیں ہے تو پھر غیر واسطہ ہوگا تو پھر وہ غیر دو حال سے خالی نہیں غیر امر مبانین ہوگا یا صفت آخر ہوگی اگر غیر امر مباین ہو تو باری تعالی کا استعمال من بغیر لازم آئیگا اور اگر واسطہ صفت آخر ہو تو پھر اس صفت کے بارے میں بحث کریں گے کہ وہ صفت بلا واسطہ لاحق ہو تو عرض ذاتی ثابت ہوا اور اگر بالواسطہ لاحق ہو تو واسطہ جڑ ہوگا یہ باطل ہے۔ اور اگر واسطہ غیر ہو کر امر مبائین ہو تو استعمال من الخیر والی خرابی لازم آئیگی اور اگر واسطہ صفت آخر ہو تو پھر اس صفت کے بارے میں ایسے ہی بحث کریں تو یہ ستلزم تسلسل ہے جو کہ باطل ہے اب ضرور کہیں نہ کہیں جا کر کہنا پڑے گا کہ یہ صفات بلا واسطہ لاحق ہیں اور یہی ہمارا مطلوب ہے تو اللہ تعالی کیلئے ایک عرض ذاتی ثابت ہو گیا یہ بحث تو ایجابی صفات کے بارے میں تھی ایسے ہی صفات سلبیہ کے بارے میں بھی بحث کریں گے تو وہی تفصیل ہوگی جو ابھی کر دی ہے تو اب دوسرا عرض ذاتی ثابت ہو گیا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ واحد حقیقی جس کا کوئی شریک نہیں ہے اس کیلئے مختلف انواع اعراض ذاتیہ ثابت ہو سکتے ہیں تو غیر کیلئے تو بطریق اولی ثابت ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اعتراض: ماتن نے جو دلیل دی ہے اس میں امر مباین کا ذکر نہیں ہے صرف اتنا کہا کہ یہ صفات جز کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں گے یا غیر کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں گے امر مباین کا ذکر نہیں کیا حالانکہ اس کا ذکر ضروری تھا کیونکہ اس کے بغیر دلیل نام نہیں ہوتی؟

جواب: ماتن کی عادت ہے کہ اکثر اوقات اشارہ سے کام لیتے ہیں مختصر یہ کہ اگر چہ مائن نے صراحتہ تذکرہ نہیں کیا امر مباین کا لیکن ضمنا تذکرہ کیا ہے کیونکہ مائن نے دلیل میں کہا ہے کہ یہ صفات غیر کے واسطہ سے لاحق نہیں ہوسکتیں وہ نہ استعمال من الغیر یا تسلسل لازم آئیگا تو استمال من المشیر اسی وقت لازم آتا ہے جب غیر امر بابین ہو۔

جو چیز عرض ذاتی کے واسطے سے لاحق ہو وہ بھی عرض ذاتی ہوتی ہے

فان قبیل: اعتراض کر کے خود اس کا جواب دیا۔
سوال: یہ ہے کہ اس دلیل سے باری تعالی کیلئے مختلف اعراض ذاتیہ ثابت نہیں ہوتے ایک عرض ذاتی ثابت ہوتا ہے اگر مختلف ثابت ہوں تو پھر تعد واعراض ذاتیہ تو ثابت ہو گا مختلف انواع ہونا ثابت نہیں ہوگا حالانکہ مقصود اعراض کی مختلف انواع کو ثابت کرتا ہے اور یہ ثابت نہیں ہوتا آپ نے کہا کہ اللہ تعالی کی بعض صفات اللہ کو بالذات لاحق ہیں کیونکہ جز یا غیر کے واسطہ سے لاحق نہیں ہو سکتیں تو ایک عرض ذاتی ثابت ہو گیا اب ہم کہتے ہیں کہ باقی صفات اس عرض ذاتی کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہیں تو وہ بھی اسی واسطہ کے حکم میں ہیں اور اگر مان لیں کہ تمام صفات بالذات بلا واسطہ لاحق ہیں تو تعدد ثابت ہوگا تا کہ عوارض کا مختلف الانواع ہونا۔

جواب: ضابطہ ہے کہ جو چیز عرض ذاتی کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہو وہ بھی عرض ذاتی ہوتی ہے اب آپ ایک صفت کو مانتے ہیں کہ یہ عرض ذاتی ہے باقی اس کے واسطہ سے جو لاحق ہوں گی تو وہ بھی عرض ذاتی ہوں گی اور دوسری شق کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ضابطہ ہے کہ اگر محل ایک ہو اور صفات میں اختلاف ہو تو یہ اختلاف نومی ہوتا ہے مثلا زید کے ساتھ سمع بصر اور تکلم یہ اختلاف نوعی ہے کیونکہ محل ایک ہے تو اس صورت میں اختلاف شخصی نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر اختلاف شخصی ہو تو محل مختلف ہوگا جیسے بیاض جو زید کے ساتھ پایا جاتا ہے اور عمر کے ساتھ تو یہ اختلاف شخص ہے حالانکہ یہاں محل یعنی اللہ تعالی واحد ہیں اور اگر اختلاف شخص ما نہیں تو
The disagreement of individuals of one type is not but with the disagreement of loci. 

His saying: 'And because it': This is connected to the meaning of the previous statement, i.e., if that (attachment) is due to another, then it is invalid because it necessitates infinite regress, and because it necessitates the Real One using another in His attributes, and that is impossible because it proves deficiency in His essence and need in His perfections. And there is scrutiny in this because if by 'using' is meant a separate matter, then it is clear that it is not necessary due to the permissibility of some other attributes attaching by means of an attribute. And if by 'using' is meant a general separate matter and an attribute, then we do not concede that need of some attributes for others proves deficiency in essence. How could it prove that, while the attribute of creation depends on knowledge, power, and will? And it is possible to base the person on that when there is a separate matter, and the previous is specific to him when there is no separate matter. So the desired result, i.e., proving another essential attribute, will be achieved from the combination of these two matters.

Proof for the possibility of different types of essential attributes for a single entity

His saying: 'We only say': In this phrase, the commentator has explained the text. The author had stated that different types of essential attributes are possible for a single entity and had given a proof. He explains it: The Most High, in essence and in consideration, is one. He has different attributes, some real and some attributive, some positive and some negative, i.e., different attributes are established for the Most High. Now we say: Some attributes, for example the positive attributes of Allah, are attached to Him either mediately or immediately. If they are attached immediately, then the desired is proven, that these attributes are essential attributes. And if they are attached mediately, then the intermediary will be a part of the Most High or not. If the intermediary is a part, this is invalid because the Most High is simple. If it is not a part, then it will be an intermediary other than Him, and that 'other' is not free from two states: it will be a separate matter or another attribute. If it is a separate matter, then the Most High's using something other would be necessary. And if the intermediary is another attribute, then we will discuss about that attribute: if that attribute is attached immediately, then an essential attribute is proven; and if it is attached mediately, then the intermediary will be a root, this is invalid. And if the intermediary is an other than Him being a separate matter, then the corruption of using the other is necessary. And if it is another attribute, then we will discuss about that attribute similarly, so this necessitates infinite regress, which is invalid. Now it must be said somewhere that these attributes are attached immediately, and this is what we desire. So one essential attribute is proven for the Most High. This discussion was about positive attributes. Similarly, we will discuss negative attributes, and the same detail will apply as was given now. So now a second essential attribute is proven. The summary is that for the Real One, who has no partner, different types of essential attributes can be proven. So for other than Him, they can be proven by a fortiori. 

Objection: In the proof given by the author, there is no mention of a separate matter. He only said that these attributes will attach through a part or through an other. He did not mention a separate matter, although its mention was necessary because without it the proof is not complete. 

Answer: It is the habit of the author that often he works with allusion. In short, although the author did not explicitly mention the separate matter, he did mention it implicitly, because the author said in the proof that these attributes cannot attach through an other, otherwise using the other or infinite regress would be necessary. So using the other is only necessary when the other is a separate matter.

Whatever attaches through an essential attribute is also an essential attribute.

Then he said: He raised an objection and answered it himself. 

Question: From this proof, different essential attributes for the Most High are not proven; only one essential attribute is proven. If they are different, then multiplicity of essential attributes is proven, but being of different types is not proven. Yet the objective is to prove different types of attributes, and this is not proven. You said that some attributes of Allah attach to Him per se because they cannot attach through a part or an other, so one essential attribute is proven. Now we say that the remaining attributes attach through this essential attribute, so they fall under the same ruling. And if we concede that all attributes attach per se without intermediary, then multiplicity is proven, but that the accidents are of different types is not. 

Answer: The principle is that whatever attaches through an essential attribute is also an essential attribute. Now you concede that one attribute is an essential attribute; the remaining attributes that attach through it will also be essential attributes. And the answer to the other part is: The principle is that if the locus is one and there is difference in attributes, this is a typal difference. For example, hearing, sight, and speech with respect to Zayd: this is a typal difference because the locus is one. In this case, there is no individual difference, because if there were individual difference, the locus would be different, like whiteness found with Zayd and with Amr: this is an individual difference. But here the locus, i.e., the Most High, is one, and there is no individual difference.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage presents a rational proof (dalil aqli) for the possibility of multiple essential attributes (a'radh dhatiyya) of different types inhering in a single entity (al-wahid al-haqiqi), specifically using the example of Allah's attributes. The author first explains the proof given in the matn (original text): if an attribute attaches to an entity mediately, the intermediary must be either a part of the entity or something other than it. For Allah, having parts is impossible (He is basit, simple). If the intermediary is something other than Allah, it must be either a separate entity (amr mubayin) or another attribute. If it is a separate entity, then Allah would be using something separate, which is impossible. If it is another attribute, then we ask about that attribute: does it attach immediately or mediately? If immediately, it is an essential attribute; if mediately, we face infinite regress (tasalsul). Thus, to avoid regress, we must conclude that some attributes attach immediately (without intermediary), establishing at least one essential attribute. The same reasoning applies to negative attributes, establishing a second essential attribute. The proof is then defended against an objection that the author did not explicitly mention 'separate entity' (amr mubayin) in the proof; the response is that it is implied. Finally, a second objection is raised: the proof only establishes one essential attribute, not multiple types. The response invokes two principles: (1) whatever attaches through an essential attribute is also an essential attribute, so attributes mediated by the first essential attribute are themselves essential; and (2) when the locus (mahall) is one, differences in attributes are typal (naw'i), not individual (shakhsi), as exemplified by hearing, sight, and speech in a single person. Thus, multiple essential attributes of different types are possible. This argument is foundational in Hanafi kalam and usul for establishing the reality of divine attributes without compromising tawhid.

Key Terms
عرض ذاتی ('arad dhati): An attribute that attaches to an entity not through a part or a separate other, but immediately or through another essential attribute.
واحد حقیقی (wahid haqiqi): The truly one entity that has no parts, partners, or composition; here referring to Allah.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Infinite regress of causes or intermediaries, considered logically absurd in this proof.
استعمال من الغیر (isti'mal min al-ghayr): Using something other than oneself; considered impossible for Allah as it implies need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the proof in this passage, what is the consequence if an attribute of Allah were to attach through a separate entity (amr mubayin)?
A) It would prove multiplicity in Allah's essence.
B) It would necessitate infinite regress.
C) It would imply that Allah uses something other than Himself, which is impossible.
D) It would prove that attributes are not essential.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof that attributes must attach immediately to a simple entity establishes essential attributes, and the principles of mediation and typal difference allow for multiple essential attributes of different types.

Analyzing the Hanafi Refutation of Istikmal min al-Ghayr in Divine Attributes
Responding to an objection about divine attributes needing completion from another

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to dissect a rational argument (dalil aqli) regarding divine attributes, identify the logical defects proposed, and explain the Hanafi position that attributes are neither externally completed nor entail infinite regress.

Core Idea
Allah's attributes are not derived from another; their interdependence does not imply deficiency.

This passage deals with a kalām objection: if Allah's attributes are said to attach through an intermediary (ghayr), then either infinite regress (tasalsul) or completion from another (istikmal min al-ghayr) becomes necessary. The author clarifies the meaning of 'ghayr' and defends the Hanafi Ashʿarī position that attributes are self-subsisting yet interdependent. This is a classic exercise in usul al-fiqh as applied to theological propositions, using rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
State the objection: that if Allah's attributes were to be attached through an intermediary (ghayr), two defects would follow.
2
Distinguish the two defects
The defects are infinite regress (tasalsul) and completion from another (istikmal min al-ghayr). Understand each: tasalsul means an endless chain; istikmal means deriving perfection externally.
3
Clarify the term 'ghayr'
Analyze what 'ghayr' means: distinct entity (amr mubayin) or another attribute. The objection assumes a specific meaning, but the author shows that if it means another attribute, tasalsul results; if a distinct entity, istikmal results – but neither applies to Allah.
4
Examine the response
The response argues that attributes are interdependent (like creation depends on knowledge) without needing an external source. Thus the objection fails because 'ghayr' cannot cause a defect when attributes are inherent to the Divine Essence.
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh reasoning
This analysis shows how a rational argument (dalil aqli) is structured in Hanafi usul: identifying a claim, its logical consequences, clarifying terms, and refuting by showing the consequence does not follow.
This is a method of istinbat for theological propositions.

محل کے تعدد کی وجہ سے ابطال توحید لازم آئیگا تو پتہ چلا باری تعالی کی صفات مختلف الانواع نہیں ۔ (واللہ اعلم بالصواب) تشریح : قولہ ولانہ : متن میں ہے ولا نہ ملزم استکمالہ اس کی شاریخ نے ترکیب بیان کی ہے کہ اس جملے کا ماقبل والے جملہ کے مضمون پر عطف ہے اور وہ مضمون یہ ہے کہ اگر صفات اللہ کو غیر کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں تو تسلسل لازم آئیگا یا تو اس مضمون پر عطف ہے والا نہ ملزم استعمالہ من غیرہ کا اب معنی یہ ہوگا اگر صفات اللہ کولاحق ہوں غیر کے واسطہ سے تو تسلسل لازم آئے گا یا استکمال من الغیر لازم آئے گا۔
استکمال من الغیر میں غیر سے کیا مراد ہے؟
وفیہ نظر :۔ غیر کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں تو دو خرابیاں لازم آتی ہیں تسلسل یا استعمال من الغیر ۔ سوال:۔ یہ ہے کہ استعمال من الغیر سے کیا مراد ہے؟ اگر غیر سے امر مباین مراد ہو تو پھر امر منفصل سے استعمال من الغير پایا جائیگا اور یہ حال ہے لیکن یہ لازم نہیں آتا اس لئے کہ ہو سکتا ہے کہ ثبوت کسی صفت آخر کی وجہ سے ہو اور اگر غیر میں تقسیم ہے یعنی امر منفصل ہو یا صفت آخر تو ہر دو صورتوں میں استعمال من الغیر لازم نہیں آتا کیونکہ صفات باری تعالٰی ایک دوسرے کی طرف محتاج ہوتی ہیں اور یہ احتیاج و نقصان استعمال من الخیر کو ستلزم نہیں ہے جیسے خلق موقوف ہے علم پر اور قدرت ارادے پر موقوف ہے لیکن اس سے کوئی نقصان لازم نہیں آتا۔
جواب دیا کہ غیر سے مراد عام ہے امر مبائین یا صفات تو اگر صفات صفات کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں تو مسلسل والی خرابی لازم آئیگی اور اگر امر مباین کے واسطہ سے لاحق ہوں تو استعمال من الغیر والی خرابی سے لازم آئیگی۔
Due to multiplicity of locus, the nullification of oneness would be necessary, so it becomes clear that the attributes of Allah are not of different types. (And Allah knows best the correct answer) Commentary: His statement 'And it does not necessitate his completion': In the text it is 'ولا نہ ملزم استکمالہ'. The commentators have explained the syntax: this clause is coordinated with the content of the preceding clause. That content is: if the attributes of Allah are attached through an intermediary of other, then infinite regress becomes necessary. Or it is coordinated with that content and 'ولا نہ ملزم استعمالہ من غیرہ' now the meaning becomes: if the attributes of Allah are attached through an intermediary of other, then either infinite regress becomes necessary, or completion from other becomes necessary.
What is meant by 'ghayr' in istikmal min al-ghayr?
And there is consideration: If they are attached through an intermediary of other, two defects become necessary: infinite regress or completion from other. Question: What is meant by completion from other? If by 'other' a distinct entity is meant, then completion from other through a separate thing is found, and this is the case, but it is not necessary because it is possible that the establishment is due to another attribute. And if by 'other' there is division, i.e., a separate thing or another attribute, then in both cases completion from other is not necessary because the attributes of Allah Exalted are need of each other, and this need and deficiency does not necessitate completion from other, just as creation is dependent on knowledge and power is dependent on will, but no deficiency becomes necessary from that.
Answer: That by 'other' is meant general, either a distinct entity or attributes. So if attributes are attached through an intermediary of attributes, then the defect of infinite regress becomes necessary; and if they are attached through an intermediary of a distinct entity, then the defect of completion from other becomes necessary.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a textual analysis addressing an objection regarding the divine attributes. The author explains a statement from the matn: 'ولا نہ ملزم استکمالہ' (and it does not necessitate His completion). The commentators parse this as being coordinated with the preceding clause, which states that if Allah's attributes were to attach through an intermediary (other than Himself), then either infinite regress (tasalsul) or completion from another (istikmal min al-ghayr) would be necessary. The author then raises a question: What exactly is meant by 'ghayr' (other) in the context of istikmal min al-ghayr? If 'ghayr' refers to a distinct entity (amr mubayin), then completion from a separate thing would occur, but this is not necessarily a defect because the attribute could be established through another attribute. If 'ghayr' is general and includes both distinct entities and other attributes, then the scenario where an attribute attaches through another attribute leads to infinite regress, while attaching through a distinct entity leads to completion from another. The response clarifies that the objection does not hold because the attributes of Allah are interdependent—e.g., creation depends on knowledge, power depends on will—without implying any deficiency or need for completion from an external source. Thus, the initial objection is refuted using rational argument (dalil aqli).

Key Terms
استکمال من الغیر (istikmal min al-ghayr): Completion from other than itself; the concept that an entity derives perfection from an external source.
تسلسل (tasalsul): Infinite regress; an endless chain of causes.
غیر (ghayr): Other; that which is distinct from the entity in question. In this passage, it encompasses both another attribute and a separate entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two defects are mentioned as possible consequences if Allah's attributes are attached through an intermediary (ghayr)?
A) Infinite regress (tasalsul) and completion from another (istikmal min al-ghayr)
B) Anthropomorphism (tashbih) and denial (ta'til)
C) Innovation (bid'ah) and division (tajziyah)
D) Necessity (wujub) and impossibility (imtina')

Key Takeaway
Allah's attributes are interdependent without need for external completion, avoiding both infinite regress and istikmal.

Can the Shakhsi Be Defined? A Hanafi Usul Refinement
Analyzing whether a shakhsi can be defined logically

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on defining a shakhsi and evaluate the logical arguments for and against definitional possibility.

Core Idea
A shakhsi can be defined by its existential distinction, even if its individual essence requires pointing.

Defining unique individuals (shakhsiyat) might seem impossible because each individual is known only by pointing or proper names. Yet Hanafi usul engages with this question deeply, as it affects how we define unique entities like the Quran. This lesson walks through the dialectical argument from al-Talwih, examining objections and refinements until the final sound position emerges.

Guided Path
1
State the problem
Recognize the central question: can a shakhsi (an individual particular) be given a logical definition (hadd)? The passage begins by quoting the claim that it cannot.
The initial claim: knowledge of a shakhsi is only by pointing or proper names; definition deals with universals.
2
Analyze the objection
The objector argues that a shakhsi is a composite consideration (murakkab i'tibari) of essence and individuality, so it can be defined by a definition covering both.
This challenges the initial claim by expanding what a definition can include.
3
Examine the rebuttal on accidental characteristics
The opponent further argues that if the definition includes accidental distinguishing features, they may change, making the definition unstable. The response shows that when accidents cease, the defined shakhsi also ceases, so the definition remains valid.
This is the critical refinement: the definition holds as long as the shakhsi exists.
4
Distinguish existential vs. cognitive distinction
The final position (al-haqq) clarifies: a shakhsi can be defined by what distinguishes it existentially (tamyiz wujudi) from all other things, but not by what specifies its individuality (which requires pointing).
This is the nuanced Hanafi view: definition can achieve differentiation, not exhaustive individuation.
5
Apply to usul al-fiqh
Consider the Quran as a shakhsi. Using this rule, it can be defined as 'the miraculous speech of Allah revealed to Muhammad' — a definition that distinguishes it from all other speech.
This shows practical utility in defining unique shar'i entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلویح قَوْلُهُ ) عَلَى أَنَّ الشَّخْصِيَّ لَا يُحَدُّ ) وَلِأَنَّ مَعْرِفَتَهُ لَا تَحْصُلُ إِلَّا بِتَعْيِينِ مُشَخْصَاتِهِ بِالْإِشَارَةِ أَوْ نَحْوِهَا كَالتَّعْبِيرِ عَنْهُ بِاسْمِهِ الْعَلَمِ وَالْحَدُّ لَا يُفِيدُ ذَلِكَ ؛ لأنْ غَايَتَهُ الحَدُّ التَّامُ ، وَهُوَ إِنَّمَا يَشْتَمِلُ عَلَى مُقَوِّمَاتِ الشَّيْء دُونَ مُشَخْصَاتِهِ وَلِقَائِلٍ أَنْ يَقُولَ الشَّخْصِيُّ مُرَكَّبٌ اعْتِبَارِيٌّ ، وَهُوَ مَجُمُوعُ الْمَاهِيَّةِ وَالنَّشَخْصِ فَلِمَ لَا يَجُوزُ أَنْ يُحَدَّ بِمَا يُفِيدُ مَعْرِفَةَ الْأَمْرَيْنِ لَا يُقَالُ تَعْرِيفُ الْمُرَكَّبِ الِاعْتِبَارِى لَفْظِيٌّ وَالْكَلَامُ فِي الْحَدّ الْحَقِيقِيّ ؛ لأنَّا نَقُولُ لَوْ سُلّمَ ذَلِكَ فَمَجُمُوعُ الْقُرْآنِ مُرَكَّبٌ اعْتِبَارِيٌّ لَا مَحَالَةَ فَحِينَئِذٍ لَا حَاجَةَ إِلَى سَائِرِ الْمُقَدَّمَاتِ وَلَا إِلَى مَا ذَكَرَ فِي تَشْخِيصِهِ مِنَ التَّكَلُفَاتِ ، وَقَدْ يُقَالُ إِنْ اقْتَصَرَ فِي تَعْرِيفِ الشَّخْصِي عَلَى مُقَوِّمَاتِ الْمَاهِيَّةِ لَمْ يَخْتَصَّ بِالشَّخْصِي فَلَمْ يُفِدُ التَّمُسِيرُ الَّذِى هُوَ أَقَلُّ مَرَاتِبِ التَّعْرِيفِ ، وَإِنْ ذَكَرَ مَعَهَا الْعَرَضِيَّاتِ الْمُشَخْصَةَ أَيْضًا لَمْ يَجِبُ دَوَامُ صِدْقِهَا لِإِمْكَانِ زَوَالِهَا فَلا يَكُونُ حَدًا ، وَفِيهِ نَظَرٌ لِجَوَازِ أَنْ يَذْكُرَ مَعَهَا الْعَرَضِيَّاتِ المُشَخْصَةَ وَعِندَ زَوَالِهَا يَزُولُ الْمَحْدُودُ أَيْضًا أَعْنِي ذَلِكَ الشَّخْصِيَّ فَلا يَضُرُّ عَدَمُ صِدْقِ الحَدٌ ، بَلْ يَجِبُ : وَالْحَقُّ أَنَّ الشَّخْصِيَّ يُمْكِنُ أَنْ يُحَدَّ بِمَا يُفِيدُ امْتِيَازَهُ عَنْ جَمِيعِ مَا عَدَاهُ بِحَسْبِ الْوُجُودِ لَا بِمَا يُفِيدُ تَعَيَّنَهُ وَتَشَخَّصَهُ بِحَيْثُ لَا يُمْكِنُ اشْتِرَاكُهُ بَيْنَ كَثِيرِينَ بِحَسَبِ الْعَقْلِ فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ إِنَّمَا يَحْصُلُ بِالْإِشَارَةِ لَا غَيْرُ . ترجمہ: قوله على ان الشخصى لايحد کیونکہ اس (شخصی) کی معرفت نہیں حاصل ہوتی مگر اس کی خصوصیات کو متعین کرنے کے ساتھ اشارے سے یا اس کی مثل سے جیسا کہ تعبیر کرنا اس کو اس کے اسم علم کے ساتھ اور حد نہیں فائدہ دیتی اس کا کیونکہ غایت (حد) کی وہ حد نام ہے اور جز این نیست کہ وہ مشتمل ہوتی ہے مئی کے اجزاء پر نہ کہ خصوصیات پر۔ اور کہنے والے کے لئے جائز
Talwih: His saying 'that the shakhsi is not defined' — because its knowledge is only attained by specifying its distinguishing characteristics through pointing or the like, such as expressing it by its proper name. And definition does not provide that because its ultimate is the perfect definition, which only includes the essential constituents of a thing, not its distinguishing characteristics. And an objector may say: the shakhsi is a composite consideration, a combination of essence and individuality, so why is it not permissible to define it by what provides knowledge of both? It is not said that the definition of a composite consideration is verbal, while the discussion is about real definition, because we say: if that is granted, then the entirety of the Quran is necessarily a composite consideration, so then there is no need for all the premises nor for the artificialities mentioned in its specification. And it may be said: if one confines the definition of the shakhsi to the essential constituents of the essence, it would not be specific to the shakhsi, so it would not provide the demarcation which is the lowest level of definition. And if one mentions along with them the accidental distinguishing characteristics, their persistent truth is not necessary due to the possibility of their removal, so it would not be a definition. And there is a critical examination: because it is permissible to mention along with them the accidental distinguishing characteristics, and when they are removed, the defined also ceases, meaning that particular shakhsi, so the lack of truth of the definition does not harm, rather it is necessary. And the truth is that the shakhsi can be defined by what provides its distinction from all other things in terms of existence, not by what provides its specification and individuation such that it cannot be shared among many according to reason, for that is only achieved by pointing, no other. Translation: 'His saying that the shakhsi is not defined' because its knowledge is only attained by specifying its distinguishing characteristics with a sign or the like, like expressing it by its proper name. And a definition does not provide that because the utmost (of definition) is the perfect definition, which is nothing but includes the essential parts of the thing, not the characteristics. And for the one who says, it is permissible...
Source pages p. 453

Commentary
This passage from al-Talwih engages in a rigorous usul debate about whether a shakhsi (an individual particular) can be defined. It begins by quoting the claim that a shakhsi cannot be defined because it is known only by pointing or by proper names, whereas a definition (hadd) only comprises essential constituents (muqawwimat). The objector argues that a shakhsi is a composite of essence and individuality, so it should be definable by a definition that includes both. The response counters that such a definition would be merely verbal (lafzi), not real (haqiqi), because if extended to the Quran, it would reduce the need for elaborate specification. Another argument holds that if the definition includes only essential constituents, it fails to single out the shakhsi; if it includes accidental characteristics, those may change and the definition would no longer hold. The rejoinder points out that when the accidental characteristics change, the shakhsi itself ceases to exist, so the definition is still valid. The final position (al-haqq) is that a shakhsi can indeed be defined by what distinguishes it from all else in existence, but only in terms of its existential distinctness, not its cognitive individuality which requires pointing. This discussion is crucial for understanding the Hanafi approach to defining terms in usul al-fiqh, especially the Quran and other unique entities.

Key Terms
شخصی (shakhsi): An individual particular that exists concretely and is distinguished from all other individuals by its unique characteristics.
حد تام (hadd tam): A complete definition that includes the essential constituents (muqawwimat) of a thing, sufficient for distinguishing it from others in essence.
مركب اعتباري (murakkab i'tibari): A composite that is mentally constructed by combining essential and accidental aspects, not a simple entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Talwih passage, what is the correct position on defining a shakhsi?
A) A shakhsi can never be defined in any way.
B) A shakhsi can be defined by what distinguishes it existentially from all others.
C) A shakhsi can only be defined by its essential constituents.
D) A shakhsi can only be pointed to, not defined.

Key Takeaway
A shakhsi can be defined by its existential distinction, even if its individuality is only known by pointing.

Why an Individual Cannot Be Defined by a Real Definition
Argues that an individual cannot be defined by a real definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a real definition (hadd haqiqi) cannot be applied to a specific individual (shakhs) and distinguish between real and verbal definitions in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A real definition consists only of universal essential components; an individual's accidental properties cannot define its quiddity.

In Hanafi usul, the question of whether a specific individual like Zaid can be given a real definition touches upon the nature of definition itself. This passage from Al-Tarwih argues that a real definition, composed solely of genus and differentia, applies universally and cannot capture the unique identity of an individual. The commentator presents the reasoning, addresses objections, and clarifies the distinction between real and verbal definitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Recognize that the author asserts a shakhs cannot be defined by a hadd haqiqi. The commentator then provides the logical basis.
The claim is not about naming or pointing, but about definition that reveals quiddity.
2
Analyze the components of a real definition
Understand that a real definition consists solely of essential components (jins and fasl). It must apply universally to all individuals of that species.
For example, 'rational animal' applies to every human, not just Zaid.
3
Examine the role of accidental properties
Accidental properties (color, height) distinguish individuals but are not essential. Including them makes the definition verbal (lafzi), not real.
The passage uses the example of Zaid's height and color to illustrate.
4
Evaluate the objection and responses
The objector says a shakhs is a conventional composite (murakkab i'tibari) of essence and accidents, so it can be defined by both. The commentator refutes this, showing that such a definition is verbal and not real.
The commentator also criticizes the first response (that it's verbal) by noting the Qur'an would then also be a conventional composite, making the author's earlier difficulties unnecessary.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi position
The final position is that a shakhs can be distinguished only by indication or naming, not by a real definition. No real definition of an individual is possible.
This is consistent with the Hanafi understanding that definitions capture universal essences.

الترويح لحل التوضيح والتلويح
ہے کہ وہ کہہ دے کہ شخصی مرکب اعتباری ہے اور وہ ماہیت و تشخص کا مجموعہ ہوتا ہے پس کیوں جائز نہیں ہے کہ حد بیان کی جائے ایسی جو فائدہ دے امرین کی معرفت کا ۔ نہ اعتراض کیا جائے کہ مرکب اعتباری کی تعریف لفظی ہے اور کلام حد حقیقی میں ہے کیونکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اگر تسلیم کر لیا جائے اس کو پس قرآن کا مجموعہ مرکب اعتباری ہے لا محالہ بس اس وقت کوئی حاجت نہیں ہے تمام مقدمات کی طرف اور اس کی طرف جس کو ذکر کیا اس کے شخصی ہونے میں تکلفات میں سے۔ اور کبھی اعتراض کیا جاتا ہے کہ اگر اکتفاء کرلیا جائے شخص کی تعریف میں ماہیت کے مقدمات پر تو نہیں مختص ہوگی وہ ( تعریف شخص کے ساتھ پس نہیں فائدہ دے گی تمیز کا وہ جو اقل مرتبہ ہے تعریف کے مراتب میں سے اور اگر ذکر کیا ( ان مقومات) کیساتھ عرضیات مشخصہ (خصوصیات ) کو بھی تو نہیں ثابت ہو گا اس کے صدق کا دائمی رہنا اس کے زوال کے امکان کی وجہ سے پس نہیں ہوگی وہ حد اور اس میں نظر ہے بوجہ جائز ہونے اس کے کہ ذکر کیا جائے اس کے ساتھ عرضیات مشخصہ کو اور اس کے زوال کے وقت زائل ہو جائے گا محدود بھی یعنی وہ شخص بھی پس نہیں ہے مضر حد کا صادق نہ آنا بلکہ واجب ہے، اور حق بات یہ ہے کہ بیشک شخصی ممکن ہے کہ اس کی حد ذکر کی جائے اس چیز کے ساتھ جو فائدہ دے اس کے امتیاز کا جمیع ماعدا سے وجود کے اعتبار سے نہ کہ ایسی چیز کے ساتھ جو فائدہ دے اس کی تعیین کا اور اسکے تشخص کا اس حیثیت سے کہ نہ ممکن ہو اس کا مشترک ہونا کثیرین کے درمیان عقل کے اعتبار سے کیونکہ یہ جز این نیست حاصل ہوتی ہے اشارہ سے نہ کہ کسی اور طرح سے۔
امر شخص کی حد کیوں بیان نہیں کی جاسکتی
تشریح : قولہ علی ان اشخص لا محد:۔ یہ شرح کی مہارت کا پہلا حصہ ہے فرض شارعا یہ ہے کہ مان نے کہا تھاکہ شخص کی حد بیان نہیں کی جاتی تو شارع اس کی دلیل دیتے ہیں کہ شخصی کی تعریف مشخصیات کی تعیین سے ہوگی اور مشخصات کی تعیین یا تو اشارہ سے ہوتی ہے یا اس کا نام و علم بیان کرنے سے ہوتی ہے اور حد سے مشخصات کی تعیین نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ حدود میں اعلیٰ درجہ کی حد حد نام ہے اور وہ بھی مقومات ( جنس فصل) پر مشتمل ہوتی ہے مشخصات پر مشتمل نہیں ہوتی تو اس سے شخص کی تعریف نہیں ہو سکتی مثلا زیدار مشخصی ہے اس کی حد بیان کریں گے حیوان ناطق کے ساتھ یہ حد تمام انسانوں پر صادق آئے گی اب زید کی معرفت تب حاصل ہوگی جب اس کے مشخصات بیان کریں گے کہ اس کا قد اتنا ہے فلاں رنگ کا ہے یا اشارہ کریں گے
یا نام لیں گے تو زید کی معرفت ہوگی اور حد ماہیت کے مقومات و اجزاء پر مشتمل ہوتی ہے خصوصیات پر مشتمل نہیں ہوتی ۔ سوال :۔ آپ نے کہا مخصی کی تعریف اسم اور علم کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے اب کسی شخص کا نام لیں تو مخاطب اس کو جانتا ہوگا یا نہیں اگر جانتا ہے تو اس کے سامنے نام لینے کا فائدہ ہی نہیں کیونکہ یہ تحصیل حاصل ہے اور اگر وہ پہلے نام نہیں جانتا تو ہم نام لیتے
رہیں اس کو معرفت حاصل نہیں ہوگی جیسا کوئی آدمی کہے (زید) تو سامعین کو پتہ نہیں چل سکے گا کہ وہ کون ہے تو یہاں پر علم و نام سے معرفت نہ ہوئی تو علم ذکر کرنے سے تعریف کہاں سے ہوئی۔

ولقائل :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض اعتراض نقل کر کے اپنی طرف سے دو جواب ذکر کئے ہیں پھر ان کی تردید کی ہے اور اپنی طرف سے قول حق پیش کیا ہے اعتراض کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ام شخصی مرکب اعتباری ہے اس لئے کہ شخصی مجموعہ ہے ماہیت کا اور تشخص کا لہذا امر شخصی مرکب اعتباری ہوا جیسے زید مرکب ہے حیوان ناطق ہے اور مشخصات و خصوصیات سے تو زیدام شخصی ہو کر مرکب اعتباری ہوا کیونکہ زید ماہیت مع التشخص کو کہتے ہیں اور مرکب اعتباری قابل حد ہے تو ایسا کیوں نہیں ہو سکتا ؟ کہ ایسی تعریف کریں جو ماہیت و تشخصات دونوں پر مشتمل ہو تو اس کو حد کہہ سکتے ہیں یعنی ایسی تعریف ہو جو مقومات اور مشخصات دونوں پر مشتمل ہو مثلاً زید حیوان ناطق ہے کالا ہے چھوٹے قد کا ہے اس میں حد بھی ہے اور ماعدا سے امتیاز بھی ہے لہذا آپ کا کہنا کہ شخص کی حد نہیں آتی یہ درست نہیں ہے۔ نوٹ ... زید کو مرکب اعتباری کہا ہے کیونکہ اس کے اندر دو جزوں کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے ورنہ خارج میں اس میں کوئی ترکیب ماہیت و تشخص کے اعتبار ) سے نہیں ہے۔
جواب (۱):۔ جب تعریف میں مشخصات اور مقومات ذکر کریں گے تو یہ مرکب اعتباری ہوگا اور مرکب اعتباری کی تعریف تعریف لفظی ہوتی ہے تعریف حقیقی نہیں ہوتی اور ہماری بحث تعریف حقیقی میں ہے۔
رو الشارح: شارع نے کہا یہ جواب درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس اعتبار سے قرآن کی تعریف بھی مرکب اعتباری ہوگی کیونکہ وہ بھی مشخصات سے مرکب ہے پھر مصنف نے اتنے تکلفات کیوں کئے ؟ اس سے شخصی ہونے کے لئے بس وہ یہ کہہ دیتے کہ یہ مرکب اعتباری ہے اور مرکب اعتباری کی تعریف لفظی ہوتی ہے اس لئے دور لازم نہیں آتا ۔
جواب (۲) ۔ بعض حضرات نے اور جواب دیاسر شخص کی حد نہیں ہو سکتی کیونکہ تعریف صرف مقومات سے ہوگی یا مقومات اور مشخصات دونوں سے ہو گی اگر تعریف صرف مقومات ( جنس و فصل) سے کریں تو ماعدا سے امتیاز نہیں ہو گا حالانکہ تعریف کا
Al-Tarwih li-Hall al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih
That he says that the individual is a conventional composite and it is a sum of essence and individuation. So why is it not permissible to give a definition that provides knowledge of both matters? Do not object that the definition of a conventional composite is verbal while the discussion is about a real definition, because we say: if that is conceded, then the Qur'an is a conventional composite necessarily, so there is no need for all those premises and that which he mentioned as difficulties in it being individual. And sometimes it is objected: if one suffices in the definition of a person with the premises of essence, it will not be specific to the person, so it will not give distinction, which is the lowest level of definition; and if one mentions with those essential components also the individuating accidents (characteristics), then its continuous truthfulness will not be established due to the possibility of their disappearance, so it will not be a definition. And there is consideration in this due to the permissibility of mentioning with it the individuating accidents, and at the time of their disappearance the defined also disappears, i.e., that person also, so it is not harmful that the definition does not apply, rather it is necessary. And the truth is that indeed it is possible to define an individual with something that provides distinction from all other things in terms of existence, not with something that provides its determination and individuality in a way that it cannot be shared among multiple persons intellectually, because this part is nothing but obtained by indication, not in any other way. Why the definition of an individual person cannot be given Explanation: His saying: 'That individuals are undefined' — this is the first part of the commentary. The author's presumption is that the text said that a person cannot be defined, so the commentator gives its proof: the definition of an individual is by determination of characteristics, and determination of characteristics either by indication or by stating its name or knowledge. A definition cannot determine characteristics because the highest level of definitions is the definition by name, and it consists of essential components (genus and differentia), not characteristics, so a person cannot be defined by it. For example, Zaid is an individual; we will define him as 'rational animal' — this definition applies to all humans. Now knowledge of Zaid is only obtained when we mention his characteristics: that his height is such, he is of such color, or we indicate, or we take his name — then knowledge of Zaid is obtained. A definition consists of essential components and parts of the essence, not characteristics. Question: You said that an individual is defined by name and knowledge. Now if we mention a person's name, will the addressee know him or not? If he knows, then mentioning the name is unnecessary because it is acquisition of what is already obtained; if he did not know the name before, we mention the name, but he still does not get knowledge — like if someone says 'Zaid', the listeners cannot know who he is. So how is definition achieved by mentioning knowledge? Answer: In one case, mentioning knowledge gives knowledge: when the addressee knows the thing but has forgotten it; when the speaker says it, he remembers the name, so knowledge is obtained. So our saying that knowledge gives knowledge is correct. The definition of a conventional composite is a verbal definition, not a real one. And there is a speaker: This is the second part of the commentary. The purpose is to quote an objection and from oneself mention two answers, then refute them and present the correct opinion. The summary of the objection is: we say that the individual person is a conventional composite because the individual is the sum of essence and individuation; hence an individual thing is a conventional composite — like Zaid is composite of rational animal and characteristics and properties. So Zaid, being an individual, is a conventional composite because Zaid is called essence with individuation, and a conventional composite is definable. So why can we not make a definition that includes both essence and individuation? We can call that a definition, i.e., a definition that includes both essential components and characteristics — e.g., Zaid is rational animal, black, short in stature — in this there is a definition and distinction from others. So your saying that a person cannot be defined is not correct. Note: Zaid is called a conventional composite because two parts are considered in him, though externally there is no composition in terms of essence and individuation. Answer (1): When we mention characteristics and essential components in the definition, then this will be a conventional composite, and the definition of a conventional composite is a verbal definition, not a real definition, and our discussion is about real definition. The commentator said: This answer is not correct because then the definition of the Qur'an would also be a conventional composite, since it is also composed of characteristics, so why did the author go through so many difficulties? For it to be individual, he could simply have said it is a conventional composite and its definition is verbal, so there is no necessary cycle. Answer (2): Some other responded by saying that a person cannot be defined because definition is either only from essential components or from both essential components and characteristics. If we define using only essential components (genus and differentia), then there is no distinction from others, although the definition's...
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from Al-Tarwih deals with a fundamental issue in Hanafi logic and usul: whether a specific individual (shakhs) can be given a real definition (hadd haqiqi). The commentator begins by stating that the author of the matn claimed that individuals cannot be defined. The commentator then provides the rationale: defining an individual would require specifying its individuating characteristics (mu'arrifat), but such specification can only be done by pointing (ishara) or by stating the name, not by a definition composed of genus and differentia. A real definition consists solely of essential components (jins and fasl) that apply to all members of the species, not to a single individual. For example, defining Zaid as 'rational animal' applies to every human, not uniquely to Zaid. To uniquely identify Zaid, we must add accidental features like height and color, but these accidents are not essential and can change, so the definition would not be permanent. The commentator then addresses an objection: if an individual is a 'conventional composite' (murakkab i'tibari) of essence and accidents, why can't we define it by a combination of essential and accidental components? The commentator first responds that such a definition would be verbal (lafzi), not real, and our concern is with real definitions. But the commentator refutes this by noting that the same would apply to the definition of the Qur'an (which is also a conventional composite), making the author's effort unnecessary. A second response argues that a real definition cannot include accidents because they are not essential; if the definition is only from essential components, it fails to distinguish the individual; if it includes both, it becomes a verbal definition. The commentator concludes that it is possible to define an individual in terms of existence (by pointing) but not in terms of quiddity (mahiyya). Hence, no real definition of a shakhs is possible.

Key Terms
شخص (shakhs): الفرد المعين من نوع كزيد
حد حقيقي (hadd haqiqi): تعريف بالمقومات الذاتية (جنس وفصل) يفيد ماهية الشيء
تعريف لفظي (ta'rif lafzi): تعريف بمركب اعتباري يشمل مقومات وعرضيات لا يفيد الحقيقة
مركب اعتباري (murakkab i'tibari): شيء اعتبر مركبا من عدة أمور مع أن حقيقته بسيطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why cannot a specific individual like Zaid be defined by a real definition (hadd haqiqi)?
A) Because Zaid is a composite of essence and accidents, and real definitions only include essential components.
B) Because Zaid is too complex to be defined.
C) Because real definitions are always verbal.
D) Because Zaid's name is sufficient for identification.

Key Takeaway
A real definition consists only of universal essential components; an individual's accidental properties cannot form part of a real definition, so no real definition of a shakhs is possible.
