Resolving the Dispute: Haqiqah vs. Majaz in Applying 'Nazm' to the Quran
Addresses an objection about applying the term 'nazm' to the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that words are interpreted in their real (haqiqah) meaning by analyzing the term 'nazm' and evaluating the objection that such usage is disrespectful.

Core Idea
Words default to their real meaning; metaphorical use requires a clear indication.

This passage presents a sharp objection: if calling the Quran 'lafz' (word) is disrespectful, then calling it 'nazm' (poetry) is even worse since the Quran condemns poets. The Hanafi answer relies on a critical usul distinction: 'nazm' in its real sense means stringing pearls, not poetry. By following the principle that the mind moves to the real meaning, the Hanafi scholar shows there is no disrespect. Let's unpack the reasoning and the underlying methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the objector's claim: applying 'nazm' to the Quran is disrespectful because the Quran condemns poets and 'nazm' is a term for poetry.
The objector cites the Quranic verse 'And it is not the word of a poet' (36:69).
2
Extract the Hanafi Response
The answer distinguishes between the real (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meanings of 'nazm' and asserts that here it is used in its real meaning.
Real meaning: stringing pearls; metaphorical meaning: poetry.
3
Apply the Usul Principle
In Hanafi usul, when a word has both real and metaphorical meanings, the default (asl) is the real meaning unless there is a clear indication (qarina) for metaphor. Since no such indication exists here, the mind goes to the real meaning.
This is a subset of the principle 'al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā' but applied to word meaning.
4
Draw the Legal Outcome
Since the real meaning involves no disrespect, applying 'nazm' to the Quran in its real sense is permissible and even more appropriate.
The text says 'the real meaning is not disrespectful, therefore applying nazm is better'.
5
Reflect on the Epistemological Weight
This analysis is based on linguistic principles (haqiqah/majaz) which are firmly established in Hanafi usul. The objection is refuted without compromising the Quran's sanctity.
The authority of this analysis comes from the accepted usul maxims, not from a specific riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان قبیل:۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے غرض اس سے اعتراض و جواب ہے اعتراض یہ ہے کہ جس طرح قرآن پر لفظ کے اطلاق میں بے ادبی ہے ایسے ہی نظم کے اطلاق میں بھی بے ادبی ہے کیونکہ اعظم کا اطلاق اشعار پر کیا جاتا ہے اور قرآن مجید میں شاعر کو برا کہا گیا ہے کما قال تعالی و ماہو بقول شاعر تو نظم کے اطلاق میں بے ادبی ہوئی ؟ جواب: یہ ہے کہ لفظ کا حقیقی معنی رمی ہے اور نظم کا حقیقی معنی ہے موتیوں کو دھاگہ میں پرونا اب نظم اطلاق اشعار پر مجاز ہے اور نظم کے معنی میں حقیقتا مستعمل ہے اور ذہن حقیقی معنی ہی کی طرف جاتا ہے نہ کہ مجازی معنی کی طرف اور حقیقی معنی کے اطلاق میں بے ادبی نہیں ہے اس لئے نظم کا اطلاق اولی ہے۔
Then it is said: This is the second part of the commentary's text. The purpose is an objection and answer. The objection is that just as applying the word 'lafz' to the Quran is disrespect, similarly applying 'nazm' is also disrespect because 'nazm' is applied to poems, and in the noble Quran the poet is condemned, as He the Exalted said: 'And it is not the word of a poet' (36:69). So in applying 'nazm' there is disrespect? The answer: The real meaning of 'lafz' is throwing, and the real meaning of 'nazm' is stringing pearls together. Now, 'nazm' is applied to poems metaphorically, and here it is used in its real meaning. The mind goes towards the real meaning, not the metaphorical, and there is no disrespect in applying the real meaning. Therefore, applying 'nazm' is better.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute about the use of the term 'nazm' for the Quran. The objector argues that since the Quran condemns poets, calling the Quran 'nazm' (poetry) is disrespectful. The commentator answers by distinguishing between the real (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meanings of 'nazm'. In its real sense, 'nazm' means stringing pearls; it is only metaphorically applied to poetry. Since the Quran is 'nazm' in the real sense (assembled in a sequence), there is no disrespect. This follows the Hanafi usul principle that words should be interpreted in their real meaning unless there is a clear indication for metaphorical use. The objection's strength is thus refuted by linguistic analysis.

Key Terms
حقیقت (haqiqah): Real, literal meaning of a word as originally coined; e.g., 'nazm' = stringing pearls.
مجاز (majaz): Metaphorical meaning used due to a connection; e.g., 'nazm' = poetry via metaphorical extension.
قرینہ (qarina): Contextual indication that determines whether haqiqah or majaz is intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the real meaning of the word 'nazm' as used in the answer?
A) Poetry
B) Stringing pearls
C) Speech
D) Revelation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle of defaulting to the real meaning (haqiqah) resolves apparent conflicts with reverence, as shown with the term 'nazm'.

Two Types of Pillar (Rukn) in Prayer
Definition of a twofold classification of pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of pillars (rukn) and explain why recitation in prayer is a non-necessary pillar according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A pillar that is the primary end is necessary; a pillar that is not is necessary only in form, not in intent.

In this brief passage, the commentator addresses a critical question: if recitation is defined as Arabic words conveying meaning, how can Persian recitation be valid in prayer? The answer hinges on a classification of pillars into those that are primary ends and those that are not. Understanding this distinction reveals the Hanafi emphasis on meaning and intention over literal form.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objector says: you define recitation as a pillar, and the Quran is words indicating meaning. Persian words are different, so how can they fulfill the same pillar?
The objection assumes the pillar is the literal Arabic words.
2
Distinguish two types of pillar
The answer classifies pillars into those that are primary ends (maqsud asli) and those that are not. Only the primary end is necessary (lazim).
This is a Hanafi usul principle: not every pillar is equally obligatory.
3
Apply to recitation in prayer
In prayer, the primary end is the meaning (understanding and connection with Allah), not the specific words. Therefore, recitation as a pillar is fulfilled by conveying the meaning, even in Persian.
This explains the permissibility of Persian recitation.
4
Draw the Hanafi principle
The Hanafi school prioritizes intention and meaning over literal wording in certain contexts. This classification is a tool (usul) for deriving rulings on non-Arabic recitation.
Other schools may differ on this issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما الکلام: یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے سوال کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ کر دیا۔ سوال:۔ ادھر کہتے ہو کہ قراءت قرآن نماز کارکن ہے اور قرآن کی تعریف کی ہے الفاظ دال علی المعنی کے ساتھ اب ایک شئی رکن ہو اور لازم نہ ہو یہ کیسے ہو سکتا ہے؟ اب الفاظ رکن ہیں اور فارسی میں قرات جائز ہے یہ رکن کیسے ادا ہوا؟ جواب: رکن کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) مقصود اصلی (۲) مقصود اصلی نہ ہو تو رکن لازم وہ ہوتا ہے جو مقصود اصلی ہو اور جو مقصود اصلی نہ ہو وہ لازم نہیں ہوتا تو یہاں چونکہ مقصود اصلی معنی ہے الفاظ نہیں اس لئے الفاظ لازم نہیں ہیں مزید تفصیل آگے آجائیگی۔
And as for the speech (kalam): This is the second part of the commentary's text. From here, an answer to a question is indicated. Question: You say that recitation of the Quran is a pillar of prayer, and you have defined Quran as 'words indicating meaning'. Now, a thing being a pillar yet not necessary, how can that be? Here the words are the pillar, but Persian recitation is permissible, how was this pillar fulfilled? Answer: The pillar is of two types: (1) the primary end, (2) not the primary end. The pillar that is necessary is that which is the primary end, and that which is not the primary end is not necessary. Here, since the primary end is meaning, not words, therefore the words are not necessary. Further details will come later.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage clarifies the nature of the pillar (rukn) of recitation in prayer. The objector points out a seeming contradiction: if recitation is defined as words that indicate meaning, then how can one fulfill it with Persian words which are different? The answer introduces a classification of pillars: some are primary ends (maqsud asli) and some are not. Only the primary end is necessary (lazim). In prayer, the primary end is the meaning (understanding and connecting with Allah), not the specific Arabic words. Therefore, Persian recitation fulfills the pillar because it conveys the meaning. This is consistent with the Hanafi emphasis on intention and meaning over literal forms.

Key Terms
مقصود اصلی (maqsud asli): The primary end or purpose; here it is the meaning of the Quran, not the words.
لازم (lazim): Necessary; a pillar that is the primary end is necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what makes a pillar (rukn) necessary (lazim)?
A) It is a part of the prayer
B) It is the primary end (maqsud asli)
C) It is in Arabic
D) It is recited aloud

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a pillar is necessary only if it is the primary end; otherwise, it can be fulfilled by alternative means that achieve the intended meaning.

Refining the Definition of Adjective in Talwih
Critiquing the definition of ṣifa with the condition of weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the precise morphological condition for a derived noun to qualify as an adjective (ṣifa) in Hanafi usul and apply this condition to classify given derived patterns.

Core Idea
Only فاعل and مفعول patterns are true adjectives — other derived patterns carry different meanings.

This passage from al-Talwih, the super-commentary on al-Tawdih, refines the definition of صفة (adjective) by adding the condition of 'weight' (وزن). The earlier definition merely said it is a derived noun whose meaning is the root meaning plus the derivative's weight. But here, Taftazani argues this actually restricts the adjective to only the active and passive participle patterns. Understanding this refinement is essential for correctly applying the concept of adjective in usul al-fiqh, especially when distinguishing between general and specific terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original definition
The earlier definition stated that an adjective (ṣifa) is a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of its root along with the weight of the derivative. Locate this in the passage.
The passage begins by discussing the division of nouns into apparent and others.
2
Spot the refinement condition
The phrase 'مَعَ وَزْنِ الْمُشْتَقِّ' (with the weight of the derived) is the key condition. But note that the author then argues this only applies to فاعل and مفعول patterns.
The author uses examples like ضارب and مضروب.
3
Recognize excluded patterns
The passage explicitly excludes nouns of place (مفعَل), instrument (مفعال), and other derived patterns like أفعل, فعلان, etc. List these exclusion categories.
E.g., مقتل (place of killing), مفتاح (key).
4
Understand the rationale
The rationale is that only the agent/patient patterns (فاعل/مفعول) are commonly used to express the meaning 'with the agent/patient'. Other patterns express different relationships (place, instrument, color, state).
The passage says: 'التعبير عما يصدر عنه الفعل أو يقع عليه بالفاعل أو المفعول شائع'.
5
Apply to new examples
Given a list of derived nouns, determine which qualify as ṣifa according to this refined definition: e.g., كاتب (yes), مكتوب (yes), أبيض (no), عطشان (no), مدرسة (no).
This step solidifies understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ ، وَأَيْضًا الاسْمُ الظَّاهِرُ) قَيَّدَ بِذَلِكَ ؛ لأنَّ الْمُضْمَرَ خَارِجٌ عَنْ الأَقْسَامِ وَكَذَا اسْمُ الْإِشَارَةِ فَكَأَنَّهُ أَرَادَ مَا لَيْسَ بِمُضْمَرٍ وَلَا اسْمِ إِشَارَةٍ وَالصِّفَةُ بِمُقْتَضَى هَذَا التَّقْسِيمِ اسْمٌ مُشْتَقٌ يَكُونُ مَعْنَاهُ عَيْنُ مَا وُضِعَ لَهُ الْمُشْتَقُ مِنْهُ مَعَ وَزْنِ الْمُشْتَقِّ فَالصَّارِبُ لَفَةٌ مُشْتَقٌ مِنْ الضَّرُبِ مَعْنَاهُ مَعْنَى الضَّرْبِ مَعَ الْفَاعِلِ ، وَالْمَضْرُوبُ مَعْنَاهُ مَعْنَى الضَّرُبِ مَعَ الْمَفْعُولِ ، وَهَذَا مَعْنَى قَوْلِهِمْ مَا دَلَّ عَلَى ذَاتٍ مُبْهَمَةٍ وَمَعْنَى مُعَيَّنٍ يَقُومُ بِهَا وَاحْتَرَزَ بِقَوْلِهِ مَعَ وَزْنِ الْمُشْتَقِّ عَنْ اسْمِ الزَّمَانِ وَالْمَكَان وَالآلَةِ وَنَحْو ذَلِكَ مِنْ الْمُشْتَقَّاتِ ، إِذْ لَيْسَ مَعْنَى الْمَقْتَل هُوَ الْقَتْلُ مَعَ الْمَفْعَلِ ، وَمَعْنَى الْمِفْتَاحِ هُوَ الْفَتْحُ مَعَ الْمِفْعَالِ ، إِذْ التَّعْبِيرُ عَمَّا يَصْدُرُ عَنْهُ الْفِعْلُ أَوْ يَقَعُ عَلَيْهِ بِالْفَاعِلِ أَوْ الْمَفْعُولِ شَائِعٌ بِخِلَافِ التَّعْبِيرِ عَنْ الْمَكَانِ وَالْآلَةِ بِالْمَفْعَلِ وَالْمِفْعَالِ ، وَلِقَائِلِ أَنْ يَقُولَ هَذَا التَّفْسِيرُ لَا يَصْدُقُ إِلَّا عَلَى صِفَةٍ تَكُونُ عَلَى وَزْنِ الْفَاعِلِ وَالْمَفْعُول ؛ لأنَّ التَّعْبِيرَ عَمَّا يَقُومُ بِهِ الْمَعْنَى إِنَّمَا يَكُونُ بِالْفَاعِلِ ، أَوْ الْمَفْعُولِ لَا بِالْأَفْعُلِ وَالْفَعْلَانِ وَالْفِعْلِ وَالْمُسْتَفْعِلِ وَالْمُفَعْلَلِ ، وَنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ فَلَيْسَ مَعْنَى الْأَبْيَضِ وَالْأَفْضَلِ مَثَلَا هُوَ الْبَيَاضُ وَالْفَضْلُ مَعَ الْأَفْضَلِ وَلَا مَعْنَى الْعَطْشَانِ هُوَ الْعَطَشُ مَعَ الْفَعَلَانِ ، وَلَا مَعْنَى الْخَيْرِ هُوَ الْخَيْرِيَّةُ مَعَ الْفِعْلِ وَلَا مَعْنَى
His statement: 'And also the apparent noun' — he restricted it with that because the pronoun is excluded from the categories, and likewise the demonstrative noun. So it is as if he intended what is not a pronoun nor a demonstrative. And the adjective according to this division is a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of that which it is derived from along with the weight of the derived word. So 'beater' (ḍārib) is a word derived from 'beating' (ḍarb), its meaning is the meaning of beating along with the agent, and 'beaten' (maḍrūb) its meaning is the meaning of beating along with the object. And this is the meaning of their statement: 'what indicates an indefinite essence and a specific meaning that subsists in it.' And he guarded by his statement 'with the weight of the derived' against the noun of time, place, and instrument and the like of the derived words, for the meaning of 'place of killing' (maqtal) is not killing along with the place-noun form, and the meaning of 'key' (miftāḥ) is not opening along with the instrument-noun form. Because the expression for that from which the action emanates or upon which it occurs by the agent or object is common, unlike the expression for the place and instrument with the forms mafʿal and mifʿāl. And one may say: this interpretation only applies to an adjective that is on the weight of fāʿil (active) and mafʿūl (passive), because the expression for that in which the meaning subsists is only by fāʿil or mafʿūl, not by afʿul, faʿlān, fiʿl, mustafʿil, mufaʿlal, and the like. So the meaning of 'white' (abyaḍ) and 'better' (afḍal) is not whiteness and excellence along with afʿal, nor the meaning of 'thirsty' (ʿaṭshān) is thirst along with faʿlān, nor the meaning of 'good' (khayr) is goodness along with fiʿl, nor the meaning of...
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is from al-Talwih, the super-commentary by Taftazani on al-Tawdih. It refines the definition of صفة (adjective) given earlier. The earlier definition stated that an adjective is a derived noun whose meaning is exactly the meaning of its root word, along with the weight of the derived word. Taftazani argues that this definition actually only applies to adjectives on the patterns of فاعل and مفعول (active and passive participles). He justifies this by explaining that the expression for what subsists with a meaning (like agent or patient) is typically done with these patterns. Other derived patterns like أفعل (for colors), فعلان (for emotions), and فعلى (for states) do not have the same relationship. For example, the meaning of 'white' (أبيض) is not 'whiteness' combined with the form أفعل; rather, it is a specific color. Thus the definition is more restrictive. This is a typical critical refinement in the Hanafi usul tradition where the hashya (super-commentary) corrects or narrows the earlier sharh (commentary) to ensure terminological precision.

Key Terms
صفت (ṣifa): In this Talwih passage, it is a derived noun on the weight of فاعل or مفعول (active/passive participle) whose meaning is the root meaning plus the agent or patient.
وزن المشتق (wazn al-mushtaqq): The morphological weight (pattern) of the derived word, e.g., فاعل, مفعول. Excludes other derived patterns like أفعل, فعلان.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Talwih, which of the following words qualifies as an adjective (ṣifa) in the technical usul sense?
A) مفتاح (key)
B) أبيض (white)
C) كاتب (writer)
D) عطشان (thirsty)

Key Takeaway
A derived noun qualifies as an adjective (ṣifa) in Hanafi usul only if it is on the weight of فاعل or مفعول, conveying agent/patient meaning.

Distinction Between Sifat and Ism in Derived Nouns
Response to a commentator's objection on sifat-ism definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between an adjective (sifat) and a noun (ism) by analyzing the primacy of the intended meaning and the relationship to the named essence.

Core Idea
A word is an adjective if the derived meaning is the primary intent; otherwise it's a noun.

In this passage, the author addresses an objection raised by a commentator regarding the definition of adjectives and nouns in derived forms. The key insight is that adjectives require the infinitive meaning to be the primary object of coinage, while nouns prioritize the essence itself. Understanding this classification is crucial for correctly analyzing derived terms in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the preliminary classification
Recognize the three categories: words coined for an absolute essence with meaning (sifat), words coined for a specific essence without meaning (ism), and words coined for a specific essence with a meaning that is external or internal (ism mushabbah).
This is the foundation for distinguishing sifat from ism.
2
Understand the author's criterion
The author uses the phrase 'ma wad'a lahu min al-mushtaqq minhu ma'a wazn al-mushtaqq'. The infinitive meaning (ma wad'a lahu min al-mushtaqq minhu) is primary, and the essence (wazn al-mushtaqq) is subordinate. In sifat, the meaning is the primary intent; in ism, the essence is primary or the meaning is secondary.
Note the inversion: meaning first, essence second, indicated by the word 'ma'a' (with).
3
Analyze the commentator's error
The commentator focused only on the morphological form (wazn) and took 'mushtaqq' to mean active/passive participle. This led to objections against words like 'mustakhraj', 'atshan', 'mudahraj'. The author's definition already accounts for them by prioritizing meaning.
The error is in method: focusing on form rather than the conceptual priority of meaning.
4
Apply the distinction to examples
Test words like 'darib' (beater): it is sifat because the meaning 'beating' is primary. For 'ahmar' (red), it is ism mushabbah because redness is external but not primary. For 'faras' (horse), it is ism because no meaning is considered.
Practice using the criteria: is the derived meaning the primary object of coinage?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب (۲):۔ حقیقت یہ ہے کہ یہ اعتراض جو شاریخ نے ذکر کیا ہے یہ تاریخ کی تقریر پر وارد ہوتا ہے ماتن کی عبارت پر یہ اعتراض وارد ہی نہیں ہوتا اس کی تفصیل کو سمجھنے سے پہلے ایک مقدمہ کو جاننا ضروری ہے۔
مقدمہ: کبھی کسی لفظ کو ذات مہمہ کے لئے وضع کیا جاتا ہے کسی معنی معین مقصودی کے اعتبار کے ساتھ اس صورۃ میں اس لفظ کا اطلاق ہر اس ذات پر ہو سکتا ہے جو اس صفت کے ساتھ متصف ہو جیسے لفظ ضارب، افضل مستخرج وغیرہ اور اس کے لئے موصوف کا ہونا ضروری ہے خواہ وہ لفظوں میں مذکور ہو یا مقدر ہوتا کہ اس معنی معین کا اس کے ساتھ قیام ہو سکے اور اس جیسے لفظ کو صفت کہتے ہیں اور کبھی کسی لفظ کو ذات معینہ کے لئے وضع کیا جاتا ہے بغیر کسی معنی کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے جیسے فرس واہل اس کو اسم کہتے ہیں کبھی لفظ کو ذات معینہ کے لئے وضع کیا جاتا ہے اور وضع میں ایسے معنی کا لحاظ کیا جاتا ہے جس کو اس ذات کے ساتھ ایک قسم کا تعلق ہو پھر اس کی دو قسم ہیں (۱) یہ معنی موضوع لہ سے خارج ہو لیکن اسم کی اجزاء کے مقابلہ میں تعیین کے لئے یہ معنی سبب ہو جیسے احمر ایسے شخص کا نام رکھ دیں جس میں حمرة پائی جاتی ہو اب یہاں حمرة معنی موضوع لہ سے خارج ہے لیکن نام رکھنے کے لئے یہ سبب بن رہا ہے (۲) یہ معنی موضوع لہ میں داخل ہو اور اسم دو چیزوں سے مرکب ہو یعنی ذات معینہ اور اس معنی مخصوص سے جیسے اسم آلہ ، ظرف زمان و مکان لفظ کی ان دونوں قسموں کو بھی اسم کہتے ہیں لیکن یہ صفت کے مشابہ ہوتے ہیں۔ تفصیل :۔ اب تفصیل سمجھیں کہ ماتن نے صفت اور اسم مشابہ صفت کے درمیان فرق کرنے کے لئے یہ عنوان قائم کیا خان كان عين ما وضع له من المشتق منه مع وزن المشتق اور ماوضع لہ من المشتق منہ سے مراد معنی مصدری ہے اور وزن مشتق سے مراد ذات مہمہ ہے جو اس معنی مصدری کے لئے موصوف بنتا ہے اب ہونا تو یوں چاہیے تھا کہ ذات کو مقدم کرتے اور معنی مصدری کو موخر کرتے لیکن ماتن نے معنی مصدری کو مقدم کر کے اس طرف اشارہ کیا کہ اس میں معنی مصدری مقصود اصلی ہے اور ذات کا ذکر تو صرف اس لئے کیا جاتا ہے کہ معنی مصدری اس کے ساتھ قائم ہو سکے اور اس کی طرف اشارہ لفظ مع کے ساتھ کیا کیونکہ یہ اکثر تابع پر داخل ہوتا ہے جیسے ان اللہ مع الصابرین ، ان الله معنا اب یہاں صابرین وغیرہ تابع ہیں اور اللہ تعالی متبوع، تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مع وزن المشتق میں وزن مشتق ( ذات مہمہ ) تابع ہے مقصود اصلی معنی مصدری ہے خلاصہ یہ کہ صفت میں معنی مقصودی موضوع لہ سے خارج ہوتا ہے البتہ یہ مقصود بالذات ہوتا ہے اور ذات مہمہ یعنی اس کا موصوف وہ تابع ہوتا ہے اور اسم مشابہ صفہ میں معنی یا تو موضوع لہ سے خارج ہوتا ہے لیکن مقصود بالذات نہیں ہوتا جیسے احمر یا موضوع لہ کا جزء ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ دونوں قسمیں مائن کے عنوان سے صفت سے خارج ہیں لیکن شاریخ کی نظر صرف وزن مشتق پر جمی رہی اور ذات کی طرف نظر نہ کی پھر انہوں نے مشتق سے مراد فاعل یا مفعول لیا پھر مستخرج ، عطشان، مدحرج وغیرہ سے اعتراض ہوا تو اس کے جواب دینے کے لئے جنس مشتق کا قول کرنا پڑا امثل مشہور ہے کہ بیج ہی سے درخت پیدا ہوتا ہے جب بیج ہی غلط بو یا تو آگے درخت میں بھی ٹیڑھا پن آتا رہا تو خلاصہ یہ کہ اعتراض آپ کی تقریر میں ہے نہ کہ مائن کی عبارت میں ۔ ہذا ما تیسر لی من تقریر سید شریف فی جواب ہذا الاعتراض۔
Answer (2): The reality is that this objection which the commentator mentioned arises from his own exposition, not from the text of the author (matn). Before understanding its detail, it is necessary to know a preliminary point. Preliminary: Sometimes a word is coined for an absolute essence while considering a specific intended meaning. In that case, the word can apply to any essence qualified by that attribute, like the word ضارب (beater), افضل (more virtuous), مستخرج (extracted), etc. For such a word, a described subject (mawsuf) is necessary, whether mentioned explicitly in the wording or implied, so that that specific meaning can inhere in it. Such a word is called an adjective (sifat). Sometimes a word is coined for a specific essence without considering any meaning, like فرس (horse) and اہل (family), and this is called a noun (ism). Sometimes a word is coined for a specific essence while in the coinage a meaning is considered that has a type of relation with that essence. Then this has two types: (1) This meaning is external to the named thing (mawdu' lahu) but serves as a cause for determination as opposed to the components of the noun, like naming a person who has redness as احمر (red). Here redness is external to the named thing but becomes a cause for naming. (2) This meaning is included in the named thing, and the noun is composed of two things: a specific essence and that specific meaning, like the names of instruments, time, place. Both these types are also called nouns, but they resemble adjectives. Detail: Now understand the detail: the author established this heading to distinguish between an adjective (sifat) and a noun resembling an adjective (ism mushabbah bi-sifat). The phrase 'what is coined from the mushtaqq minhu along with the form of the derived word' (ma wad'a lahu min al-mushtaqq minhu ma'a wazn al-mushtaqq). By 'ma wad'a lahu min al-mushtaqq minhu' is meant the infinitive meaning, and by 'wazn al-mushtaqq' is meant the absolute essence that becomes the described subject for that infinitive meaning. Now it should have been that the essence is mentioned first and the infinitive meaning later, but the author mentioned the infinitive meaning first to indicate that in it the infinitive meaning is the primary intended, and the essence is only mentioned so that the infinitive meaning can inhere in it. This is indicated by the word 'with' (ma'a), because it often enters on the subordinate, like 'Indeed Allah is with the patient' (Quran), 'Allah is with us'. Here the patient etc. are subordinate and Allah is the principal. So it is understood that in 'ma'a wazn al-mushtaqq', the form of the derived word (the absolute essence) is subordinate, the primary intended is the infinitive meaning. Summary: In the adjective (sifat), the intended meaning is external to the named thing, but it is the primary object of intent, while the absolute essence (its described subject) is subordinate. In the noun resembling an adjective (ism mushabbah bi-sifat), the meaning either is external to the named thing but not primary object of intent, like احمر, or is a part of the named thing. Therefore both these types are excluded from the definition of adjective by the author's title. But the commentator's gaze remained fixed only on the form of the derived word and did not consider the essence. Then he took derived word as meaning the active or passive participle. Then objections were raised based on examples like مستخرج, عطشان, مدحرج, etc. To answer these, he had to mention the genus of the derived word. The famous proverb is that a tree is produced from the seed; if the seed itself is sown crooked, then the tree will continue to have crookedness. So the summary is that the objection is in your exposition, not in the author's text. This is what was facilitated for me from the explanation of Sayyid Sharif in answer to this objection.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage is a response to an objection raised by a commentator against the author's definition. The author (matn) distinguishes between adjectives (sifat) and nouns (ism), particularly nouns that resemble adjectives. He establishes a preliminary classification of words based on coinage: (1) words coined for an absolute essence with a meaning, which are adjectives; (2) words coined for a specific essence without meaning, which are nouns; (3) words coined for a specific essence but with a meaning considered in coinage, which are further divided into two types. The author's criterion for sifat is that the derived meaning (ma'nā maşdari) is the primary intent, and the essence is subordinate. The commentator mistakenly focused only on the morphological form (wazn) and considered derived (mushtaqq) to mean agent/patient nouns, leading to objections that the author's framework already resolves. The commentary emphasizes that the objection stems from the commentator's own position, not the author's text.

Key Terms
صفت (ṣifat): A word coined for an absolute essence while considering a specific meaning; the meaning is primary intent and external to the named thing.
اسم (ism): A word coined for a specific essence without meaning or with a meaning that is not primary or is internal.
اسم مشابہ صفت (ism mushabbah bi-sifat): A noun that resembles an adjective: either the meaning is external but not primary (like 'ahmar') or internal to the named thing (like instrument names).
مشتق (mushtaqq): A derived word; in this context, a word that has a morphological pattern suggesting derivation from a root.
وزن مشتق (wazn al-mushtaqq): The morphological form of the derived word; in the author's framework, it represents the absolute essence that serves as the described subject for the infinitive meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what distinguishes an adjective (sifat) from a noun (ism) in terms of priority?
A) In sifat, the essence is primary; in ism, the meaning is primary.
B) In sifat, the derived meaning is primary intent; in ism, the essence is primary or the meaning is secondary/internal.
C) In sifat, the word is always derived; in ism, it is never derived.
D) There is no distinction; all words are nouns.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between adjective and noun hinges on whether the derived meaning is the primary object of coinage or merely incidental.

Ishtiqaq (Derivation) and Its Application to Alam and Ism al-Jins
Definition of ishtiqaq and classification of nouns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ishtiqaq in two ways and classify a noun as derived (mushtaqq) or non-derived (ghayr mushtaqq) according to the Hanafi usul perspective.

Core Idea
A proper noun is never derived in its naming sense, but may be derived in its original meaning; the truly derived noun is the common noun.

This passage explains a subtle point from the matn about proper nouns (alam) and common nouns (ism al-jins) being either derived or non-derived. The commentator provides two definitions of derivation (ishtiqaq) and clarifies why examples like 'Hatim' and 'Zayd' differ. Understanding this distinction is crucial for analyzing word origins in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two noun categories
The matn divides nouns into proper (alam) and common (ism al-jins). Identify which examples correspond to each category (Hatim/Zayd for alam; Maqtal/rajul for ism al-jins).
Note that 'Hatim' is a proper name but has a root meaning.
2
Understand the two definitions of ishtiqaq
The commentator provides two definitions: one by knowledge (ilm) focusing on proportionality in meaning and composition, and one by practice (amal) focusing on extracting from root letters. Write both definitions in your own words.
3
Apply the definitions to the examples
Take the word 'Hatim'. Analyze whether it fits each definition. Does it have proportionality in meaning and composition with its root? Is it extracted from the root letters? Conclude whether it is derived or not.
4
Resolve the status of proper nouns
The commentator states that a proper noun is not derived with respect to its proper meaning, but may be derived with respect to its original lexical meaning. Explain why 'Zayd' cannot be considered derived even in that sense.
5
Determine the true derived noun
The passage concludes that the truly derived noun is only the common noun (ism al-jins). Explain why this is the case and why the proper noun is not considered derived in its proper sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( قَوْلُهُ وَهُمَا أَى : الْعَلَمُ وَاسْمُ الْجِنسِ إِمَّا مُشْتَقَّانِ كَحَاتِمٍ وَمَقْتَلٍ وَلَا يَصِحُ التَّمْثِيلُ بِنَحْوِ ضَارِبٍ ; لِأَنَّهُ جَعَلَ الصَّفَةَ قَسِيمًا لِاسْمِ الْجِنْسِ أَوْ لَا كَزَيْدٍ وَرَجُلٍ ، وَالاشْتِقَاقُ يُفَسِّرُ تَارَةً بِاعْتِبَارِ الْعِلْمِ فَيُقَالُ هُوَ أَنْ تَجِدَ بَيْنَ اللَّفْظَيْنِ تَنَاسُبًا فِي أَصْلِ الْمَعْنَى ، وَالتَّرْكِيبِ فَتَرُدَّ أَحَدَهُمَا لِلْآخَرِ فَالْمَرْدُودُ مُشْتَقٌ ، وَالْمَرْدُودُ إِلَيْهِ مُشْتَقٌ مِنْهُ ، وَتَارَةً بِاعْتِبَارِ الْعَمَلِ فَيُقَالُ هُوَ أَنْ تَأْخُذَ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ مَا يُنَاسِبُهُ فِي حُرُوفِهِ الْأُصُولِ وَتَرْتِيبِهَا فَتَجْعَلَهُ دَالًّا عَلَى مَعْنَى يُنَاسِبُ مَعْنَاهُ فَالْمَأْخُوذُ مُشْتَقٌ وَالْمَأْخُوذُ مِنْهُ مُشْتَقٌ مِنْهُ ، وَلَا يَخْفَى أَنَّ الْعَلَمَ لَا يَكُونُ مُشْتَقًا بِاعْتِبَارِ الْمَعْنَى الْعَلَمِيِّ ، بَلْ باعْتِبَارِ الْمَعْنَى الْأَصْلِي الْمَنْقُولِ عَنْهُ فَالْمُشْتَقُّ حَقِيقَةً هُوَ اسْمُ الْجِنْسِ لَا غَيْرُ
(His statement: 'and they both, i.e., the proper noun and the common noun, are either derived like Hatim and Maqtal, and it is not correct to exemplify with something like ضارب because he made the adjective a counterpart of the common noun, or not derived like Zayd and Rajul.' And derivation (ishtiqaq) is interpreted sometimes with respect to knowledge: it is said that it is that you find between the two words proportionality in the core meaning and composition, so you refer one back to the other; the referred is derived (mushtaqq) and the referent is the source (mushtaqq minhu). Sometimes with respect to practice: it is said that it is that you take from the word something that corresponds to it in its original letters and their order, and make it indicative of a meaning that corresponds to its meaning; the taken is derived and the taken from is the source. It is not hidden that the proper noun is not derived with respect to its proper meaning, but rather with respect to the original meaning from which it was transferred. So the derived in reality is the common noun only.
Source pages p. 528

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a statement from the matn regarding the classification of proper nouns (alam) and common nouns (ism al-jins) as either derived (mushtaqq) or non-derived. The commentator explains that examples of derived proper nouns like Hatim and Maqtal (which have a verbal root) should not be confused with adjectives like ضارب (beater), because the matn already separated adjectives from common nouns. He then provides two definitions of ishtiqaq: (1) by consideration of knowledge (ilm) — finding a proportional relation between two words in meaning and composition; (2) by consideration of practice (amal) — extracting a word from another while preserving root letters and order, to indicate a related meaning. He clarifies that a proper noun is not derived in its proper sense (as a name), but may be considered derived with respect to its original lexical meaning from which it was borrowed. Hence, the true derived word is only the common noun (ism al-jins).

Key Terms
علم (ʿalam): A proper noun, a name for a specific entity.
اسم الجنس (ism al-jins): A common noun, a name for a category of entities.
اشتقاق (ishtiqāq): Derivation: either by noting proportionality between words (by meaning and composition) or by extracting a word from another's root letters to indicate a related meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the example of ضارب not suitable for illustrating a derived proper noun?
A) Because ضارب is not a derived word.
B) Because the matn made the adjective a counterpart of the common noun, not the proper noun.
C) Because ضارب cannot be used as a proper noun.
D) Because ضارب is a common noun, not derived.

Key Takeaway
Derivation (ishtiqaq) is defined by proportionality in meaning and composition; a proper noun is not derived in its naming sense, only in its original lexical meaning, while the common noun is the only truly derived noun.

Ism Jins and 'Ilm: Derived and Non-Derived Categories
Defining categories of ism jins and 'ilm with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify nouns as ism jins or 'ilm and as mushtaq or ghayr mushtaq, and justify why words on the sifat pattern (e.g., ضارب) are excluded from derived ism jins examples.

Core Idea
Both generic and proper nouns can be derived or non-derived; derivation is not category-specific.

This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary clarifies the classification of nouns into ism jins (generic) and 'ilm (proper), each capable of being derived (mushtaq) or non-derived (ghayr mushtaq). The commentator adds a critical refinement: words on the sifat pattern (fa‘il) belong to a separate category and must not be used as examples of derived ism jins, ensuring taxonomic precision in legal language.

Guided Path
1
Identify the noun's function
Determine whether the noun names a common class (ism jins) or a specific entity ('ilm).
e.g., 'rajul' names any man (ism jins); 'Zayd' names one man ('ilm).
2
Assess derivation
Check if the word shares a root with a simpler form; if yes, it is mushtaq (derived); if no, ghayr mushtaq.
e.g., 'Hatim' from ح ت م (determination/generosity); 'Zayd' has no such root.
3
Apply the category distinction
Both ism jins and 'ilm can be mushtaq or ghayr mushtaq; do not confuse with sifat.
Sifat (e.g., ضارب) is a separate category from ism jins and 'ilm.
4
Eliminate false examples
Words like ضارب on the pattern of fa‘il are sifat, not ism jins, and must be excluded from ism jins examples.
Using ضارب as derived ism jins would combine two distinct categories, which is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اسم جنس کے بارے میں کہا تھا کہ کبھی یہ مشتق ہوں گے اور کبھی غیر مشتق - شاریخ ان کی مثالیں بیان کرتے ہیں۔ کہ علم مشتق ہو جیسے حاتم اور اسم جنس مشتق ہو جیسے مقتل اور علم غیر مشتق ہو جیسے زید اور اسم جنس غیر مشتق ہو جیسے رجل ۔ ولا صیح یہ شرح کی عبارت کا دوسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارع ایک فائدہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ ضارب کو اسم جنس مشتق کی مثال نہیں بنا سکتے اس لیے کہ ضارب صفت کا صیغہ ہے اور صفت کو مصنف نے اسم جنس کا قسیم بنایا ہے اب اگر اس کو اسم جنس کی مثال بنا ئیں تو قسیمین کا اجتماع لازم آئے گا اور یہ باطل ہے۔
And regarding ism jins, it was said that sometimes it is derived and sometimes non-derived. The commentator gives examples: that 'ilm (proper noun) is derived like Hatim, and ism jins is derived like maqtal, and 'ilm non-derived like Zayd, and ism jins non-derived like rajul. And the statement 'wa la sahi' is the second part of the commentary text. Here the commentator mentions a benefit: that 'darib' cannot be taken as an example of derived ism jins because 'darib' is a form of sifat (adjective), and the author made sifat a counterpart of ism jins. So if it were made an example of ism jins, it would entail combining two counterparts, which is invalid.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from the sharh on the categories of ism jins (generic noun) and 'ilm (proper noun). The base text stated that both can be derived (mushtaq) or non-derived (ghayr mushtaq). The commentator provides examples: 'ilm mushtaq: 'Hatim' (derived from the attribute of generosity); ism jins mushtaq: 'maqtal' (place of killing, derived from qatl); 'ilm ghayr mushtaq: 'Zayd' (a proper name not indicating any attribute); ism jins ghayr mushtaq: 'rajul' (man, a generic noun not derived). The commentator then adds a crucial refinement: the word 'darib' (one who strikes) cannot serve as an example of derived ism jins because 'darib' is a form of sifat (adjective). The author classified sifat as a separate category, distinct from ism jins and 'ilm. Using 'darib' as ism jins would erroneously combine two distinct categories (ism jins and sifat) into one example, which is logically invalid. This guard against mixing categories is a typical Hanafi concern for precise classification in usul.

Key Terms
اسم جنس (ism jins): A generic noun that indicates a common meaning, e.g., رجل (man).
مشتق (mushtaq): A word derived from another, sharing its root letters and basic meaning, e.g., حاتم from حتم (determination/generosity).
غیر مشتق (ghayr mushtaq): A word not derived from another, having no etymological connection to a simpler form, e.g., زید.
علم ('ilm): A proper noun that indicates a specific entity, e.g., Hatim or Zayd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can't ضارب (darib) be used as an example of derived ism jins?
A) It is not derived from any root.
B) It is a form of صفت (adjective), which the author made a separate category from اسم جنس.
C) It is a proper noun.
D) It is non-derived.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the classification of nouns into ism jins, 'ilm, and sifat is distinct; derivation alone does not determine category, and mixing categories is invalid.

Two Types of Ishtiqaq: Conceptual and Practical Derivation
Definitions of ishtiqaq: conceptual and practical

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ishtiqaq 'ilmi and ishtiqaq 'amali and explain their roles in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Ishtiqaq 'ilmi traces meaning mentally; ishtiqaq 'amali forms words from roots.

This passage from a classical sharh introduces two definitions of derivation (ishtiqaq) essential for interpreting Arabic legal texts. Understanding the difference between conceptual and practical derivation sharpens your ability to analyze how words carry meaning and how roots generate new terms—a skill fundamental to Hanafi istinbat (legal derivation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
The passage introduces two types: 'ilmi (conceptual) and 'amali (practical). Scan for these terms and note that each describes a different kind of relationship between words.
The terms 'ilmi and 'amali are not metaphors here; they correspond to theoretical vs. applied derivation.
2
Analyze the conceptual definition (ishtiqaq 'ilmi)
Ishtiqaq 'ilmi is a mental operation: the mind traces one word back to another based on correspondence in original meaning (معنی اصلی) and letter arrangement (ترتیب حروف). The derived word (mushtaq) is conceived as returning to its source (mushtaq minhu).
This is a relationship of mental correspondence, not physical transformation.
3
Analyze the practical definition (ishtiqaq 'amali)
Ishtiqaq 'amali involves actually taking one word from another (اخذ) such that the derived word's original letters and their arrangement correspond to the source. The derived word is then made to indicate a meaning suitable (مناسب) to the source meaning.
This is the process of word formation from a root, e.g., ضارب from ضرب.
4
Apply to the example
The passage gives the example of ضرب (darb, striking) and ضارب (darib, striker). In conceptual derivation, the mind relates them via shared meaning and letter order. In practical derivation, the word ضارب is actually formed from the root ضرب with the active participle pattern.
This example illustrates how both definitions operate on the same word pair.
5
State the key distinction
The passage explicitly contrasts them: ishtiqaq 'ilmi considers correspondence in original meaning and composition (معنی اور ترکیب), while ishtiqaq 'amali considers correspondence in original letter arrangement and composition (ترتیب اصلیہ اور ترکیب). The first is about mental relationship, the second about morphological formation.
Memorize this distinction—it appears in many usul discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشتقاق کی تعریفات
والاشتقاق یفسر :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کا تیسرا حصہ ہے یہاں سے شارح اشتقاق کے معنی کو بیان کر رہے ہیں اشتقاق کی دو تعریفیں ہیں علمی اور عملی ۔ تعریف علمی: یہ ہے کہ اشتقاق علمی کہتے ہیں کہ دولفظوں کے درمیان مناسبت کا ہونا معنی اصلی کے اعتبار سے اور حروف کی ترتیب کے اعتبار سے اس طور پر کہ ذہن میں ہی تصور کے درجہ میں ایک لفظ کو دوسرے لفظ کی طرف لوٹا دیں۔ جس کو لوٹایا جائے وہ مشتق ہے اور جس کی طرف لوٹایا جائے گاوہ مشتق منہ ہو گا۔
تعریف عملی: اشتقاق عملی کہتے ہیں کہ ایک لفظ سے دوسرے لفظ کو لیا جائے اس طور پر کہ اس کے حروف اصلی اور ان کی ترتیب میں مناسبت ہو پھر اس لفظ کو دال بنایا جائے ایسے معنی پر کہ جس معنی کی ماخوذ منہ کے معنی کے ساتھ مناسبت ہو۔ مثلاً ضرب کے لفظ سے ضارب کا لفظ لے لیا عقلی درجے میں پھر یہ لحاظ کیا جائے کہ ضارب کے حروف اصلی اور حروف کی ترتیب یہ ضرب کے مناسب ہے ان دونوں میں فرق یہ ہو گا کہ اشتقاق علمی میں تناسب بین اللفظین اصل معنی اور ترکیب میں ملحوظ ہوتا ہے اور اشتقاق عملی میں تناسب بین الملفظین ترتیب اصلیہ اور ترکیب میں ملحوظ ہوتا ہے۔
Definitions of Ishtiqaq: Al-Ishtiqaqu yufassar: This is the third part of the commentary. Here the commentator explains the meaning of Ishtiqaq. There are two definitions: 'ilmi (conceptual) and 'amali (practical). Conceptual definition: Ishtiqaq 'ilmi is said to be the correspondence between two words in terms of original meaning and arrangement of letters, in such a way that in the mind, at the level of conception, one word is traced back to the other. That to which it is traced back is the mushtaq (derived), and that from which it is traced is the mushtaq minhu (source). Practical definition: Ishtiqaq 'amali is said to be that one word is taken from another such that there is correspondence in their original letters and their arrangement, then that word is made indicative of a meaning that is suitable to the meaning of the source. For example, the word 'darib' is taken from 'darb' at the mental level, and then it is considered that the original letters and arrangement of 'darib' correspond to 'darb'. The difference between them is that in ishtiqaq 'ilmi, the correspondence between the two words is considered in terms of original meaning and composition, while in ishtiqaq 'amali, the correspondence between the two words is considered in terms of original arrangement and composition.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage is a definition section from the sharh explaining the term ishtiqaq (derivation). It presents two definitions: 'ilmi (conceptual) and 'amali (practical). The conceptual definition focuses on the mental relationship between two words: one is derived from the other in terms of root meaning and letter order. The derived word (mushtaq) is thought of as returning to its source (mushtaq minhu). For example, 'Hatim' is derived from the attribute of generosity. The practical definition focuses on the actual formation of one word from another: the derived word is made to indicate a meaning related to the source word's meaning, with correspondence in root letters and order. An example is 'darib' (striker) taken from 'darb' (striking). The key distinction: conceptual derivation considers correspondence in meaning and composition, while practical derivation considers correspondence in letter order and composition. This distinction is foundational in Hanafi usul for analyzing word meanings and legal interpretation.

Key Terms
اشتقاق علمی (ishtiqaq 'ilmi): Conceptual derivation: the mental relationship where one word is traced back to another in meaning and letter order.
اشتقاق عملی (ishtiqaq 'amali): Practical derivation: taking one word from another with correspondence in original letters and arrangement, indicating a suitable meaning.
مشتق (mushtaq): The derived word, e.g., ضارب from ضرب.
مشتق منہ (mushtaq minhu): The source word from which derivation occurs, e.g., ضرب from which ضارب is derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Objection to Derivation of Proper Nouns in Hanafi Usul
Objection and resolution on derivation of proper nouns

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi usul scholars distinguish between derived and non-derived nouns specifically for 'ilm (proper nouns) and identify the rational basis for the objection.

Core Idea
Proper nouns designate entities, not attributes; therefore they cannot be derived in the same sense as generic nouns.

In this passage, the commentator challenges the author's classification of 'ilm (proper nouns) as either derived (mushtaq) or non-derived. The argument is based on the function of proper nouns: they primarily indicate a specific entity (dhat mu'ayyanah), not a meaning. This lesson unpacks the rational proof behind this objection and its implications for Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's claim
The author states that both ism jins (generic noun) and 'ilm (proper noun) can be derived or non-derived. Understand the basis: derivation typically implies indication of a meaning (ma'na).
The author's classification groups 'ilm with ism jins in terms of derivability.
2
State the objection
The commentator objects that 'ilm cannot be derived because its primary function is to indicate a specific entity, not a masdari meaning. A derived word normally conveys a meaning, but a proper noun like 'Hatim' points to a person, not necessarily generosity.
The objection is rational: if 'ilm were derived, it would have to indicate a meaning, but it doesn't.
3
Analyze the example
Consider the word 'Hatim'. Does it primarily denote the generous person or the attribute of generosity? The objection argues that even if 'Hatim' originally derived from 'hatm' (generosity), its usage today is to identify a specific individual.
This shows the shift from meaning to entity, making derivation irrelevant in actual usage.
4
Understand the resolution
The objector concedes that 'ilm can indicate a masdari meaning in a generic sense (ma'na jinsi), but that would make it like ism jins. Thus, the property of derivation properly applies only to ism jins, not to 'ilm as proper nouns.
The discussion returns to ism jins, which remains the only category that can be derived or non-derived.
5
Evaluate the usul principle
This objection clarifies a key usul principle: derivation is about conveying a meaning (ma'na masdari), not just linguistic origin. For proper nouns, the legal effect (if any) may come from the entity, not the derived attribute.
This distinction impacts how we analyze legal texts: a proper noun in a ruling is not automatically interpreted through its etymological meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کیا علم مشتق ہو سکتا ہے؟
ولا کنگھی :۔ یہ شرح کی عبارت کو چوتھا حصہ ہے۔ یہاں سے شارع مصنف پر اعتراض کر رہے ہیں اعتراض:۔ مصنف نے کہا کہ اسم جنس اور علم کی دو قسمیں ہیں مشتق اور غیر مشتق یہ کہنا غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ علم جب مشتق ہوگا تو یہ ذات معینہ پر دال ہوگا۔ نہ کہ معنی مصدری پر مثلا حاتم کا لفظ یہ ذات معینہ پر دال ہے نہ کہ معنی مصدری پر پس یہ کہنا کہ علم مشتق ہوتا ہے یہ غلط ہے البتہ علم معنی مصدری پر دال ہوتا ہے معنی جنسی کے اعتبار سے پس کلام لوٹ گئی اسم جنس کی طرف کہ اسم جنس ہی مشتق غیر مشتق ہو گا نہ کہ علم۔
Can 'ilm (proper noun) be derived? 'Wa la kanghi': This is the fourth part of the commentary. Here the commentator objects to the author. Objection: The author said that ism jins and 'ilm have two types: derived and non-derived. This statement is wrong. Because when 'ilm is derived, it would indicate a specific entity, not a masdari meaning. For example, the word 'Hatim' indicates a specific entity, not a masdari meaning. So saying that 'ilm is derived is incorrect. Rather, 'ilm indicates a masdari meaning in terms of generic meaning. So the discussion returns to ism jins: that ism jins alone is derived or non-derived, not 'ilm.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage presents a critical objection from the commentator against the author's classification. The author claimed that both 'ilm (proper noun) and ism jins (generic noun) can be derived (mushtaq) or non-derived (ghayr mushtaq). The commentator argues that this is incorrect for 'ilm. The reasoning: a derived word normally indicates a meaning (e.g., the attribute from which it is derived), but a proper noun's primary function is to designate a specific entity (zat mu'ayyanah), not a meaning. For instance, the proper noun 'Hatim' refers to a particular person, not to the abstract attribute of generosity (the masdar meaning). Therefore, saying that 'ilm is derived is false. However, the objector concedes that 'ilm can indicate a masdari meaning in a generic sense (e.g., 'Hatim' may imply generosity), but that would make it like ism jins. Thus, the objection concludes that only ism jins can truly be described as derived or non-derived, not 'ilm. This is a typical Hanafi refinement: proper nouns are not derived in the same sense as generic nouns because their primary function is designation, not indication of a derived meaning.

Key Terms
علم ('ilm): A proper noun that indicates a specific entity, e.g., Hatim, Zayd.
معنی مصدری (ma'na masdari): The abstract meaning of the verbal noun, e.g., generosity from the root حتم.
ذات معینہ (dhat mu'ayyanah): A specific entity or individual.
مشتق (mushtaq): Derived word that indicates a meaning from which it is taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the objector argue that 'ilm (proper noun) cannot be derived?
A) Because derived words are always from verbs.
B) Because 'ilm indicates a specific entity, not a masdari meaning.
C) Because 'ilm is always a generic noun.
D) Because the author made a mistake in the category.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, proper nouns are not considered derived in the technical sense because their primary function is to designate entities, not convey meanings.

The Usul Rule for Repeated Nouns: Nakirah vs Ma'rifah
Usul rule with Quranic and fiqhi applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule: when a noun is repeated, if it remains nakirah it indicates a different referent; if it becomes ma'rifah it indicates the same referent.

Core Idea
Repeating a nakirah as nakirah = different; repeating as ma'rifah = same.

This passage from the commentary on al-Tawdih wa al-Talwih presents a fundamental usul rule governing the interpretation of repeated nouns in legal texts. Understanding whether the second mention refers to the same or a different entity is crucial for deriving correct rulings from the Quran and for resolving issues like multiple acknowledgments in Hanafi fiqh. The rule hinges on the definiteness of the noun: a repeated nakirah indicates a new individual, while a repeated ma'rifah indicates identity. The author supports this with Quranic evidence and illustrates it with a fiqhi example from iqrar, noting an intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish nakirah and ma'rifah
Recall that nakirah (indefinite) refers to an unspecified individual, while ma'rifah (definite) specifies a particular individual through prior reference (ʿahd).
2
State the core rule
If a noun is first mentioned as nakirah and then repeated as nakirah, the second refers to a different individual. If repeated as ma'rifah, the second refers to the same individual. The same rule applies if the first was ma'rifah.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
In Surah al-Inshirah (94:5-6), 'العسر' (a ma'rifah) is repeated as ma'rifah, proving it is the same difficulty; 'يُسْرًا' (a nakirah) is repeated as nakirah, proving it is a different ease.
This is the basis for Ibn Abbas's statement that one difficulty cannot overcome two eases.
4
Apply to the fiqhi example (iqrar)
If someone acknowledges a specific thousand (ma'rifah) in one session and later in a separate session acknowledges a thousand absolutely (nakirah), according to Imam Abu Hanifa, two thousands are due because the second is a different thousand. If in the same session, only one is due due to unification of the speech act.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that even with separate sessions, only one thousand is due, because repetition in custom is for emphasis. This introduces a nuance based on ʿurf (custom).
This validates the use of ʿurf as a secondary source in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واقع ہو اور اس سے مراد ایک فرد مجہول ہو ۔ کہ اگر اسی نکرہ کو دوبارہ نکرہ کی صورت میں ذکر کیا جائے ۔ تو اس سے مراد پہلے نکرہ کے علاوہ کوئی اور فرد ہوگا ۔ اور اگر اس کو معرفہ کی صورت میں ذکر کیا جائے تو اس سے مراد بعینہ پہلے والا فرد ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ لام تعریف میں اصل عہد ہے اور یہاں اس پر محمول کرنا ممکن ہے کیونکہ پہلے یہ معہود ہے لھذا اس کو عہد پر محمول کیا جائے گا اور اس سے پہلے والا فرد مراد ہوگا۔ اور اگر پہلے ایک لفظ کو معرفہ ذکر کیا جائے تو اس کا حکم بھی دونوں صورتوں میں یہی ہے یعنی اگر دوبارہ اس کو ٹکرہ ذکر کیا جائے تو اس سے پہلے فرد کے علاوہ کوئی اور فرد مراد ہوگا اور اگر اس کو معرفہ ذکر کیا جائے تو اس سے بعینہ پہلے والا فرد مراد ہو گا گویا معلوم ہوا کہ اصل اعتبار دوبارہ لوٹانے کا ہے کہ دوبارہ اگر نکرہ مذکور ہو تو اس سے مراد پہلے والے کا غیر ہو گا اور اگر دوبارہ معرفہ مذکور ہو تو اس سے پہلے والا بعینہ مراد ہو گا پہلے والا چاہے نکرہ ہو یا معرفہ ۔ قال ابن عباس : ۔ یہاں سے مذکورہ بالا صورتوں کی مثالیں دے رہے ہیں اگر کرہ کو دوبارہ نکرہ ذکر کیا جائے یا معرفہ کو دوباره معرفہ کو ذکر کیا جائے تو ان دونوں کی مثال فان مع العسر يسرا ان مع العسر یسرا۔ یہاں العسر معرفہ کو دوبارہ بھی معرفہ کی صورت میں ذکر کیا گیا اس لیے ثانی عصر سے مراد بھی اول عمر ہے یعنی دونوں سے ایک ہی عسر مراد ہے اور یسرا نکرہ کو دوبارہ نکرہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے تو ثانی "سر" سے اول یر" کا غیر مراد ہے یعنی دونوں سے الگ الگ یسر مراد ہیں۔ یہی توجیہ ہے کہ حضرت ابن عباس نے اس آیت کو لیکر فرمایا کہ ایک عسر دو یسر پر غالب نہیں آسکتی۔ والا صبح ان هذا تاکید : ۔ اس آیت میں بعض حضرات نے یہ فرمایا ہے کہ یہاں ثانی آیت اول آیت کی تاکید ہے اور عسر اور یسر دونوں سے ایک ہی عسر یا سیسر مراد ہے ،اتن نے اسی قول کو اصبح قرار دیا ہے۔
اور اگر یکرہ کو دوبارہ معرفہ کی صورت میں ذکر کیا جائے تو اس کی مثال جیسے قرآن پاک میں ہے " كما ارسلنا الی فرعون رسولا یہاں رسول نکرہ ہے اور اس سے مراد حضرت موسیٰ ہیں اور اس کے بعد ہے فصی فرعون الرسول یہاں رسول کو معرفہ بنا کر ذکر کیا گیا ہے اور اس سے مراد بھی حضرت موسیٰ ہیں ۔ تو معلوم ہوا کہ اگر نمرہ کو دوبارہ معرفہ ذکر کیا جائے تو دونوں سے ایک ہی مراد ہوگا۔
اور اگر معرفہ کو ٹکرہ بنا کر لوٹایا جائے تو اس کی مثال اصول فخر الاسلام میں مذکور نہیں ہے البتہ ایک فقہی مسئلہ اس کی مثال بن سکتا ہے۔ کوئی آدمی اقرار کرے اقر بالف مقید ۔۔ یعنی اس ہزار کا اقرار کرے جو چیک میں ہوں یہاں "الف" معرفہ ہے کہ مطلق ہزار کا اقرار نہیں کر رہا بلکہ چیک میں مقید ہزار کا اقرار کر رہا ہے۔ اس کے بعد دوبارہ اگر وہ ہزار کا اقرار کرتا ہے دوسری مجلس میں لیکن اس ہزار کو مطلقا ذکر کرتا ہے۔ تو اس سے مراد پہلے والے ہزار کے علاوہ کوئی اور ہزار مراد ہو گا لھذا امام صاحب کے نزدیک اس پر دو ہزار لازم ہونے چاہیں کیونکہ جب معرفہ کو دوبارہ نکرہ ذکر کیا جاتا ہے تو وہ اول کے مغایر ہوتا تو یہاں دوسرا ہزار اول ہزار کا غیر ہو گا لہذا دو ہزار واجب ہونے چاہئیں لیکن یہ تب ہے جب اقرار دو مجلسوں میں کیا ہو ۔ اگر ایک ہی مجلس میں اقرار ہے تو پھر ایک ہی ہزار لازم ہوگا کیونکہ مجلس کو تمام کلمات متفرقہ کو جمع کرنے میں اثر حاصل ہے لہذا دو مرتبہ کا اقرار کلام واحد شمار ہوگا لیکن صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مجلس ایک نہ بھی ہو پھر بھی ایک ہزار واجب ہوگا ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عرف میں تکرار اقرار پہلے کی تاکید کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر دوبارہ بھی ہزار کو چیک کے ساتھ مقید کر کے ذکر کرتا ہے تو بھی ایک ہزار ہی لازم ہوگا کیونکہ معرفہ کو جب دوبارہ معرفہ ذکر کیا جائے تو وہ عین اول ہوتا ہے تو یہاں دوسرے اقرار کو پہلے کی تاکید سمجھا جائے گا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب۔
It occurs and the intended meaning is an unknown individual. If that same nakirah is mentioned again as a nakirah, then the second refers to a different individual than the first. If it is mentioned as a ma'rifah, then the second refers to exactly the same individual as the first. Because the lam of definition fundamentally indicates prior reference (ʿahd), and it is possible to apply it here because the first is already known. Therefore, it is interpreted as referring to the prior instance, and the same individual is meant. If a word is first mentioned as a ma'rifah, the same ruling applies in both cases: if it is then repeated as a nakirah, it refers to a different individual; if repeated as a ma'rifah, it refers to exactly the same individual. Thus, the principle is that the second mention—if nakirah, it is different; if ma'rifah, it is the same, regardless of whether the first was nakirah or ma'rifah. Ibn Abbas said: From here examples of the above cases are given. If a nakirah is repeated as a nakirah or a ma'rifah as a ma'rifah, the example of both is the verse: 'فَإِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا إِنَّ مَعَ الْعُسْرِ يُسْرًا'. Here 'الْعُسْر' (the difficulty) is ma'rifah and is repeated as ma'rifah, so the second refers to the same difficulty as the first; both refer to one difficulty. 'يُسْرًا' (ease) is nakirah and is repeated as nakirah, so the second 'يُسْر' refers to a different ease from the first; two different eases are meant. This is the explanation of why Ibn Abbas said regarding this verse: One difficulty cannot overcome two eases. As for the view that the second verse is a mere emphasis (tawkid) of the first, some scholars hold that both difficulty and ease are the same; the author deemed this view weak (aṣbaḥ). If a nakirah is repeated as a ma'rifah, an example is the Quranic verse: 'كَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا إِلَىٰ فِرْعَوْنَ رَسُولًا' where 'رَسُولًا' is nakirah meaning Musa, and then 'فَعَصَىٰ فِرْعَوْنُ الرَّسُولَ' where 'الرَّسُولَ' is ma'rifah referring to the same Musa. Thus, when a nakirah is repeated as a ma'rifah, both refer to the same individual. If a ma'rifah is repeated as a nakirah, no example is found in Uṣūl al-Fakhr al-Islām, but a fiqh issue can serve as an example. A person acknowledges: 'I acknowledge a thousand that is in a cheque'—here 'a thousand' is ma'rifah (specific). If later in another session he acknowledges a thousand absolutely, that second thousand refers to a different thousand, so according to Imam Abu Hanifa, two thousand become obligatory, because when a ma'rifah is repeated as a nakirah, it is different from the first. But this is if the acknowledgments are in two separate sessions. If in one session, only one thousand is obligatory because the session unites the separate statements into a single utterance. However, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that even if the sessions are separate, only one thousand is obligatory; their argument is that in custom, repetition of acknowledgment is for emphasis. Similarly, if he repeats the thousand with the cheque restriction (i.e., as ma'rifah), then also only one thousand is obligatory, because when a ma'rifah is repeated as a ma'rifah, it is identical to the first, so the second is considered an emphasis of the first. And Allah knows best the correct.
Source pages p. 619

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul rule about how the repetition of a noun (nakirah or ma'rifah) determines reference. The author establishes the principle: if a nakirah is repeated as a nakirah, it refers to a different individual; if repeated as a ma'rifah, it refers to the same. The same applies if the first was ma'rifah. The explanation is based on the lam of definition indicating prior reference (ʿahd). The author provides Quranic evidence: in Surah al-Inshirah, 'العسر' is repeated as ma'rifah, so it is the same difficulty; 'يسرا' is repeated as nakirah, so it is a different ease. This is why Ibn Abbas said one difficulty cannot overcome two eases. The author dismisses the view that the second verse is mere emphasis. Then another example: from the story of Musa, 'رسولا' (nakirah) is later repeated as 'الرسول' (ma'rifah), referring to the same person. Finally, a fiqhi example from acknowledgments (iqrar): if someone acknowledges a specific thousand (ma'rifah, tied to a cheque) and later in another session acknowledges a thousand absolutely (nakirah), according to Abu Hanifa two thousands are due because the second is different. But if in one session, only one is due because the session unifies. The two companions (Sahibayn) argue that even with separate sessions, only one is due because custom treats repetition as emphasis. Also, if the second acknowledgment also specifies the cheque (ma'rifah), only one is due because it is identical. The passage ends with 'Wallahu aʿlam biṣ-ṣawāb'.

Key Terms
نكرة (nakirah): An indefinite noun that does not specify a particular individual.
معرفة (ma'rifah): A definite noun that specifies a particular individual by a prior reference or definition.
عہد (ʿahd): The concept of prior reference or knowledge of the noun from context.
تاکید (tawkid): Emphasis; a rhetorical device where a statement is repeated to reinforce it.
عرف (ʿurf): Customary practice of a community that can influence legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the iqrar example, if someone acknowledges 'a thousand that is in a cheque' (ma'rifah) and later in the same session acknowledges 'a thousand' (nakirah), what is the ruling according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) Two thousands are due because the second nakirah indicates a different thousand.
B) One thousand is due because the session unifies the speech acts.
C) Two thousands are due because of custom.
D) One thousand is due because the second is emphasis.

Key Takeaway
The repetition of a noun as nakirah indicates a different referent; as ma'rifah indicates the same referent, a key usul rule for interpreting legal texts and resolving disputes like double acknowledgments.
